This is what lets the target path in (2) find the shell's code. `GHJIG_ROOT_OVERRIDE` is a **test-only seam** (precedent: `GHJIG_STATE_DIR_OVERRIDE`, ┬з3.2.2); on the production hook path the **ambient environment is never consulted** (#537) тАФ an inherited `$GHJIG_ROOT` (or a legacy `$GHJIG_SHELL_ROOT`) cannot redirect which shell tree the hooks load, which kills the cross-clone contamination vector where a stale global export made clone B's hooks source clone A's helpers. The #537 demotion is a **clean cut, no deprecation shim**: a lingering legacy export is functionally ignored, and surfaced by a SessionStart banner arm (┬з6.5(c)).

`$GHJIG_ROOT` is therefore an **internal, exported-only** variable, not an external input: the hook entry points and the CLI scripts export it after self-locating (above). The `bin/ghjig` wrapper's `export GHJIG_ROOT` on entry is **convenience output, not load-bearing** тАФ every downstream consumer re-derives the root itself rather than trusting the inherited value:

```bash
#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail
export GHJIG_ROOT="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")/.." && pwd -P)"
exec claude "$@"
```

Deliberately-invoked scripts no longer keep an env-first default: as of #539 the four CLI scripts (`dir_mode_project.sh`, `migrate_v3.sh`, `onboard_target.sh`, `setup_project.sh`) drop `: "${GHJIG_ROOT:=$SCRIPT_ROOT}"` and self-locate unconditionally with the idiom above, then `export GHJIG_ROOT` for their children тАФ the ambient environment is retired as an input **everywhere**, not just on the hook path (`scripts/ghjig_skip.sh` already worked this way). The lib consult sites тАФ four files, `audit_log_path.sh`, `dir_mode_project_resolve.sh` (├Ч2), `inject.sh` (├Ч2, including the former `${GHJIG_ROOT:?}` precondition), `self_register.sh` тАФ adopt the same idiom in place of reading the environment; each self-locates *into* `GHJIG_ROOT` before any bare `$GHJIG_ROOT` use (libs run under `set -u`), which converts the prior convention "every entry must export first" into a **local structural guarantee** at the consumer. This also fixes a live unset-reachable bug where `narrowing_candidates.sh`/`promotion_candidates.sh` reached `audit_log_path.sh` with `GHJIG_ROOT` never exported (the fallback resolved to a filesystem-root-anchored `/.claude/audit/тАж`).

**Agent-side command resolution (#539).** `.claude/commands` flows can rely on none of the above: each command step runs as a separate Bash call with no shared state, agent shells carry no `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR`, and ambient `$GHJIG_ROOT` is retired as an input. Every `$GHJIG_ROOT/тАж` reference in a command file is recast **structurally**, through the binding symlink every registered project carries тАФ by one of two forms, keyed to whether the reference sits **inside a fenced multi-line `bash` block** (which can bind a local `$GR` variable) or is a **bare/inline reference**:

- **Fenced `bash` block** references (a multi-line block that `source`s, `bash`-invokes, or appends to a shell-root path тАФ e.g. `. "$GR/.claude/hooks/тАж"`, `bash "$GR/scripts/тАж"`) bind `$GR` once via the CWD-robust prelude below and reuse it. `git rev-parse --show-toplevel` does not assume the block runs from the project root, and the guard **fails loud** rather than expanding empty (or, inside a nested/vendored repo, silently resolving to the wrong root):

  ```bash
  GR="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel 2>/dev/null)/.claude/ghjig-root"
  [ -e "$GR/.claude" ] || { echo "GHJig: not inside a registered project (cd to the project root, or run scripts/register.sh)"; exit 1; }
  ```

- **Bare/inline** references тАФ both a passive template the agent merely *reads*/copies **and** a single-line `Source тАж`/invocation the agent runs as one Bash call тАФ use the project-root-relative path `.claude/ghjig-root/тАж` directly, with no shell variable (a `$GR/` token here would be a dangling reference, since `$GR` lives only inside a fenced block). These resolve against the **command-execution CWD, which is the project root** тАФ the documented invariant for every command flow (`/onboard`, `/reconcile-spec`, etc. explicitly run from the target repo's cwd). If that invariant is violated the inline source **fails loud** (undefined helper тЖТ command error), never silently loading the wrong tree; the extra CWD-robustness of the fenced-block prelude is reserved for the multi-line blocks that already carry it, so the common inline case stays a single clean token.

Because the dogfood repo commits its own self-symlink (#539, ┬з3.6), both forms behave identically in targets and in the shell repo.

Inside hook scripts, shell-side **code** (helpers, hooks) is accessed via `$GHJIG_ROOT`, while target files and **per-project ephemeral state** are accessed via `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` тАФ keep code (shared) and state (per-project) cleanly separated (┬з3.2.2).

#### 3.2.2 Per-project ephemeral state (`ghjig-state/`)

Ephemeral runtime assets тАФ the **audit log**, the `.claude/state` **caches** (issue-type, issue-filer, status, pr; the park log), and the scope-guard **registry** тАФ resolve per project under `ghjig-state/` (#314 + #316, Directive #311). The audit log and caches resolve via `ghjig_state_dir()`; the registry resolves via `ghjig_registry_file [project_dir]`; both live in `hookrt.sh`.

`ghjig_state_dir()` resolution order (`set -u`-safe, no external calls): `GHJIG_STATE_DIR_OVERRIDE` (test seam) тЖТ `${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}/.claude/ghjig-state` when `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` is set (Claude Code guarantees it for hook commands) тЖТ otherwise **empty**, in which case callers fall back to the legacy shared `$GHJIG_ROOT/.claude/{audit,state}`.

`ghjig_registry_file [project_dir]` serves two execution contexts with a single definition (#316):
- **Argless** (hook context тАФ `cwd_guard.in_scope`/`path_in_scope`): defers to `ghjig_state_dir()` тЖТ `${esd}/registry.txt`, else the legacy shared `${GHJIG_ROOT:-}/.claude/state/registry.txt`.
- **With an explicit project-dir argument** (launcher / CLI context тАФ `bin/ghjig`, `register.sh`/`inject`, `self_register`, `dr_check_registry_guard` тАФ where `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` is unset because the call *precedes* the Claude session): `${1}/.claude/ghjig-state/registry.txt`.

The caller passes the project root it already holds (the `<dir>` argument or `pwd -P`), so registry discovery becomes "does `<dir>` carry its own `ghjig-state/registry.txt`?" тАФ a **self-describing per-project registry**, not a lookup in a shared cross-project index. Under Directive #311's model there is no longer a central authority listing every project.

**Back-compat read-floor.** Every *reader* тАФ `cwd_guard.in_scope`/`path_in_scope` (hook context) and `dr_check_registry_guard`/`bin/ghjig` (CLI context) тАФ when the per-project registry file is **absent**, falls back to *reading* the legacy shared `$GHJIG_ROOT/.claude/state/registry.txt`. This keeps a target registered before #316 (legacy entry only, no `ghjig-state/registry.txt` yet) enforcing on its next session, honoring the #311 "existing setups keep working" constraint. The fallback is **read-only** and triggers **only when the per-project file is absent** тАФ once a target is registered the new way (per-project file present), the shared registry is never consulted for it, so a migrated target gets strict isolation. Writers (`inject`, `self_register`) always write per-project, so write-isolation (success signal 2) is unaffected; and because `in_scope` only ever matches the *current* path against the registry, reading the shared registry as a floor cannot leak another project's scope into the current session.

Consequence: in hook context two projects bound to the same canonical code source have **mutually-invisible** audit/caches **and registries** (writing audit/registry/state in project A leaves project B's `ghjig-state/` unchanged); in plain-Bash context (env unset, no arg) behavior is unchanged (back-compat тАФ the legacy shared paths remain the floor). This realizes the ┬з1.7 / MISSION principle that the **codebase is shared** while **ephemeral state isolates per project**. `ghjig-state/` is added to the target's `.git/info/exclude` (the shell repo excludes its own `ghjig-state/` via its tracked `.gitignore`).

**Fail posture (security).** The registry gates the `out-of-scope` enforcement matcher (┬з6.1). A missing/empty registry yields `in_scope=false` тЖТ hooks pass through transparently (**fail-open**), unchanged from the pre-#316 shared-registry behavior тАФ the move changes only *which path* is read, never the `[ -f "$registry" ] || return 1` posture or the #218 trailing-slash normalization. Because the resolver is `set -u`-safe, an unset `GHJIG_ROOT` (a plain-Bash context that never passed through the wrapper or a hook export, ┬з3.2.1) cannot abort the guard. Dogfood coherence: `self_register` writes through `ghjig_registry_file "$SHELL_ROOT"`, so the shell's registration write-target equals the path `cwd_guard` reads under `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR=$SHELL_ROOT` тАФ a mismatch would silently disable enforcement inside the shell repo (┬з3.6).

### 3.3 Scope guard тАФ cwd-based

All hook scripts prelude:

```bash
# Match physical PWD against registered (physical) paths in the registry.
# The registry is written by register.sh / clone-into.sh; clones inside workspace/ are recorded the same way.
# It resolves per-project via ghjig_registry_file (hookrt.sh, #316): argless = hook
# context (CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR), set -u-safe, legacy shared path as the floor.
REGISTRY=$(ghjig_registry_file)
PWD_REAL=$(cd "$PWD" 2>/dev/null && pwd -P) || exit 0
[ -f "$REGISTRY" ] || exit 0
in_scope=0
while IFS= read -r entry; do
  [ -z "$entry" ] && continue
  case "$PWD_REAL/" in "$entry"/*) in_scope=1; break ;; esac
  [ "$PWD_REAL" = "$entry" ] && { in_scope=1; break; }
done < "$REGISTRY"
[ "$in_scope" = "1" ] || exit 0
```

тЖТ If `ghjig` is invoked from an unregistered directory, hooks pass through transparently. Works regardless of logical vs physical `$PWD` (we use PWD_REAL). External path registration is covered by the same mechanism.

**Fail-open contract.** All three guard exits тАФ an unresolvable `PWD_REAL` (`cd тАж || exit 0`), an absent or empty registry (`[ -f "$REGISTRY" ] || exit 0`), and an out-of-scope cwd (`[ "$in_scope" = 1 ] || exit 0`) тАФ fail **open**: a missing/empty/unreadable registry or an unregistered cwd means enforcement is **off**, never on. This is the guardrail-not-sandbox framing (┬з6.1): the shell narrows what a careful engineer would not do *inside a registered project*, and is silent everywhere else; a registry that cannot be resolved can only under-enforce (pass through), never lock the user out. (The escape hatch, ┬з7, and the helper fail-policy table, ┬з6.1, follow the same fail-open posture.)

The registry (per-project `.claude/ghjig-state/registry.txt`, or the legacy shared `.claude/state/registry.txt` outside hook context) format: one physical path (`pwd -P` output) per line. Comments and blank lines are ignored.

### 3.4 User-global isolation

The shell's installation and operation leave no changes in the user-global environment. The only way to "disable" the shell is to stop invoking `ghjig`. No deactivation procedure or cleanup script is needed.

**Surfaces never touched**:
- `~/.claude` (user-global Claude settings)
- shell rc/login files (`~/.zshrc`, `~/.bashrc`, `~/.bash_profile`, `~/.profile`, `~/.config/zsh/*`, `~/.config/fish/*`, etc.)
- global git config (`~/.gitconfig`, `~/.config/git/*`)
- PATH auto-registration тАФ the user adds `<shell-root>/bin` to PATH or uses absolute path / alias themselves. The shell never injects an export line into rc files.
- LaunchAgents, systemd user units, login items, or any auto-start registration

`bootstrap.sh` boundary:
- Allowed: check dependencies (`gh`, `git`, `python3`, `jq`), run `gh auth status`, create `.claude/audit/` and `.claude/state/` inside the shell repo.
- Forbidden: any modification of the surfaces above, package manager invocations, sudo.

Target repos are the shell's work тАФ they fall outside this isolation rule (the injection in ┬з3.2 is intended behavior).

### 3.5 Entry point

`scripts/setup.sh <local-path | repo-url>` is the single host-side orchestrator: it runs `scripts/bootstrap.sh` (deps check) тЖТ `scripts/register.sh` or `scripts/clone-into.sh` (the register/clone arg contract below) тЖТ `scripts/lib/onboard_checks.sh` (onboard pre-flight) тЖТ an optional dir-mode gate (`scripts/onboard_target.sh`, default N), then prints the next command (or, with `--enter`, execs `claude` directly). Reachable by relative path, so the `ghjig` PATH export is optional тАФ only needed to invoke `ghjig` from an arbitrary directory.

`ghjig` is meant to start at the root of `workspace/<repo>/`. Subdirectories work too (walk-up), but starting at the root avoids edge cases in monorepos where subprojects may carry their own `.claude/`.

**External path support**: a target repo can live outside the shell's `workspace/` (e.g. `~/code/<repo>`). `scripts/register.sh <abs-path>` (1) creates a `workspace/<basename>` symlink, (2) records the target's physical path (`pwd -P`) in the target's per-project `.claude/ghjig-state/registry.txt` via `ghjig_registry_file "$target"` (#316), (3) runs the inject logic of ┬з3.2. The shell's `.gitignore` whitelists `workspace/*` so the shell git tree doesn't pick up target trees even in the external-path case. Direct clones into `workspace/` are also recorded in the registry тАФ the guard is always registry-based.

**Auto-register prompt**: when `ghjig <path>` is called with an unregistered external path, prompt once before entering the session:
```
$ ghjig ~/code/foo
? '/Users/.../code/foo' is not registered. Register as workspace/foo and enter? [Y/n]
```
yes тЖТ run `scripts/register.sh` тЖТ inject logic (┬з3.2) тЖТ start session. no тЖТ exit.

**Monorepo subprojects**: clone-into injects **only at the repo root**. Subprojects with their own `.claude/` are not recursively injected. When the user starts `ghjig` in a subproject, the walk-up finds the root's shell injection. The subproject's `.claude/CLAUDE.md` is merged via Claude Code's default walk-up behavior.

**Discovery surface** (Issue #318, Directive #311): `ghjig list` prints the registered target projects, one resolved physical path per line, then exits 0. Like `--version` it short-circuits **before** the cwd registry guard (┬з3.3), so it works from any cwd including unregistered ones, and has no side effects (no audit, no registry mutation, no cwd change). Enumeration is **advisory, not authoritative** тАФ post-#316 the registry is self-describing per-project (┬з3.2.2), so there is no single global index. `list` unions two sources and dedups by resolved absolute path: (1) the `workspace/*` symlinks (`register.sh` creates one per registration тАФ the most complete set), resolving each and **skipping dangling** links; (2) the legacy shared `$GHJIG_ROOT/.claude/state/registry.txt` (catches pre-#316 + dogfood entries). A target injected without a `workspace/` symlink, or whose symlink was removed, is **invisible to `list` by design** тАФ this incompleteness is inherent to the shared-code/per-project-state model, not a bug.

**Binding-health surface** (Issue #334, Directive #311): when `ghjig <dir>` enters an injected target (`<dir>/.claude/settings.local.json` is a symlink) whose binding `<dir>/.claude/ghjig-root` is **missing or dangling**, it emits one non-blocking stderr warning naming the repair (`scripts/register.sh <dir>`) before `cd`-ing in and `exec claude`. This is the launch-time detector for the broken-binding silent-no-op that the #318-removed SessionStart banner structurally could not surface (the SessionStart hook is itself invoked *through* the binding тАФ ┬з6.5(c)); `ghjig` runs *before* the session and resolves the dir directly, so it is the one place that can warn. Healthy bindings and non-injected dirs stay silent; the check has no side effects beyond the warning.

**Version surface** (Issue #123, Directive #122): `ghjig --version` reads the top-level `VERSION` file (single line, semver 0.x format тАФ `MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH` with `MAJOR=0` per Directive #122 constraint #1) and exits 0 with that string on stdout. If `VERSION` is missing or empty, the handler falls back to `git -C "$SHELL_ROOT" describe --tags --always`; if both fail, a one-line diagnostic is printed to stderr and the process exits 1. The `--version` short-circuit runs immediately after `SHELL_ROOT` resolution and before the cwd-based registry guard (┬з3.3), so it works from any cwd including unregistered paths. The flag has no side effects: no audit log, no registry mutation, no cwd change. Tags follow `v` + semver (e.g., `v0.2.0`) and are pushed manually post-merge тАФ `gh pr merge` does not push tags, and the merge gate does not assert tag-state freshness (explicit Directive #122 non-goal).

### 3.6 Shell self-registration

The shell repo itself must appear in its own registry so that `cwd_guard.in_scope` (┬з3.3) returns true when `ghjig` is invoked from the shell root. Without it, the shell's own hooks short-circuit on `in_scope || exit 0` and the dogfooding promise of ┬з17 is empty тАФ the shell can't enforce its own discipline on itself. Self-registration writes through `ghjig_registry_file "$SHELL_ROOT"` тЖТ `$SHELL_ROOT/.claude/ghjig-state/registry.txt` (#316), which is exactly the path `cwd_guard` reads in a dogfood session (`CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR=$SHELL_ROOT` тЖТ argless `ghjig_registry_file` тЖТ the same file). Write-target == read-target; a divergence would silently fail-open the shell's own scope guard.

`scripts/bootstrap.sh` (and `scripts/register.sh "$SHELL_ROOT"`) ensure `$SHELL_ROOT` is present in the registry (idempotent тАФ repeated runs do not duplicate). Self-registration performs no `workspace/<basename>` symlink and no `inject_into` against the shell, because the shell IS the injection source and a `workspace/` symlink would loop into `workspace/` contained within `$SHELL_ROOT`. It **does**, as of #539, create the per-project **binding symlink** `.claude/ghjig-root` тАФ for the dogfood repo a **committed relative self-symlink** `.claude/ghjig-root -> ..` (from `$SHELL_ROOT/.claude/ghjig-root`, `..` resolves to `$SHELL_ROOT`, so `.claude/ghjig-root/.claude/hooks/<e>.sh` == `$SHELL_ROOT/.claude/hooks/<e>.sh`). This makes the binding symlink **uniform**: *every* registered project тАФ injected targets (symlink created at inject time, ┬з3.2) and the dogfood repo alike тАФ carries `.claude/ghjig-root`, so the structural `.claude/ghjig-root`-relative resolution used by hook settings (┬з3.2.1 consumer (2)) and the agent-side command prelude (┬з3.2.1) works identically in both. The self-symlink is relative (not absolute) so it survives a re-clone of the shell repo to any path; it is committed so a fresh clone carries it without a bootstrap run. The dogfood hook hot path still resolves via `${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}`-direct (┬з3.2.1 consumer (1)) тАФ the self-symlink is what the *deliberately-invoked* and *agent-side* structural paths use, not a change to the hook hot path.

`scripts/register.sh "$SHELL_ROOT"` (or any path that physical-resolves to the shell root) recognizes this case and:
- skips the `workspace/<basename>` symlink (would otherwise create a directory loop);
- skips `inject_into` (the source files are the destinations);
- ensures the registry entry exists;
- ensures the committed `.claude/ghjig-root -> ..` self-symlink exists (idempotent; #539).

For target repos this is unchanged: ┬з3.2 inject + registry entry, both performed by `clone-into.sh` / `register.sh` as before.

### 3.7 Context lifecycle: flush тЖТ clear тЖТ reconstruct

The injection mechanism (┬з3.2) and its runtime surfaces (┬з6.4 per-turn status, ┬з6.5(b) session restore) are the *inbound* half of the MISSION dual тАФ selective injection pulls durable memory into the working context. This section names the full loop they presuppose: **flush тЖТ clear тЖТ reconstruct**, the operational form of MISSION's `active тЖТ archived, not active тЖТ deleted` invariant.

A context **clear** is the bluntest narrowing tool: it discards the entire working context. Done naively it is `active тЖТ delete` тАФ task-scoped state that lived only in the conversation (decisions taken, the current phase, what the next step was) is lost. The MISSION invariant requires it instead be `active тЖТ archived`: the active surface contracts, but the artifact persists in durable memory for later selective re-injection. Three steps make that hold:

1. **Flush** (the gap this section closes) тАФ *before* a clear, distill task-scoped session state into durable memory. The flush is **explicit / skill-invoked** (`/flush`, ┬з5.24), not automatic. What it distills is the small, reconstructable core: the current branch, issue, PR, phase, and the next intended step тАФ the same field set `status_compact` (`helpers/status.sh`) projects. Where it writes (durable-memory targets, in priority order):
   - the **PR body** тАФ curated per the PR-as-living-doc rule (┬з1.4), the richest task-scoped artifact when a PR exists;
   - a record under **`.claude/state/`** тАФ the always-available target (a branch may have no PR yet), carrying the `status_compact` field set;
   - **GitHub artifacts** generally (issue/PR comments) for anything narrative that belongs on the durable record.

   The flush writes *at least one* durable artifact, so that after the clear the state is recoverable rather than gone.

2. **Clear** тАФ the working context is discarded. The shell does **not** and **cannot** intercept Claude Code's native `/clear` (it is outside the shell boundary, ┬з3.4); `/flush` therefore *precedes* a clear and makes it safe, rather than replacing or wrapping it. The clear-trigger contract is **explicit only** in this revision: the operator (or a skill) decides when to clear. **Threshold-based / automatic triggering is deferred** (┬з0.4) тАФ both because the shell cannot hook the native clear, and because a wrong automatic clear has a high cost-asymmetry (┬з6.0): a clear is irreversible within the session.

3. **Reconstruct** тАФ on the next session, **SessionStart session restore (┬з6.5(b))** re-injects the durable memory: the current branch's full PR body, the referenced issue body, the MISSION summary, and one `/status` snapshot (CLAUDE.md is natively loaded whole, not re-injected here); ┬з6.4 then keeps the per-turn surface narrow. This is the *already-built* inbound half тАФ this section adds no new reconstruct path, deliberately, to avoid a parallel injection surface that could drift from ┬з6.5(b).

**Known gap (noted, not closed here):** ┬з6.5(b) restore re-injects the PR body, the issue body, and a `/status` snapshot тАФ it does **not** currently read the `.claude/state/` flush record written in step 1. So when a PR exists, reconstruct is complete; on a branch with no PR yet, the `.claude/state/` record is written (the archive exists) but is not auto-re-injected at SessionStart. Closing that gap тАФ teaching ┬з6.5(b) restore to read the flush record тАФ is a follow-up, kept out of this revision to hold the change to one section + one affordance.

**Discard-boundary = Execution** (Directive #477). The flush тЖТ clear тЖТ reconstruct loop is the *session-level* application of the MISSION `active тЖТ archived` invariant; the **discard boundary at the Execution unit** (┬з1.2) is the *within-task* application. The within-Execution authoring churn (the Code phase's file reads, abandoned approaches, lint/smoke iterations) is `active тЖТ delete`-able once the Code commit lands тАФ it was never durable тАФ while **directive-level memory is preserved** (`active тЖТ archived`, the cross-Execution context a Directive carries). The `implementer` subagent (┬з4.12) + `/implement` (┬з5.28) enforce the boundary structurally: Phase C runs in the subagent's ephemeral context and only the structured result (commit + plan-deviations + discoveries) crosses back, so the churn is discarded at the Execution edge rather than flushed. This is the **default Code-phase route** (Directive #477 signal-4: the formal A/B measurement was descoped, the narrowing hypothesis adopted as operating policy on circumstantial evidence), with a **documented opt-out** for trivial / glue edits that stay in the main loop and **fail-open reversibility** as the safety valve; preserving directive-level memory across Executions is the EI-2 coding-memory loop (signal 3, closed).

---

## 4. Subagent specifications

Each agent is defined in `.claude/agents/<name>.md` as YAML frontmatter + body.

### 4.1 planner

**When**: before any code edit. Required for 3+ file changes, migrations, schema changes, API changes, or external contract changes.

**Input**: user request, linked issue body, MISSION.md, target CLAUDE.md.

**When MISSION is absent**: planner proceeds with `issue body + README + CLAUDE.md` alone. The "How this serves the mission" section is labeled `(MISSION.md absent тАФ review /onboard stub suggestion)`. Don't synthesize a MISSION via inference.

**Output** (markdown that drops straight into the PR body):

```
## How this serves the mission
<Which MISSION.md item this contributes to>

## Plan
<Why this approach, trade-offs, decision rationale>

## Target base
<branch name; default `main`. For non-`main`, name the topic-branch / feature-branch the PR will merge into. See SPEC ┬з10.5.>

## Alternatives considered
- <Alternative 1>: <one-line why-not>
- <Alternative 2>: <one-line why-not>
(If the choice is forced тАФ single viable approach тАФ say so explicitly with a one-line justification rather than fabricating alternatives.)

## Key context
<related file:line>

## Checklist
- [ ] **Doc**: <doc update item 1>
- [ ] **Doc**: <doc update item 2>
- [ ] **Test**: <failing test item>
- [ ] **Code**: <implementation item>
- [ ] **Code**: <implementation item>

## Out of scope
<What this PR will NOT do>

## Risks
<Compatibility, performance, data, security>

## Open questions
<To be decided before proceeding>
```

Checklist order: **Doc first, Test next, Code last**. Granularity: one item тЙИ one commit тЙИ 30 min to 2 hours.

**Alternatives section is mandatory** тАФ even when the choice feels obvious. A "no alternatives тАФ forced choice" entry with a one-line justification is acceptable; an empty section is not. The section exists so reviewers see what was rejected and why, and so future-you can revisit the trade-off without re-running the analysis.

### 4.2 explorer

**When**: locating code, symbol lookups, "where is X defined", "who calls Y" тАФ read-only wide search. Protects the main context.

**Constraints**: no code edits. No dumping large files. Always summarize.

**Output**:
- Definition location (`path:line`)
- Up to 5 main references (`path:line` + one-line context)
- Related modules
- If nothing found: say "not found" and suggest next searches.

### 4.3 doc-writer

**When**: Phase A. Any change that alters external surface.

**Responsibilities**:
- Identify affected SSOT docs (MISSION, README, CLAUDE.md, ARCHITECTURE, ADR, API doc).
- Patch each doc preserving its existing format and tone.
- For absent docs, propose a minimal stub only after user confirmation.
- When an irreversible decision is detected, recommend writing an ADR (`docs/ADRs/NNNN-title.md`).

**Forbidden**: inventing target SSOT content (humans must review and sign off). Only stub proposals when absent.

### 4.4 test-writer

**When**: Phase B, right after doc.

**Responsibilities**:
- Take Phase A docs / spec as input; write a failing test.
- Reuse existing test patterns, tools, fixtures.
- Cover intended behavior + at least one boundary / exception / error path.
- Run it and confirm it **fails** (intentionally). If it passes, either Phase A is wrong or the test is too weak.

**Principles**:
- Suspect over-mocking.
- One test = one assertion.
- If tooling is absent (e.g. pytest not installed), report and stop. Don't guess.

### 4.5 code-reviewer

**When**: before commit / PR. Auto-invoked by `/review`, `/ship`.

**Premise**: assume no knowledge of the main assistant's discussion or reasoning. Input is:
- The full PR diff. Prefer `gh pr diff <num>` (or `--web` equivalent) over a literal `git diff main...HEAD` тАФ the PR's `baseRefName` may be non-`main` for topic-branch / experimental work (┬з10.5), and `gh pr diff` honors that automatically. The principle is "review what the PR actually changes against its declared base," not "everything since main."
- Read-only adjacent context for changed files (for call-graph tracing, as needed) тАФ read via `git show <HEAD_SHA>:<path>` at the resolved PR-head SHA (below), **not** from the ambient working tree
- Target `MISSION.md`, referenced issue body (for MISSION fit + acceptance criteria evaluation)
- Full PR body (for declared plan + checklist verification)

Nothing outside this input.

**Artifact resolution (canonical; #544).** A worktree-isolated reviewer (┬з1.5) is checked out at the **harness-chosen base** (`origin/main`), **not** the PR head тАФ so an ambient `git diff`/full-file read reviews the *wrong artifact* and can still emit APPROVE (observed live in PR #543: three ship reviewers ran at the base SHA while the PR head had advanced; one approved a diff it never saw). The reviewer therefore **resolves its artifact from the pushed PR head by construction**, never from the ambient worktree:
- **Head SHA**: `gh pr view <n> --json headRefOid --jq .headRefOid`.
- **Diff**: `gh pr diff <n>` (equivalently `git fetch origin refs/pull/<n>/head && git diff <base>...<HEAD_SHA>`).
- **Changed-file context**: `git show <HEAD_SHA>:<path>` тАФ read-only git, **no checkout**. This closes the residual hole where an adjacent full-file context read would otherwise hit the stale base worktree even when the diff itself was fetched correctly.
- **`reviewed-head:` line**: the verdict's **first line** is `reviewed-head: <sha>`, the SHA the reviewer **independently derived** from the artifact it actually resolved (not one handed to it тАФ see ┬з5.7 caller-side blind compare). If the reviewer cannot confirm its resolved copy equals the current PR head (a `gh`/`fetch`/resolve failure of its own), it **says so explicitly and its verdict is invalid** тАФ an unconfirmed head is never an approve.

**Known residual (deferred, #544 follow-up тАФ not built here).** The `reviewed-head:` line binds the *artifact the reviewer resolved*, not the *cognitive act of review* тАФ a reviewer could resolve the head correctly yet reason over stale context. A **content-challenge** (the reviewer quotes a specific diff line the caller privately knows, binding the review act to the artifact) is the intended tightening; it is deferred to a follow-up issue, tracked here as a known limitation.

**Check**:
- Consistency (coherent changes, missing adjacent callers)
- Tests (alignment with Phase B, regression risk)
- Error handling (at boundaries only, no defensive code creep)
- Security surface
- Obvious performance traps
- Readability, naming тАФ and, for a language with a rubric at `.claude/rubrics/<lang>.md`, the **readability / language-idiom axis** (┬з4.5.1)
- Scope (extraneous changes?)
- **Doc sync (Phase A reflected?)**
- **MISSION fit (contributing to or violating which item?)**
- **Issue acceptance criteria met?**
- **Enforcement-style (┬з6.0)** тАФ *only for diffs that add/change a hook, gate, matcher, or standing guidance*: a new block must name its positive alternative and the negative/positive face must match the cost-asymmetry (┬з6.0 P1 + P4); a bare block or gateless guidance is a one-sided regression. (n/a for diffs touching no enforcement surface.)

**Output**: ship / ship after fix / block. Each finding cites `path:line`.

**Materializing the verdict as a GitHub review**: `/file-review <pr>` (┬з5.29) is the producer that runs this reviewer and posts its verdict as a first-class, `commit_id`-pinned GitHub review.

#### 4.5.1 Readability / language-idiom review axis (#546)

A **first-class review concern distinct from correctness.** Correctness ("does it work") is covered by `shellcheck` (the fail-closed CI gate, ┬з11), `code-reviewer`'s correctness/scope/security checks, and the smoke suite. This axis covers the *other* senior-engineering quality dimension the MISSION quality bar names тАФ **is the code written the way its language wants to be written** (readable, well-factored, reaping the language's intended benefits/philosophy: idiomatic bash here; OOP/SOLID in C#/Java, Pythonic contracts in Python, idiomatic ownership in Rust/Go for future rubrics). Without it the shell could green-light correct-but-unidiomatic code тАФ the gap #546 named.

**Mechanism тАФ a per-language rubric conditionally read into `code-reviewer`.** The rubric for each language lives in **one home**, `.claude/rubrics/<lang>.md` (the contract-in-a-file pattern of the reviewer-prompt SSOTs, ┬з9 тАФ SPEC references it, never restates it). `code-reviewer` detects the languages present in the diff and, for each with a rubric file, reads it and applies its criteria as **advisory idiom-notes**. This satisfies the narrowing mechanism (MISSION "The mechanism") on both limbs: the read is **conditioned on the languages actually in the diff** (a non-bash diff never loads the bash rubric) and is spent inside the **reviewer's own isolated ephemeral context** (a worktree-isolated subagent returns only its distilled verdict), so neither the acting context nor a non-matching review grows. **Language-extensibility** falls out for free тАФ adding `python.md`/`rust.md` later is a new *file*, zero reviewer-prompt change; bash is the first file, not a hardcode of the mechanism.

**Advisory, never a block (┬з6.0 P1/P3/P4).** An idiom finding is emitted under a distinct advisory section of the verdict and **never escalates to `block`** тАФ `code-reviewer`'s `block` stays reserved for correctness / scope / security / doc-sync / AC / enforcement-style. By P1 the cost of a wrong "unidiomatic" nudge is ignorable, so the axis takes the **positive/advisory face**; the whole device *is* the positive face (a reviewer producing an advisory artifact), with no negative counterpart to pair (P4 satisfied by construction). It is deliberately **born advisory** (P3 observe-before-harden): whether any subset ever hardens toward a gate is a future ┬з6.0 decision informed by operating experience, not taken now.

**Deterministic-vs-LLM boundary (AC1), made explicit.** Drawn inside each rubric and stated here: the **deterministic** subset тАФ *decidable by an existing tool or a fixed-string grep* (bash: quoting/array conventions delegated to the already-pinned `shellcheck`, `safe_source`-not-raw-`source` discipline, the `git add -A/-u` prohibition) тАФ is surfaced by the **born-advisory, non-gating** checker `scripts/lint_bash_idioms.sh` (a thin wrapper that **reuses** `scripts/lint.sh`'s pinned-shellcheck resolver plus fixed-string project-policy greps тАФ not a second lint engine, #276/#490 reuse discipline; **never** wired into the fail-closed CI lint gate). The **LLM-judgment** subset тАФ threshold/design smells no linter should decide (function size/altitude, DRY-across-helpers, and the named *detection-by-attribute-combination-where-an-explicit-discriminator-exists* smell) тАФ lives only in the rubric as prose plus a worked-example pair, applied by the reviewer LLM. Because the smoke harness is deterministic and cannot run the reviewer LLM, the LLM-judgment half is demonstrated by that structurally-explicit worked-example pair (anti-vacuity/anti-drift smoke-locked), not by executing the reviewer; only the deterministic subset is truly executed in smoke.

### 4.6 security-reviewer

**When**: PRs touching auth / authz / sessions / external input / new deps / crypto / hashing / randomness / new IO boundaries.

**Input / artifact resolution**: same artifact-resolution contract as ┬з4.5 тАФ resolve the diff and changed-file context from the **pushed PR head** (`gh pr view <n> --json headRefOid`, `gh pr diff <n>`, `git show <HEAD_SHA>:<path>`), never the ambient (possibly base-pinned) worktree, and emit `reviewed-head: <sha>` as the verdict's first line. An unconfirmed head тЖТ invalid verdict. This is the reviewer whose base-pinned APPROVE in the high-asymmetry tier (┬з4.11) is highest-cost, so the pin is load-bearing here.

**Check areas**: authentication / authorization, injection (SQL / shell / HTML / path), sensitive data exposure, weak crypto, CSRF / CORS / headers, dependency risk.

**Output**: High / Medium / Low / Info. Each finding: risk + exploit scenario + remediation.

### 4.7 issue-reviewer

**When**: invoked by `/file-issue` before `gh issue create`. Validates the rationale triad of SPEC ┬з5.2 тАФ every issue passes through this gate.

**Input**:
- Proposed issue body (title + body + label).
- Target `MISSION.md` (if absent, label as `(MISSION.md absent тАФ review /onboard stub suggestion)`).
- Open-issues list (`gh issue list --state open`).

**Check**:
- **MISSION fit**: does the body cite a specific MISSION item? "It's general improvement" or "tidy" answers fail.
- **Why now**: does the body explain what changes if this waits? Vague "would be nice" fails.
- **Existing-coverage**: scan open-issues / open-PRs; does another issue cover this, or would a comment on an open PR suffice? If yes тЖТ suggest the cheaper path.
- **Acceptance criteria**: explicit, testable, тЙе1 item.
- **Enforcement-style fit (┬з6.0)** тАФ *only when the proposed issue adds/changes a hook, gate, matcher, or standing guidance* (else n/a): the negative/positive face must match the cost of being wrong (┬з6.0 P1) and a proposed block must name its alternative / proposed guidance must have a gate behind it (┬з6.0 P4); a mismatch or one-sided proposal тЖТ `refine`.
- **Phase-slice (Check 6 тАФ advisory, never blocks)**: flags a proposed Issue that is a single **phase-slice** (doc-only / test-only / code-only) of a larger multi-phase change whose sibling phases would be filed as *separate* issues тАФ the anti-pattern the ┬з1.2 issue-level corollary names (one change = one Execution Issue; the phases are commits, not issues). This check is **advisory only**: it surfaces as a report NOTE and **never** escalates to `block` on this basis тАФ `block` stays reserved for the rationale-triad checks 1тАУ5, and the `ship`/`refine`/`block` verdict grammar (below) is unchanged. **Observable discriminator** тАФ issue-reviewer sees only the body + the open-issues list, never the codebase build-state, so the lead signal is either (a) the **body itself deferring a sibling phase of the same change** (e.g. "Out of scope: tests / code filed separately") or (b) the **open-issues list carrying a sibling phase-slice of the same change** (reuse the Check-3 open-issues fetch); a not-yet-built state is confirmatory only, never the lead. Legitimately single-surface changes are **not** flagged тАФ a pure-docs / README / typo change, a standalone ADR or SPEC-clarification where the doc *is* the terminal artifact, a test-only hardening PR, or a refactor тАФ nor is a dir-mode Directive that legitimately spawns multiple Execution Issues (separate changes, not phases of one). Full worked-example set lives in `.claude/agents/issue-reviewer.md` (┬з9 тАФ exemplars not duplicated here).

**Output**: one of three verdicts on stdout's last line, each with a one-line reason:
- `ship` тАФ file as-is.
- `refine: <one-line why>` тАФ return for body revision before filing.
- `block: <one-line why>` тАФ don't file at all (existing-coverage hit, scope problem, or non-MISSION work).

Inside `attended` mode the verdict surfaces to the user; inside `unattended` mode it gates the next step directly. Hook into `attended` is non-skippable тАФ Auto mode does not suppress this gate (SPEC ┬з5.2).

### 4.8 plan-reviewer (adversarial-pairing plan review, #530)

**When**: invoked by `/work-on` after the planner and the two challengers (below), to **judge the contest** and gate the plan-approval step.

**The omission bias this fixes.** Historically the `planner` authored both the Plan *and* its own `## Alternatives considered`, and `plan-reviewer` only *graded that self-curated list*. The interested party controlled the choice set, so the structural failure mode was **omission** тАФ a genuinely superior approach the planner never surfaced could not enter the contest, and its absence was invisible from inside the loop (a "not strawmen" check catches crude weakness but not a plausible list that silently excludes the real winner). This matters most under `unattended` mode, where a clean `plan-reviewer` verdict *substitutes for human plan approval* (┬з1.5, ┬з5.3): a reviewer grading a rigged set is a weak substitute for the human it replaces, who would have brought their own rival approach.

**Adversarial pairing (the default whenever the planner is invoked).** The planner produces **one base Plan A** and **no longer authors alternatives**. `/work-on` then runs an **upstream axis selector** and dispatches **two independent, mutually-blind `plan-challenger` agents** (┬з4.8.1) on **two distinct axes**, **parallel + worktree-isolated**. Each returns exactly one of three outcomes on its axis: a plan that **dominates A**, a **genuine non-dominating alternative** (a real trade-off), or an **explicit reasoned concession** (names the axis it tried + why A held). `plan-reviewer` then **judges the three candidates {A, B1, B2}**.

**Axis selection.** The selector (homed **upstream in `/work-on`**, between the planner and the challenger dispatch тАФ *not* inside a challenger or the reviewer, since blind challengers cannot self-coordinate distinctness and an interested agent choosing its own axis re-introduces bias) designates the **2 highest-leverage _focus_ axes for this specific change** (a **weight, not a filter** тАФ the remaining menu axes are not discarded; the domination bar keeps them in view, ┬з4.8.1) from a fixed menu: **{correctness, simplicity/maintainability, performance, security, cost/effort, robustness/risk, extensibility, UX}**, and assigns one to each challenger as its **lead**. **No hardcoded axis pair** тАФ a fixed pair (e.g. simplicity+robustness) would itself be an omission mechanism, systematically excluding performance/security from ever being challenged, relocating the very bias this fixes rather than removing it. The selector emits a **drop-axis attestation** (`audit_log info plan-axis`, observe-only, P3 observe-before-harden тАФ Directive #570) naming the focus/deferred split, and `plan-reviewer` gains an **axis-selection sanity check** (an after-the-fact judge backstop confirming the focus axes fit the change, keeping the selector itself non-adversarial); full contract in the `/work-on` step-5.5 prose + `plan-reviewer.md` (┬з9).

**Why this is a DEFAULT, not gated (the ┬з4.11 relationship тАФ both legs required, do not state only one):**
1. **Generation diversity тЙа vote redundancy.** ┬з4.11's "N-way independent voting is blast-radius-gated, *never* a default" governs **vote redundancy** тАФ N copies of *one* reviewer casting approve-verdicts that tally to a majority gate, where correlated votes de-risk nothing. #530 is **generation diversity** тАФ *distinct authors* producing *distinct artifacts* for *one* judge, with no vote tally. ┬з4.11's correlated-vote caution does not reach it.
2. **Isolation protects the acting context, not the token budget.** MISSION narrowing protects the **acting/working context** (what the parent loop holds), not total token spend. `plan-challenger`s are **worktree-isolated subagents**: they spend tokens in *their own* contexts and return only **distilled verdicts** to the parent тАФ so two challengers do **not** grow the acting context. The honest residual is higher *total tokens* + ~1 parallel planner-latency; that is a favorable trade for the **plan artifact, whose blast radius governs all downstream code** тАФ the highest-leverage artifact in the flow.

**Guards (both challenger outcomes can degenerate; the judge rejects both):**
- **Lazy concession** тАФ a concession is valid **only if** it names the axis tried + why A held; an empty "A is fine" is rejected (rubber-stamp regression).
- **Fake-diff** тАФ a "different-but-worse" plan that does not actually dominate resolves to **A stands** (the inverse strawman).
- **Minimalism-by-deferral** (Directive #567; the mirror of `fake-diff`) тАФ an axis win (simplicity / cost / effort) bought by **deferring, weakening, or measurement-gating a declared mandatory invariant** is *not* a domination: it resolves to **A-stands / disqualification**, never a soft trade-off. "No worse elsewhere in a way that matters" **includes** a dropped mandatory invariant, and such a drop is **never** dismissable as "technical taste alone."
- **Dismissal evidence-burden** (Directive #570 / #571; the **judge-side** mirror of `fake-diff` / `minimalism-by-deferral`) тАФ the guards above police the *challengers*; this one polices the **judge's own** `A-stands` verdict. An `A-stands` against a *domination claim* is valid only when the judge **refutes** the challenger's specific weakness with evidence (scaled to its *claimed* magnitude), never merely **outweighs** it with A-advocacy; it closes the reclassification-to-dodge and unevidenced-down-rate escape hatches and fires only on a domination claim (never a concession / `fake-diff`), so benign incumbent-presumption holds. Full contract in the reviewer-prompt SSOT `.claude/agents/plan-reviewer.md` (┬з9).

**Mandatory-invariants manifest + before-contest gate (Directive #567).** `/work-on` dispatch passes a **`Mandatory invariants`** field to the planner, both `plan-challenger`s (┬з4.8.1), and `plan-reviewer`, **derived at dispatch from existing SSOT** (issue AC / MISSION / ADRs / the affected component's contract) тАФ never invented by a reviewer (┬з6.0). `plan-reviewer` runs an **invariant-preservation gate *before* the axis contest**: a candidate that defers/weakens/measurement-gates a declared mandatory invariant is **disqualified regardless of axis score** (the ┬з6.0 hard-negative-gate rationale). Empty manifest тЖТ the reviewer **attests the invariant set it checked against** (including "none declared"), *not* a hard block (┬з6.0). A **symmetric steelman** step (Directive #570/#573; folded into `plan-reviewer`, not a new "defender" role) argues the strongest case for **every** candidate {A, B1, B2} тАФ A included, so A's advocacy is retained тАФ with no candidate privileged by generation order, split into an **invariant limb** (Check 0) and an **axis limb** (the lead of Check 1); it supersedes the former A-only steelman-the-incumbent, correcting the advocacy asymmetry symmetrically rather than only for A. The `plan-challenger` mandate's **domination logic** (┬з4.8.1) is **unchanged** by #567 тАФ the fix is at the judge + dispatch, not the adversary (its *framing* was later refined to weight-not-filter / lead-with by Directive #570/#575, still without touching the domination bar) тАФ and the `planner` (┬з4.1) is unaffected beyond receiving the field. The full gate + guard + steelman contract is the reviewer-prompt SSOT `.claude/agents/plan-reviewer.md`; this section references it (┬з9), not restates it.

**Shared-blindspot check** тАФ the reviewer reads the code/issue directly. Scoped to same-model prior correlation (A/B1/B2 on one model can share a blindspot тАФ adversarial structure breaks *framing* bias, not *shared-prior* blindness) **and** the N>2 residual (a change with 3+ live axes that 2 challengers cannot cover). It is **not** a substitute for a systematically-omitted axis тАФ the upstream selector, not this backstop, is what prevents systematic omission.

**Input**: the base Plan A (markdown); the two challenger outputs {B1, B2} with their assigned axes; the issue body; target `MISSION.md`; the **`Mandatory invariants`** field (┬з6.0, Directive #567 тАФ the dispatch-derived SSOT manifest).

**Check**:
- **Invariant-preservation gate (before the contest, ┬з6.0)**: disqualify any candidate that defers/weakens/measurement-gates a declared mandatory invariant, regardless of axis score; an empty manifest тЖТ attest the set checked ("none declared"), not a block. This gate is **sequenced ahead of** the axis-contest judgment below (contract SSOT: `.claude/agents/plan-reviewer.md`).
- **Judge the contest {A, B1, B2}**: pick the winner; or declare **A forced / high-confidence** when both challengers fail to beat it (both concede or fake-diff); or **surface a genuine trade-off** (attended: to the user; unattended: resolve per mode) when no candidate dominates. Verify challenger **genuineness** (reject lazy-concession; fake-diff тЖТ A-stands).
- **Scope hygiene**: items in `Checklist` map to `Acceptance criteria`; anything orphaned belongs in `Out of scope` or a follow-up issue.
- **Phase-order sanity**: Doc тЖТ Test тЖТ Code per ┬з1.2; relaxation reasons noted if applicable.
- **Target base fit**: the `Target base` field (┬з4.1) names a branch; a `main`-default plan proposing experimental-base work (or vice versa) fails.
- **Enforcement-style fit (┬з6.0)** тАФ *only when the plan introduces/changes a hook, gate, matcher, or standing guidance* (else n/a): face must match the cost of being wrong (P1), a planned block names its alternative / guidance has a gate (P4).

**Output**: the same three verdicts as `issue-reviewer` тАФ **the `^VERDICT: (ship|refine|block)` grammar is unchanged** (the 3-way adjudication collapses to these three tokens: a winning challenger or a surfaced trade-off тЖТ `refine` carrying the winner/trade-off forward; A-stands тЖТ `ship`). `refine` causes `/work-on` to re-run the contest with the feedback; `block` stops with a comment on the issue.

**Non-adopted / subsumed (recorded so a future edit cannot silently reintroduce them):**
- **naive parallel-independence** (N identical-prompt planners) тАФ **non-adopted**: identical prompts on one model converge (correlated draws), buying redundancy without diversity. The diversity mechanism is *distinct-axis mutual-blindness*, not repetition.
- **reviewer-steelman-only** (the judge authors its own single rival) тАФ **subsumed**: two *independent* challengers steelman better than a judge authoring the rival it then adjudicates (which re-introduces a milder interested-party bias). The reviewer's code-read survives only as the shared-blindspot *backstop*, not as the primary rival source.
- **N>2 challengers / more axes** тАФ a **deferred future ┬з4.11-style high-asymmetry escalation** (for a change with 3+ live axes); no gate is built now, and the shared-blindspot check backstops the N>2 residual in the interim.

#### 4.8.1 plan-challenger

**When**: dispatched by `/work-on` (├Ч2, parallel + worktree-isolated) after the planner and axis selection, before `plan-reviewer`.

**Mandate**: **beat Plan A**, **leading with** the single **focus axis passed by the caller** while holding all axes in view (a weight, not a filter тАФ Directive #570/#575; the domination bar's "no worse elsewhere" keeps every axis live, the focus axis is only the lead). Mutually blind (no visibility into the other challenger). Return one of: **dominates-A** (a superior plan on the axis) / **genuine non-dominating alternative** (a real trade-off) / **reasoned concession** (names the axis tried + why A held тАФ a bare "A is fine" is rejected downstream). Never manufacture a different-but-worse plan to avoid conceding (the fake-diff the judge resolves to A-stands). The challenger also receives the **`Mandatory invariants`** field (┬з4.8, Directive #567) тАФ an axis win bought by dropping a listed invariant is not a domination (the `minimalism-by-deferral` guard the judge applies); the mandate is otherwise **unchanged** by #567.

**Working-tree discipline**: read-only-by-intent, invoked with worktree-isolation and constrained to read-only git тАФ same posture as the other read-only reviewers (┬з1.5, #285). Tools: `Read, Grep, Glob, Bash`.

**Session-restart caveat (┬з4.9.3)**: `plan-challenger` is a new `subagent_type`; until the next session restart `/work-on` routes it through `general-purpose`. Its prompt is **self-describing** (it instructs `general-purpose` to behave as `plan-challenger`) so the fallback is functionally complete; restart is canonical.

### 4.9 Director subagents

The dir-mode workflow (┬з1.7) uses one reviewer subagent (`activation-reviewer`, ┬з4.9.1). A second (`roadmap-reviewer`, ┬з4.9.2) is documented for future activation.

#### 4.9.1 activation-reviewer

**When**: invoked by `/file-directive` (proposed Directive body, ┬з5.10), `/activate` (re-check on the possibly-edited body before ProposedтЖТActive, and on unblock, ┬з5.12), `/revise-directive` (the new body before replacement, ┬з5.16), and `/complete-directive` (completion claim + linked-Execution-Issue evidence, ┬з5.13); and тАФ via the Initiative rulebook тАФ by `/consume-initiative` (contract-evaluability at Initiative intake, extraction-faithfulness on the proposed Directive set, ┬з5.21). Mirrors the structure of `issue-reviewer` (┬з4.7) and `plan-reviewer` (┬з4.8) тАФ review only, never authors content.

**Type-label dispatch**: `activation-reviewer` is **type-neutral** тАФ it resolves the reviewed Issue's type label and applies the matching rulebook. The `directive` label present тЖТ the Directive checks below. The `initiative` label present (#254, M2) тЖТ the **Initiative rulebook** (contract-evaluability тАФ the termination condition must be evaluable without code knowledge; and extraction-faithfulness тАФ extracted Directives decompose the termination condition without smuggling strategy); the reviewer never activates or mutates an Initiative (the shell consumes them), it judges the Initiative/extraction as input for the M3 consume flow. Absent (an Execution Issue, `task`/`bug`) тЖТ an Execution rulebook (schema completeness, acceptance-criteria verifiability, scope clarity, MISSION fit, duplicate coverage; **parent-fit is gated by label** тАФ applied only to the `execution` type, while `task`/`bug` are standalone per the ┬з1.7 `execution`/`task`/`bug` type-label definitions and skip the parent checks and the Parent-mismatch matrix). For a Directive, the **alignment check branches on parent kind** (#254): a `## MISSION fit` MISSION-section parent is judged against MISSION; a line-1 `Parent Initiative: #N` parent is judged against that Initiative's termination condition (the parent-XOR guarantees exactly one). The **reviewer verdict vocabulary** (#172, canonical here): `activation-reviewer` тЖТ `pass` / `revise` / `reject`, while `issue-reviewer` (┬з4.7) and `plan-reviewer` (┬з4.8) retain `ship` / `refine` / `block` 1:1 (out of #172's scope) тАФ uniform across both `activation-reviewer` rulebooks; only the *checks* differ by type. The structured refile fields and the type-mismatch / parent-mismatch matrices apply on `reject`.

**Input**:

- **For proposal review:** the proposed Directive body (objective, success signals, non-goals, constraints, and the parent тАФ a `## MISSION fit` field **or** a line-1 `Parent Initiative: #N` marker, ┬з1.7), plus the list of currently `Status=Active` Directives (via `gh issue list --label directive --label '-status:proposed' --state open` тАФ Issues are the SSOT; the Project is a lagging derived view and is NOT consulted, ┬з1.7/┬з5.11).
- **For completion review:** the Directive's body (success signals as written at activation), the list of linked Execution Issues (Issues with `Parent` = this Directive), and their close states / AC ticks.

**Checks**:

- **Invariant-preservation gate (before the evidence judgment, ┬з6.0, Directive #567)** тАФ sequenced **ahead of** the checks below: a Directive proposal or completion claim that **defers, weakens, or measurement-gates** a declared mandatory invariant (derived from existing SSOT тАФ issue AC / MISSION / ADRs / the affected-component contract, never invented) is gated as pass/fail тАФ `reject` a defer/weaken/gate of a definitional guarantee, or `revise` per the `revise`-vs-`reject` boundary rule; an **empty manifest** тЖТ the reviewer **attests the invariant set it checked against** ("none declared"), *not* a hard `reject` (┬з6.0). Same before-contest ordering and empty-manifest attestation as `plan-reviewer` (┬з4.8); contract SSOT: `.claude/agents/activation-reviewer.md`.
- **Schema completeness** тАФ does the body cover objective / success signals / non-goals / constraints / MISSION fit (or, for an Initiative-parented Directive, a `Parent Initiative: #N` marker)? Missing any тЖТ `revise`.
- **Parent-kind alignment** (#254) тАФ a Directive has exactly one parent kind; judge alignment against it: a `## MISSION fit` parent against the named MISSION section, a line-1 `Parent Initiative: #N` parent against that Initiative's termination condition. Both-or-neither parent kind тЖТ `revise` (the parent-XOR, ┬з1.7). The full per-check detail is in the contract SSOT `.claude/agents/activation-reviewer.md` (check 1.5).
- **Success-signal verifiability** тАФ are signals objectively testable, or vague aspiration? "Engineering reviews go faster" without a metric тЖТ `revise`.
- **Scope clarity** тАФ is the objective bounded? "Improve the codebase" тЖТ `reject`.
- **Non-goal clarity** тАФ are exclusions explicit or implied? Vague exclusions invite scope creep.
- **Active-Directive conflict** тАФ does the proposed Directive overlap with an existing `Status=Active` Directive? If yes тЖТ `revise` or `reject` with a pointer.
- **Evidence sufficiency (completion only)** тАФ do the linked Execution Issues collectively satisfy each success signal? A signal with no linked Execution Issue тЖТ `revise` ("need engineering evidence"). A signal whose Execution Issues are open or stalled тЖТ `revise`.

**Output** тАФ three verdicts: `pass` / `revise` / `reject` (the **reviewer verdict vocabulary** above). On `reject` the verdict additionally carries the structured refile fields (`verdict` / `reason` / `refile-target-type` / `refile-target-parent` / `refile-body-draft`) and follows the type-mismatch / parent-mismatch matrices. The full output contract тАФ verdict meanings, the `revise`-vs-`reject` boundary rule, the structured fields, both matrices, the `<!-- activation-verdict: <verdict> -->` marker, and the N=3 `revise`тЖТ`reject` escalation тАФ is specified in `.claude/agents/activation-reviewer.md` (the contract SSOT). Callers apply the post-verdict handling per ┬з2.1 (Directive lifecycle) and ┬з5.12 (`/activate`).

**Rules**: do not author body content for a `revise` (matches ┬з4.7 rule; the one exception is the `reject` `refile-body-draft` field тАФ drafting there IS the preserve signal). Verdict is content-only; filer identity affects only the caller's post-verdict handling. Judge from the inputs above only. Auto-approving without scanning active-Directive conflicts is a regression against the ┬з1.5 reviewer-pattern integrity.

#### 4.9.2 roadmap-reviewer (deferred)

Cross-Directive coherence check тАФ MISSION alignment, Directive sequencing, drift detection. Deferred until operating experience surfaces the friction; see MISSION's "Success looks like" тЖТ orchestrator criterion.

#### 4.9.3 Session-restart caveat for new reviewer subagents

Claude Code enumerates available `subagent_type` values **at session start** by scanning `.claude/agents/*.md`. A reviewer added mid-session is **not routable** as a first-class subagent until the next session start: `Agent({subagent_type: "<new-name>"})` falls back to `general-purpose`, which loses the Type-aware specialized prompt.

This caveat is the parallel of ┬з6.1's "Session-restart caveat for hook-spec changes" тАФ Claude Code binds its routing surfaces (hook configuration AND subagent enumeration) at session start. Both bindings are stable for the session's duration; both are picked up automatically at the next session.

Empirical confirmation (Directive #62 / PR #67-followup): in the dogfood session, `.claude/agents/directive-reviewer.md` landed via PR #50 mid-session (this reviewer was later renamed to `activation-reviewer` by Issue #170 under Directive #167; the historical filename is retained here because it records the actual PR #50 event). Every subsequent `Agent({subagent_type: "directive-reviewer"})` invocation routed through `general-purpose` because the harness's `subagent_type` enumeration had been frozen against the pre-#50 state. A session restart resolves this automatically тАФ no `.claude/settings.json` registration needed, no harness-config change. The same mechanism applies to the Issue #170 rename itself: until a session restart, `subagent_type: "activation-reviewer"` falls back to `general-purpose`.

**Mitigation for the in-session window**: the falling-back-to-`general-purpose` path is functionally complete тАФ the agent's prompt instructs `general-purpose` to behave as the new reviewer. The cost is the loss of Type-aware specialization (the harness's per-subagent prompt + tool restriction). Acceptable for one session; restart at session end is canonical.

**Hook-side note**: the smoke `┬з42` structural assertions (PR #50) lock the agent file's shape, so the routing-layer regression is the only failure mode this caveat names. The behavioral surface that catches the routing regression is **smoke ┬з42e** (issue #69, under Directive #62; extended for the type-neutral reviewer by #170): three assertions gated behind `GHJIG_BEHAVIORAL_SMOKE=1` invoke `activation-reviewer` with a synthetic minimal-but-valid Directive body (asserting `^VERDICT: pass`), a synthetic Directive body missing the `## Success signals` section (asserting `^VERDICT: (revise|reject)`), and a synthetic minimal-but-valid Execution Issue body exercising the Execution-rulebook dispatch (asserting `^VERDICT: pass`). Env-var unset тЖТ ┬з42e is a no-op so default smoke stays deterministic and offline; env-var set тЖТ the block exercises the live `subagent_type: "activation-reviewer"` route end-to-end. A regression in either the agent file or the routing surface flips at least one of the three verdicts.

> **┬з4.10 triage classifier тАФ retired (#173, Directive #167).** The former triage classifier agent was deleted: its `status:proposed` substantive gate is now `activation-reviewer` (┬з4.9), and its template-shape classification is absorbed by `/activate`'s type-mismatch matrix. `/triage` survives only as a one-cycle deprecation alias (see ┬з5.12). The `triage` audit category is retained in ┬з2.1 as append-only history. (The ┬з4.10 number is retired and not reused; the high-asymmetry reviewer tier below is **┬з4.11**.)

### 4.11 High-asymmetry reviewer tier (Issue #428)

A cross-cutting reviewer **tier**, not a subagent: where a wrong *approve* is irreversible or corrupts shared history, a single reviewer's verdict is replaced by an **N-way independent vote**. This is the reviewer-side counterpart of ┬з6.0 P1 тАФ the same cost-asymmetry that makes the protected-branch / secret matchers hard negative gates makes these *approvals* warrant redundancy. It is **blast-radius-gated, never a default**: N-way everywhere would bloat the acting context (the narrowing principle, MISSION) and correlate votes, so the common path stays single-reviewer. It extends the existing conditional dispatch (`/ship` step 2 already spawns `security-reviewer` only when the diff touches a security surface).

**Enumerated high-asymmetry decision set** (closed тАФ `is_high_asymmetry <kind>` in `helpers/blast_radius.sh` returns rc 0 for exactly these, rc 1 otherwise):
- `merge-security-surface` тАФ `gh pr merge` to the default branch of a PR whose diff touches a security surface (the ┬з4.6 trigger), at `/ship`.
- `force-push` тАФ a force-push / history-rewrite judgment surfaced *inside the `/ship` motion* (the ┬з13 rebase-pull tail or a named-branch escape). This is the **reviewer judgment** when a force-push is legitimately part of shipping тАФ distinct from the autopilot force-push **negative gate** (┬з6.1), which still blocks unreviewed force-pushes independently.
- `directive-completion` тАФ the `/complete-directive` evidence evaluation (┬з5.13).
- `irreversible-adr` тАФ merging a PR carrying an ADR (`docs/ADRs/`) to the default branch, at `/ship`. ADR *authoring* via `/adr` is a reversible doc-write (the file is editable until merged); the irreversible point is the merge, so the tier fires there, not in `/adr`.

**Mechanism тАФ N=3, majority=2, independent.** For a high-asymmetry decision the invoking skill spawns the relevant reviewer type (`security-reviewer` for `merge-security-surface`/`force-push`, `activation-reviewer` for `directive-completion`, `code-reviewer` for `irreversible-adr`) **three times as independent fresh subagent invocations** тАФ worktree-isolated, artifact-only (the ┬з4.5 "no knowledge of the main assistant's discussion" premise), with **no shared context** between the three. **Independence is load-bearing**: redundancy de-risks only if the votes don't correlate through a shared prime тАФ a serial debate where each reviewer sees the others' verdicts is explicitly *not* this (it is the rejected design).

**Fixed-denominator tally (#544).** The denominator is **fixed at 3**; majority = **2 valid approve-verdicts of 3**. A vote is *valid* only if the reviewer's independently-reported `reviewed-head` (┬з4.5) matches the caller's privately-held expected head (┬з5.7 blind compare); a mismatch, absent, or unconfirmed head is a **non-approve invalid vote тАФ fail-closed, never counted as APPROVE**. An invalid vote is **not an abstention that lowers the bar**: it still consumes one of the three slots, so two invalid votes make majority unreachable (max 1 valid approve) тЗТ non-majority тЗТ `hard` blocker тЗТ park. The bar is always 2-of-3, never 2-of-(valid votes).

This **parallel** N=3 is distinct from ┬з4.9.1's **serial** N=3 (the `revise`тЖТ`reject` escalation, which counts *consecutive revise verdicts on one reviewer across rounds*). Here the three are simultaneous, independent, and tally to one gate decision; there one reviewer is re-consulted over time.

**Mode coupling** (┬з5.7.1): in `unattended`, the majority tally gates directly (it substitutes for the human exactly as a single reviewer's verdict does). A non-majority on a high-asymmetry decision is a **`hard` blocker** тАФ unfixable without a product decision тАФ so `/ship` parks (┬з5.7.1 hard-blocker path) for human adjudication; the park is the named next action (┬з6.0 P4), not a bare refusal.

**Fail-open** (┬з4.9.3 / ┬з6.1 session-restart caveat): `is_high_asymmetry` is sourced via `safe_source`; on a miss (the helper absent in a pre-#428 session) the gated decision **degrades to a single reviewer** with an `audit_log warn reviewer-tier` record тАФ never a lockout. A wrong *degrade* costs the redundancy on one decision (recoverable); a lockout would block all shipping (not) тАФ the asymmetry that picks fail-open.

### 4.12 implementer (Issue #486; Directive #477)

**When**: Phase C (Code), **by default** тАФ `/work-on` routes the Code phase here via `/implement` (┬з5.28). The **opt-out** is for trivial / one-line / glue edits and the orchestrator's own glue (Directive #477 Non-goal 2), which the main assistant authors directly in its own loop. The default-flip is Directive #477 **signal-4**: the formal A/B measurement was descoped and the context-narrowing hypothesis (┬з1.2 / ┬з3.7) adopted as operating policy on circumstantial evidence, hedged by fail-open reversibility (a missing implementer path degrades to main-loop authoring) rather than a measured result.

**Premise**: the write-capable counterpart of the artifact-only reviewers (┬з4.5). It implements strictly from a supplied **manifest** and has **no knowledge of the main assistant's conversation** тАФ the same "judge/act from the artifact, not the discussion" discipline, applied to authoring rather than review.

**Input = manifest** (the caller assembles it, ┬з5.28): the **Plan** (PR-body / planner output), the **failing Phase-B test** + how to run it, the **named relevant file paths**, and the **directive-level learnings** тАФ the distilled `### Learnings for the next Execution` blocks `/work-on` (┬з5.3 step 4.5) reads back from the parent Directive's `/reflect` comments (┬з5.15) and injects as **advisory context** (closes Directive #477 signal 3). If the Plan or the failing test is missing, the manifest is incomplete тАФ the subagent reports and stops rather than inferring the intent; the directive-level learnings field is **optional** (advisory; its absence does not make the manifest incomplete).

**Output = structured return** (and nothing else): exactly (a) the commit / diff ref(s) authored, (b) plan-deviations (where/why it diverged from the Plan), and (c) discoveries (signal worth surfacing). The file reads, abandoned approaches, and lint/smoke iterations stay in the subagent's **ephemeral context** and are not returned тАФ that churn-discard is the point (the within-Execution authoring churn never re-enters the parent context).

**Norms**: follows Doc тЖТ Test тЖТ Code (it is the Code phase тАФ Doc/Test already exist, do not re-author them), commit-format (┬з10.2), and authors its commit in the **work language** (┬з5.7.2). Working-tree discipline (#285): write-capable, but git is constrained to its own `add`/`commit` тАФ stage **only the manifest-named paths** (`git add <those paths>`); **never** `git add -A`/`-u` (a blanket stage sweeps in the parent's uncommitted work), and never a tree-mutating git command (`checkout`/`restore`/`stash`/`reset`/`clean`) that touches it. Because the implementer is **not** worktree-isolated (its commit must land on the PR branch, ┬з1.5), this path-scoped-add discipline is the substitute for isolation; the caller also surfaces a dirty tree before dispatch (┬з5.28).

**┬з4.9.3 caveat**: a freshly-added `subagent_type: implementer` falls back to `general-purpose` until the next session restart; `implementer.md`'s self-describing prompt makes that fallback functionally complete (the Type-aware tool restriction is the only loss), restart is canonical.

---

## 5. Slash commands

### 5.0 `/bootstrap-repo`

**When**: once, on a brand-new target that has **no default branch** тАФ an empty GitHub repo (zero commits) or a greenfield local directory freshly `git init`'d (unborn HEAD). This is **stage-0**: it precedes `/onboard` (┬з5.1). The adoption lifecycle (`clone-into.sh` тЖТ `register.sh` тЖТ `/onboard` тЖТ `/onboard-dir-mode`, ┬з2) presupposes a default branch with at least one commit already exists; `/bootstrap-repo` is the step that produces it, so there is an owner for the no-default-branch starting state rather than ad-hoc manual git.

**Precondition**: the target has no commits / no default branch. If a default branch already exists (`git rev-parse --verify HEAD` succeeds), `/bootstrap-repo` **refuses** тАФ the repo is already past stage-0 and `/onboard` is the right entry point.

**Outputs**: a default branch (`main`) carrying a single seed commit тАФ `MISSION.md` from `.claude/templates/mission.md` and `README.md` from `.claude/templates/readme_for_target.md` тАФ pushed to the remote so the repo is ready for `/onboard`. Stage-0 seeds only these two SSOT files; `.github/` templates, labels, and substrate remain `/onboard` / `/onboard-dir-mode` concerns (┬з5.1, ┬з1.7).

**The bootstrap exception (target repos).** The protected-branch gate is name-based (`PROTECTED_BRANCH_PATTERN`, ┬з6.1): on an unborn HEAD, `git symbolic-ref --short HEAD` returns `main` (rc=0) while `git rev-parse --verify HEAD` fails, so `is_protected_branch()` matches by name and the seed commit (and the Edit/Write that authors `MISSION.md`/`README.md` on that branch) is blocked тАФ correct, desirable behavior for the general case. `/bootstrap-repo` owns the **narrowly-scoped** exception for *this one seed commit only* тАФ it does **not** weaken the gate. **In-agent escape (┬з7):** the two in-command forms are stripped before the hook in the live Bash tool, so they cannot disarm the seed commit. `/bootstrap-repo` instead writes a `branch`-category **file-based skip token** immediately before the seed commit тАФ `scripts/ghjig_skip.sh branch '<seed-commit-subject>' '<reason>'` тАФ and the seed commit then succeeds **in-agent** (the hook reads the token at fire time, audits it, and consumes it). The seed-commit subject is the high-entropy fingerprint:

```
scripts/ghjig_skip.sh branch 'chore: seed first commit (MISSION + README)' 'stage-0-bootstrap-seed-on-unborn-HEAD'
git commit -m "chore: seed first commit (MISSION + README)"
```

Running the seed commit in a **real terminal** (no hook in the path, the commit succeeds directly) remains the fallback. Either way the bypass routes through `should_skip branch` and is recorded in `audit.jsonl`. This generalizes the **shell's own-repo** first-commit exception (┬з16 item 15) to *target* repos: both are the same chicken-and-egg case (the first commit cannot ride a flow that presupposes a prior commit).

**Steps**:

1. **Preflight** тАФ refuse if `git rev-parse --verify HEAD` succeeds (already has commits) with `"target already has a default branch тАФ run /onboard, not /bootstrap-repo"`. Refuse if not inside a git work tree.
2. **Seed SSOT** тАФ copy `MISSION.md` from `.claude/templates/mission.md` (a draft for the user to complete) and `README.md` from `.claude/templates/readme_for_target.md`, **via a Bash file copy** (`cp`), not the Edit/Write tool. The Edit/Write protected-branch arm (┬з6.1) blocks writes on the unborn-HEAD `main` and cannot be disarmed by a trailing sentinel (there is no command string to carry it); a `cp` into the registered target path carries no protected-branch check and is in-scope, so it is the correct seeding path.
3. **Seed commit** тАФ `git add MISSION.md README.md`, write the `branch`-category file token (`scripts/ghjig_skip.sh branch '<seed-commit-subject>' '<reason>'`, ┬з7), then run the seed commit above **in-agent** (the hook reads, audits, and consumes the token at fire time). Running it in a **real terminal** is the fallback. The seed commit message is a `chore` (no issue # required тАФ there is no issue tracker state yet).
4. **Publish** тАФ `git push -u origin main` (GitHub adopts the first pushed branch as the repo default).
5. **Handoff** тАФ print `Next: /onboard` so the operator continues into the read-only onboarding check.

**Forbidden**:
- Running on a repo that already has a default branch (preflight refuses).
- Bypassing the protected-branch gate for anything other than the single seed commit тАФ the exception is scoped to stage-0, not a general escape.
- Mutating `/onboard`'s responsibilities (`.github/`, labels, substrate) тАФ stage-0 seeds only `MISSION.md` + `README.md`.

### 5.1 `/onboard`

**When**: once, right after a target repo is first cloned. **Precedes**: stage-0 `/bootstrap-repo` (┬з5.0) must already have produced a default branch тАФ `/onboard` is a read-only check and assumes a seedable, cloned, registered repo; a brand-new target with no default branch goes through ┬з5.0 first.

**Steps**:

1. **Upstream check** тАФ `gh repo view --json isFork,parent`. Fork тЖТ block.
2. **Permission check** тАФ push permission required. Missing тЖТ advise and block.
3. **Target SSOT check**:
   - `MISSION.md` present? Absent тЖТ strong warning + draft proposal from `.claude/templates/mission.md` (no auto-create).
   - `SPEC.md` present? `SPEC.md` is **required for any project that carries code** (┬з1.3) тАФ it is the behavioural SSOT, so requiredness keys on the presence of code, not on whether an external contract (CLI, API, schema, protocol) exists. Absent on a code-carrying project тЖТ scaffold the slot from `.claude/templates/spec.md` (no auto-authoring of contract content тАФ the MISSION boundary).
   - Report `README.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` presence.
4. **`.github/` check**:
   - `ISSUE_TEMPLATE/` absent тЖТ suggest shell template.
   - `PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md` absent тЖТ suggest shell template.
   - `CODEOWNERS` absent тЖТ recommend.
5. **Branch protection check** тАФ `gh api repos/{owner}/{repo}/branches/main/protection`. Report missing items (PR required, review required, status checks required, force push blocked). Setup requires admin, so just print commands.
6. **CI presence** тАФ check `.github/workflows/`. Absent тЖТ recommend appropriate workflows.
7. **Local git-hook tier** (┬з6.7) тАФ install and verify the committed `.githooks/` enforcement tier by running `scripts/install_git_hooks.sh`, which sets the **repo-local** `core.hooksPath` (never `--global`/`--system`, ┬з3.4), then `--check` to confirm activation. Because the change is repo-local and reversible (`git config --unset core.hooksPath`), this is the one activation `/onboard` performs rather than only recommends тАФ it respects the ┬з3.4 user-global boundary. The per-clone bootstrap gap (a clone that never ran the installer) is re-surfaced each session by the SessionStart drift arm (┬з6.7).

No automatic changes beyond the repo-local git-hook activation (step 7). All other recommendations require human review and execution.

### 5.2 `/file-issue [--quick] <description>`

**Steps**:
- Confirm title, body, label with the user.
- Force MISSION reference and acceptance criteria in the body.
- **Rationale check** (before `gh issue create`): surface (a) which MISSION item this serves, (b) why now vs later, (c) whether an existing issue or an open-PR follow-up note would suffice. If any of (a)тАУ(c) is weak, refine the issue or drop the request instead of filing. The check is mandatory тАФ Auto / unattended mode does not skip it; a poorly-justified issue propagates downstream into planner output and merged code, where the cost of redirection is highest.
- **Reviewer gate**: invoke `issue-reviewer` (┬з4.7) on the proposed body before `gh issue create`. In `attended` mode the verdict surfaces to the user (who may override); in `unattended` mode the verdict gates the next step (`ship` тЖТ proceed; `refine` тЖТ re-author the body with the feedback and re-invoke; `block` тЖТ stop and surface the reason). The reviewer fills the human-confirm slot when no human is present. On a **non-pass** verdict the invoking flow emits a categorized reject-audit record (`issue-review`/`plan-review`/`activation` category + a reason-class token; the contract lives in ┬з6.1, #361) тАФ this applies to every reviewer gate in the command family (issue-reviewer here, plan-reviewer ┬з5.3, activation-reviewer ┬з5.12/┬з5.13), feeding the `scripts/promotion_candidates.sh` consumer.
- `--quick`: one-line issue (label `bug`) for fast creation. Rationale check + reviewer gate still required, in compressed form (one-line "serves X mission item, blocks Y" suffices). The `bug` label matches the `bug-report.yml` Issue Form template.
- **Directive parenting** (added by tracking #41 child #6, issue #47): when the new Issue is parented to a `Status=Active` Directive (via `--parent <directive-id>` or interactive prompt listing active Directives, ┬з1.7), prepend the `Parent Directive: #N` body marker (line 1); the Project `Parent` field is **derived** from that marker by `issues-to-project-mirror.yml` тАФ `/file-issue` writes the Issue only, never the Project directly (┬з1.7 Issues-as-SSOT). `--no-parent` opts out. Rationale check + `issue-reviewer` gate apply unchanged тАФ parenting is metadata, not part of the rationale triad.
- **Full-symmetry stamp** (#172): `gh issue create` applies the `status:proposed` label so every new Execution Issue enters the lifecycle as Proposed and requires `/activate <N>` (┬з5.12) before it is actionable.
