This is why `issue-reviewer` (author-side, here) and `activation-reviewer` (observer-side, at `/activate`) are complementary, not redundant (┬з2.1). The output `Next:` line points at `/activate <N>`. `/work-on` against a `status:proposed` Issue is blocked by `proposed-protect` (┬з6.1) until activation.
- **Priority** (#291; parity with `/file-directive`, ┬з5.10): `/file-issue` captures a `P0`/`P1`/`P2`/`P3` priority and applies it as a label at create time, so an Issue never lands priority-less (a priority-less backlog can't be triaged). Source order: an explicit `--priority P<N>` flag тЖТ else **ask the user** in `attended` mode тЖТ else **default `P2`** in `unattended` mode (the same default `/file-directive` uses). The `P<N>` label is **graceful-degradation guarded** тАФ applied only if present on the target (tier тЙе 2), else a warn and file-without-it тАФ and the priority is also recorded in the `issue-file` audit line so it survives a degraded label. An Execution Issue carries its own priority (it does not silently inherit the parent Directive's).
- Call `gh issue create`, return the number.

### 5.3 `/work-on <issue#> [--base <branch>]`

**Steps**:

1. `gh issue view <#> --json title,body,labels,comments` тАФ read the issue.
2. Validate body тАФ if acceptance criteria are missing or vague, ask the user to fix it. **Don't start work with an ambiguous goal.**
3. Resolve the **target base** (default `main`; override via `--base <branch>`). `git fetch origin && git checkout <base> && git pull --ff-only`. If `<base>` is not `main` and is not reachable locally or remotely, fail with a clear message тАФ `/work-on` does NOT auto-create alternate bases (see ┬з10.5).
4. Create branch:
   ```
   USER=$(gh api user --jq .login)
   TYPE=<detected type>
   SLUG=<kebab of issue title>
   git checkout -b "${USER}/${TYPE}/${ISSUE}-${SLUG}"
   ```
   If the branch already exists on remote: `git pull --ff-only origin <branch>`.
4.5. **Read back directive-level learnings** (closes Directive #477 signal 3 тАФ the directive-level coding-memory loop). When the Issue body carries a `Parent Directive: #N` marker (line 1, ┬з5.2), read the accumulated `### Learnings for the next Execution` blocks from #N's enriched `/reflect` comments (┬з5.15) and inject them as **advisory context** into (a) the planner input (step 5) and (b) the `directive-level learnings` field of the `/implement` manifest (┬з4.12). Advisory only тАФ context the next Execution starts from, never a gate; absent/empty learnings (no parent Directive, or no enriched reflections yet) is a normal no-op. This is the *read* half of the loop `/reflect`'s Learnings section (┬з5.15) writes.
5. Invoke `planner` agent (with issue body + MISSION + target CLAUDE.md context + the resolved `<base>` + the step-4.5 directive-level learnings when present). The planner produces **one base Plan A** and **no longer authors `## Alternatives considered`** тАФ the interested party no longer controls the choice set (┬з4.8). Its output must include the mandatory `## Target base` section (┬з4.1); the `Target base` value must equal the `<base>` passed in.
5.5. **Axis selection.** Run the lightweight **upstream axis selector** (homed here, between the planner and the challenger dispatch тАФ *not* inside a challenger or the reviewer, since mutually-blind challengers cannot self-coordinate distinctness): designate the **2 highest-leverage _focus_ axes for this specific change** (a **weight, not a filter** тАФ ┬з4.8) from the fixed menu **{correctness, simplicity/maintainability, performance, security, cost/effort, robustness/risk, extensibility, UX}**, and assign one to each challenger as its lead. **No hardcoded axis pair** (a fixed pair would relocate the omission bias by systematically excluding performance/security тАФ ┬з4.8). Emit the observe-only **drop-axis attestation** (`audit_log info plan-axis` тАФ source `hookrt.sh` then a bare `audit_log`; ┬з4.8, Directive #570).
5.6. **Challenger dispatch.** Dispatch **two independent, mutually-blind `plan-challenger` agents** (┬з4.8.1), **parallel + worktree-isolated**, one assigned axis each. Each attempts to **beat Plan A** and returns one of: **dominates-A**, a **genuine non-dominating alternative**, or a **reasoned concession** (names the axis tried + why A held). This step **rides the existing planner gate** тАФ it fires exactly when the planner is invoked (non-trivial changes), never on trivial/glue edits; there is **no new tier gate and no `blast_radius` involvement**.
6. **Reviewer gate**: invoke `plan-reviewer` (┬з4.8) to **judge the contest {A, B1, B2}** тАФ the base Plan A plus the two challenger outputs with their assigned axes. Parse the verdict line (`^VERDICT: (ship|refine|block)`). In `attended` mode the verdict surfaces to the user; in `unattended` mode it gates the next step (`ship` тЖТ step 7; `refine` тЖТ re-run the contest with the feedback, then re-review; `block` тЖТ stop with a comment on the issue naming the structural problem). On any non-pass verdict the flow emits the categorized reviewer-reject-audit record (┬з6.1). The reviewer substitutes for the human reviewer when no human is present.
7. **Wait for user approval of the plan.** Approval requires an **approach check**: confirm with the user that the winning candidate from the contest record (A / B1 / B2 / verdict) is the right one, not just that a plan exists. In `unattended` mode, a clean `plan-reviewer` verdict from step 6 counts as approval.
8. **Write and commit Phase A (Doc)** тАФ the first commit on the branch is real Doc work, never an empty seed. The branch graph begins with content the PR Plan describes, not a placeholder.
   ```
   # тАжedit the SSOTs identified by the plan (MISSION, README, CLAUDE.md, ARCHITECTURE, ADR)тАж
   git add <changed SSOTs>
   git commit -m "<type>(#<#>): <subject>

   {Closes|Refs} #<#>"
   git push -u origin HEAD
   gh pr create --draft --base "<base>" --title "<type>(#<#>): <subject>" --body "<template>"
   ```
   First-line trailer: use `Closes #<#>` when `<base>` is the repo's **default branch** (resolved via `gh repo view --json defaultBranchRef`, not a hardcoded `main` тАФ #504); otherwise use `Refs #<#>` (per ┬з10.4 тАФ the issue closes only when work reaches the default branch, which is `main` on most repos but `master`/other elsewhere).

   If the planner's Phase A isn't ready to commit (e.g. blocked on clarification), defer the PR тАФ keep the issue + plan in conversation. **Never fall back to an empty seed commit just to open the draft PR.**
9. Insert plan + checklist + ship gate sections in the PR body.
10. Sync internal TaskList with the checklist.
11. Continue with the next phase (Test).

### 5.4 `/sync-pr`

Explicit entry point for updating the PR body. The main assistant does this automatically; this command lets the user trigger it on demand. After a successful sync, `/sync-pr` references `/replan-check` (┬з5.26) as a post-sync advisory step тАФ the body was just curated, the natural cadence to compare it against the actual diff for structural divergence.

Refetch the remote body once before updating. The shell stores the SHA-256 of the last body it saw at `.claude/state/pr-cache/<owner>%2F<repo>__pr-<n>.json` (the `/` between owner and repo is URL-encoded as `%2F` so `<owner>/<repo>` slug boundaries survive the filename); the file holds at least `last_seen_body_sha256`, `last_synced_head`, and `last_synced_at`. If the remote body's SHA differs from `last_seen_body_sha256`, an external edit happened (reviewer, parallel session, GitHub UI) тАФ the automatic update aborts with a stderr message naming the conflict, and merging is the human's call. After a successful sync the cache is rewritten. A corrupt cache file (unparseable / missing key) also aborts the sync rather than silently treating as "first sync."

The cache lives under `.claude/state/`, which is gitignored тАФ it's per-clone state, not part of the repo's history. The helper `.claude/hooks/helpers/pr_cache.sh` exports `pr_cache_read`, `pr_cache_write`, and `pr_cache_check`. The repo slug is derived from `gh repo view` of the cwd, overridable via `$PR_CACHE_REPO` (used by the smoke test suite). `/ship` reuses the cache transitively by routing its body curation through `/sync-pr` (┬з5.7 step 5). `/work-on` doesn't update the body after PR creation, so it doesn't touch the cache directly; later edits go through `/sync-pr`.

### 5.5 `/status`

`/status` and the `UserPromptSubmit` hook both delegate to the canonical helper at `.claude/hooks/helpers/status.sh`. Two output modes:

- `status_compact` тАФ multi-line plaintext block, the standard turn-context surface.
- `status_json` тАФ same fields as stable JSON for diff-comparison or piping.

Fields (both modes):
- Branch + dirty status
- Linked issue (#, title) тАФ extracted from `Closes #N` / `Refs #N` in the PR body
- PR (#, draft/ready, checklist progress `[x/y]`, CI status) тАФ `gh pr view`, `gh pr checks`
- Next unchecked checklist item
- Current phase (Doc / Test / Code / Review / Ship), inferred from the next unchecked item's section heading
- Active mode (attended / unattended) per ┬з5.7.1
- **Bound canonical root** (#318) тАФ the shared shell root this project resolves to, surfacing the ┬з1.7 shared-code model. Source: `$GHJIG_ROOT` (exported by the hooks after self-location, ┬з3.2.1) or `readlink $CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/.claude/ghjig-root`.
- **Ephemeral-state locality** (#318) тАФ `project-local` when `ghjig_state_dir()` resolves to `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/.claude/ghjig-state` (the normal hook-context case, ┬з3.2.2), else `legacy-shared`. Surfaces that audit/caches/registry isolate per project.
- **Active work language** (#325) тАФ the language of durable repository artifacts, resolved via `resolve_work_lang` (┬з5.7.2). Compact `work-lang:`, JSON `work_lang`.

`UserPromptSubmit` (┬з6.4) emits `status_compact` instead of a hand-rolled branch summary. Keeping the source single ensures `/status` and per-turn injection never drift.

The UserPromptSubmit hook reuses this output for the short per-turn summary.

**Cache**: status results are cached at `.claude/state/status-cache/<branch>.json` with a TTL of `STATUS_CACHE_TTL` seconds (default 5; env-overridable). The cache key is the branch name, so a `git checkout` to a different branch transparently loads a different cache file. Hits skip every `gh` round-trip (today: `gh pr view`, `gh issue view`, `gh pr checks` тАФ 3 calls per uncached invocation). The 5-second TTL is short enough that real PR/issue/CI changes surface within one user turn (turns typically exceed 5 s) and long enough to dedupe a flurry of prompts. Cache files live under `.claude/state/` (gitignored).

### 5.6 `/review [--staged | <base>]`

Invokes `code-reviewer`. If the diff touches a security surface, also invokes `security-reviewer`. No auto-fix unless explicitly asked.

**Reviewer-head pin (#544)**: when reviewing a pushed PR, `/review` applies the same caller-side blind compare as `/ship` (┬з5.7) тАФ compute the expected head privately (`gh pr view <n> --json headRefOid`, never revealed to the reviewer), compare each reviewer's independently-reported `reviewed-head` (┬з4.5), and treat a mismatch/absent head as a fail-closed invalid vote. The reviewer resolves its artifact from the PR head per ┬з4.5.

### 5.7 `/ship`

Runs the ship sequence from ┬з2 (steps 0тАУ8), plus the pre-ready sub-step gates 7.5тАУ7.7 detailed below. `/ship` runs the full test suite (step 4) before transitioning to ready (step 8). Tests are `/ship`'s responsibility; the hook does not add a separate test gate on ready transition (┬з6.1).

**High-asymmetry reviewer tier** (┬з4.11): when a ship decision is high-asymmetry тАФ a `merge-security-surface` merge to the default branch, a `force-push` judgment inside the ship motion, or an `irreversible-adr` merge (a PR carrying `docs/ADRs/`) тАФ `/ship` classifies it via `is_high_asymmetry` and replaces the single-reviewer verdict with an N=3 independent majority vote. A non-majority is a `hard` blocker тЖТ park (┬з5.7.1). The common path (no high-asymmetry kind) stays single-reviewer.

**Reviewer-head pin тАФ caller-side blind compare (#544).** Because a worktree-isolated reviewer is checked out at the base, not the PR head (┬з1.5), the reviewer pins its artifact to the PR head and reports `reviewed-head:` (┬з4.5); `/ship` closes the loop from the caller side:
- **Compute expected head once, privately.** Before dispatch, `/ship` resolves the true head via `gh pr view <n> --json headRefOid` and **holds it privately тАФ it is NEVER passed to or revealed to any reviewer.** Passing it would let a reviewer echo it back (a tautological pass); the reviewer must derive its `reviewed-head` *independently* for the compare to mean anything.
- **Blind compare each verdict.** `/ship` compares every reviewer's independently-reported `reviewed-head` against the private expected head. A verdict whose `reviewed-head` тЙа current PR head, or is absent/unconfirmed, is a **non-approve: an invalid vote, fail-closed тАФ never counted as APPROVE** (feeds the ┬з4.11 fixed-denominator tally: invalid тЙа abstention).
- **`gh`-resolve failure at dispatch тЖТ park (hard).** If `/ship` cannot resolve the expected head at all, no reviewer output can be trusted тЖТ `hard` blocker тЖТ park (┬з5.7.1). A reviewer's *own* fetch/resolve failure instead makes only *its* vote invalid. No path proceeds unchecked.
- **Merge-time re-pin (TOCTOU).** Before the merge step, `/ship` re-reads the PR head; if it has advanced past the reviewed SHA since the votes were cast, the prior review is **stale тЖТ re-review**. Never merge an unreviewed head.

**Live immediately for #544's own ship.** The caller-side leg (compute-expected-head + blind compare + non-approve) lives in `ship.md`/`review.md` command text, read at invocation time тАФ so it is **in force immediately for this fix's own ship**, independent of the ┬з4.9.3 session-restart caveat. That caveat gates only the *agent-prompt* changes (the reviewer-side `reviewed-head` emission in `code-reviewer.md`/`security-reviewer.md`), which route through `general-purpose` until the next session restart; the caller-side gate does not wait on a restart.

**Merge-review gate (#586, replacing the merge-attestation file, #544).** The pre-merge review integrity backstop is a **GitHub review at the current PR head**, not a local attestation file. The ┬з6.1 `merge-review` gate admits a `gh pr merge` only when a passing review exists **pinned to the head being merged** тАФ a native `APPROVED` review whose `commit_id` equals the current head, or (for a self-shipped PR) a self verdict marker at the head under the identity constraints in ┬з6.1. A skipped review (no head-pinned passing review), a stale review (an `APPROVED`/marker at a superseded head), or an outstanding `CHANGES_REQUESTED` at the head all **block**. The gate reads the review objects authoritatively via `gh` and fails CLOSED on any lookup failure (┬з6.1). Because the evidence is a real GitHub review rather than a forgeable local file, an **aborted or failed review leaves no passing head-pinned review** and the merge stays blocked. **Merge-time re-pin (TOCTOU)**: a late push that advances the head past the reviewed SHA makes the prior review stale тАФ the gate blocks and the review must re-run at the new head; never merge an unreviewed head. Automated production of that review inside `/ship` тАФ invoking `/file-review` (#585) at the confirmed head after the review pass resolves and before the merge тАФ is **delivered in #587**: `/ship`'s clean arm now posts the head-pinned review itself when `review-gate=required` and none exists yet, then merges via the classifier-deferred exact form (┬з5.7.1). #586 delivered the gate and the toggle; #587 integrates the auto-production, so the head-pinned review is now produced by `/ship` rather than by a separate manual `/file-review` invocation.

CI monitoring: snapshot `gh pr checks --json state` right before ready transition тАФ already failing тЖТ block. Right after the transition, run `gh pr checks --watch` in background and return immediately. On failure, the PostToolUse hook notifies the user.

**Checklist audit (mandatory step 7.5, between CI snapshot and `gh pr ready`)**: scan the PR body for any `- [ ]` line. Each unchecked item must be resolved before transition тАФ ticked if done, marked `[~] N/A тАФ <reason>` if intentionally skipped, or removed if obsolete. The audit applies to every checklist in the body (Plan, Test plan, Docs touched, Ship gate). Per SPEC ┬з1.4, stale uncheckedness at merge propagates as misinformation into future context.

**Issue AC closeout (mandatory step 7.6, before `gh pr ready`)**: for every issue in the PR's `closingIssuesReferences`, run `scripts/ac_closeout.sh <pr-num>` to post the canonical `## AC closeout (resolved by PR #N)` comment with each acceptance-criterion item ticked or `[~] N/A`'d. The helper is idempotent, and its skip guard mirrors the gate **exactly** тАФ it skips an issue only when a **trusted-filer** comment (author association тИИ OWNER/MEMBER/MAINTAINER/COLLABORATOR) already carries the strict canonical `^## AC closeout (resolved by PR #N)` marker; a loose `^## AC closeout` lookalike or an untrusted-author comment does **not** satisfy the skip (#556). Were the remedy's guard looser than the gate's, a drive-by lookalike would make the remedy skip while the gate kept blocking тЖТ merge deadlock. The PreToolUse `ac-closeout` gate (┬з6.1) blocks `gh pr merge` when an unchecked-AC closing issue lacks this marker, so running step 7.6 here satisfies the merge gate by construction. Steps 7.5 (PR-body side) and 7.6 (issue side) together are the symmetric halves of "PR-as-living-doc" (┬з1.4) across the `Closes #N` linkage. Skipped (all-Directive closing set) when Directives close via `/complete-directive`, not AC checkboxes.

**Changelog gate (mandatory step 7.7, before `gh pr ready`)**: the PR must satisfy the ┬з18.1 fragment contract (CI-enforced per ┬з18.6) *before* ready, not after a red CI check тАФ exactly one of {a fragment exists for the PR number or one of its `closingIssuesReferences`, the `skip-changelog` label is present} must hold. This is a **presence** check; fragment *shape* stays CI's job (┬з18.5). When neither holds, `/ship` invokes `/changelog` (┬з5.23) to author the fragment or apply the label тАФ `attended` proposes for confirmation, `unattended` decides automatically (┬з5.7.1) тАФ so the flow self-heals instead of failing at CI. The skip decision follows ┬з18.7.

When mode is `unattended` (see ┬з5.7.1), `/ship` continues past step 8 into the CI-wait тЖТ merge / park branch.

### 5.7.1 Operating modes (attended / unattended)

`/ship` has two terminal behaviors selected by **mode**:

- **`attended`** (default): `/ship` stops at "ready" and hands off to a human reviewer.
- **`unattended`**: after "ready", `/ship` waits on CI / required reviews and either merges or parks the PR for human attention.

**Resolution priority** (high тЖТ low):

1. `--mode=<attended|unattended>` flag on `/ship`
2. `$GHJIG_SHELL_MODE` env var
3. `.claude/state/mode` per-target file (one of `attended` / `unattended`, no other content)
4. default `attended`

Unknown values fail closed to `attended` and emit a stderr warning naming the offending source. `settings.json` is intentionally **not** a layer тАФ that file is symlinked across targets (┬з3.2) and a mode key would leak between unrelated work.

**Review-gate toggle** (`.claude/state/review-gate`, #586). A separate, orthogonal toggle governs whether the ┬з6.1 `merge-review` gate is enforced. It takes one of two values:

- **`required`** (default): a `gh pr merge` is admitted only when a passing GitHub review exists at the current PR head (the `merge-review` gate, ┬з6.1).
- **`bypass`**: the `merge-review` gate is skipped тАФ the merge is admitted without a head-pinned review тАФ **except** it still **blocks** a covered-form (`gh pr merge --auto --merge --delete-branch`) **agent self-merge** (PR author == merger, fail-closed on the author/merger lookup), the #592 backstop that keeps the static `permissions.allow` (┬з5.7.1) from ever being the sole guard for that exact form. **Every `bypass` merge is loudly audit-logged** (`audit_log warn merge-review bypass`) so a standing bypass never goes unobserved (┬з6.5(d) friction advisory reads the aggregate).

**Resolution priority** (high тЖТ low), mirroring the mode and work-lang toggles:

1. `$GHJIG_REVIEW_GATE` env var
2. `.claude/state/review-gate` per-target file (`required` / `bypass`, cwd-relative, read exactly as `resolve_mode` reads `.claude/state/mode`)
3. default `required`

`resolve_review_gate` (home: `ship_mode.sh`) is the resolver. **Unknown / empty / whitespace-only / malformed values fail CLOSED to `required`** тАФ the deliberate divergence from `resolve_mode`, which fails to `attended`. The safe direction differs by what the toggle guards: `resolve_mode`'s failure surface is *autonomy* (fall back to the more conservative human-in-the-loop `attended`), whereas `review-gate`'s failure surface is a *merge integrity gate* тАФ the conservative direction there is to **require** a review, not to **skip** it. A garbled value must never silently open the gate. Like the mode and work-lang toggles, `settings.json` is intentionally **not** a layer тАФ it is symlinked across targets (┬з3.2) and a review-gate key would leak between unrelated work.

**Blocker taxonomy** тАФ `ship_classify_blocker` returns one of:

| State | Criterion |
|-------|-----------|
| `clean` | All required CI checks green; required reviewers (if any) satisfied; branch protection rules satisfied. Eligible for auto-merge. |
| `soft` | CI is `pending` / `in_progress` / `queued`, **or** there is a CI failure that is attributable to the agent's own last commit and is fixable without new product decisions. One self-fix attempt is permitted (see below). |
| `hard` | Required-review with no available reviewer, undiagnosable / non-attributable CI failure, branch-protection rule the agent cannot satisfy, or a `soft` state that has already consumed its one self-fix attempt. |

**Soft-blocker behavior**: at most **one** self-fix-and-push attempt per `/ship` invocation. The retry pushes a `fix(#N): ...` commit and returns to the CI-wait state. A second `soft` outcome immediately escalates to `hard` тАФ no further fix attempts.

**Hard-blocker behavior** (parking) тАФ all four actions, in order, and idempotent:

1. Post a `gh pr comment` with a deterministic state summary (blocker reason + current SHA + CI snapshot).
2. Apply label `unattended-parked` (create the label on demand if missing). If the label is already present from a previous park on the same PR, `ship_park_pr` writes a single `park-suppressed: <reason>` line to the log instead of reposting the comment, and emits no comment to stdout. The original park comment remains canonical; the label remains applied.
3. Append one line to `${SHIP_PARK_LOG_PATH:-$GHJIG_ROOT/.claude/state/unattended-park.log}` (shell-side, gitignored тАФ not the target's MEMORY.md). The override exists for smoke-test isolation. On suppressed repeat, only the `park-suppressed: <reason>` line is appended. **Additionally, on a fresh park** (not the suppressed-repeat arm), `ship_park_pr` emits one `audit_log warn unattended-park parked "reason=<token>"` record (guarded by `command -v audit_log` тАФ best-effort, so a standalone invocation without the runtime still writes the park-log unconditionally). This is **additive** (the human-readable park-log is unchanged, not a schema change): it bridges overnight park frequency тАФ the highest-value unattended friction signal тАФ into `audit.jsonl`, the aggregate the ┬з6.5(d) friction advisory reads, so parks stop being invisible to the friction-observability loop (#398, Directive #391). The `unattended-park` audit category records park-as-friction-signal; it is read **directly** by the ┬з6.5(d) advisory (neither `narrowing_candidates.sh` nor `promotion_candidates.sh` matches a `warn`/`parked` record).
4. Stop. Do not toggle draft or self-assign.

**Classifier robustness**: `ship_classify_blocker` fails closed to `hard` in two failure modes and emits a one-line stderr warning naming the cause:

- empty stdin тЖТ `ship_classify_blocker: no input on stdin тАФ defaulting to hard`
- missing `jq` dependency тЖТ `ship_classify_blocker: jq not found тАФ defaulting to hard`

The intent is to make overnight runs debuggable without changing the safe fail-closed default. Either condition resolves the classification to `hard` and the dispatch path proceeds to park.

**Merge mechanism**: `gh pr merge --auto --merge --delete-branch` (no-fast-forward merge commit; PR branch's commits are preserved on `main`). This requires repo-level auto-merge to be enabled at GitHub. If the API call fails because auto-merge is disabled, fall back to the park path (log + label + comment) with reason `auto-merge-disabled`.

**Why `--merge` rather than `--squash`**: SPEC ┬з1.2 makes the Doc тЖТ Test тЖТ Code commit graph load-bearing тАФ the arc is the artifact that proves the discipline happened. Squash erases the arc on merge (the PR branch is deleted; only a single new commit lands on `main`). `--merge` keeps both: the individual phase commits stay on `main`, plus a merge commit anchors the PR-as-a-unit so `git log --first-parent main` gives a clean PR-level view. The visible cost is a busier `git log`; the audit-trail philosophy in ┬з6/┬з7 trades that for the preserved arc.

**Composition with branch protection**: server-side rules in GitHub are always authoritative. `unattended` does not bypass them. A required-reviews rule with no available reviewer resolves to `hard` and parks тАФ the shell never self-approves or auto-requests review against policy.

**Composition with Auto mode**: Auto mode (single-conversation clarification suppression) is orthogonal to operating mode. Any combination is valid: `attended + Auto`, `unattended + non-Auto`, etc. Mode controls the `/ship` terminal behavior; Auto controls in-turn prompting.

**Composition with the auto-mode classifier (#587)**: Claude Code's auto-mode classifier is an **outer harness authority** тАФ like branch protection above, the shell does not own it and cannot repeal it; in auto mode it adjudicates each shell command the agent runs. A narrow `permissions.allow` entry for the **exact** `/ship` merge form тАФ `Bash(gh pr merge --auto --merge --delete-branch)`, an order-sensitive exact match (no trailing-argument wildcard) that resolves *before* the classifier тАФ makes the classifier **defer that one command** to the shell's own `merge-review` gate (#586, ┬з6.1). It opens nothing else: any other `gh pr merge` shape (a positional PR number, `--repo`, a different flag order) misses the matcher, so the classifier re-engages.

**Bypass coupling (load-bearing).** The `permissions.allow` entry is **static** тАФ a rule cannot read shell state, so it defers the classifier for the covered exact form **unconditionally**, regardless of `review-gate`. The deferral is safe **only while `review-gate=required`**, where `/ship` emits the covered command solely *after* the merge-review gate accepts. Under `review-gate=bypass` the merge-review hook self-skips its review requirement (┬з6.1) тАФ save the #592 covered-form self-merge backstop below тАФ so `/ship` **withholds** the covered exact form entirely: any merge it would attempt uses a *non-covered* shape (a positional PR number, a different flag order) that the classifier still adjudicates, so an unattended agent self-merge blocks and `/ship` parks (the classifier **re-engages** on the non-covered shape). Safety under `bypass` therefore rests on `/ship`'s **command discipline** тАФ not emitting the covered form тАФ plus the classifier gating every non-covered shape; it does **not** rest on the classifier re-engaging on the covered form (it does not тАФ that form is statically deferred). This upholds Directive #584 Constraint 1 for the sanctioned `/ship` flow: no `/ship` path lets an unattended agent self-merge without a shell review gate in front of it. **Closed (#592):** the `merge-review` hook now **blocks a covered-form agent self-merge** (PR author == merger) even under `bypass` тАФ fail-closed on the author/merger lookup тАФ so an emission of the exact covered string faces the hook regardless of `review-gate`, and the static `permissions.allow` is **never the sole guard**. What `bypass` still admits is honest and narrow: **non-covered** shapes (the classifier re-engages on them) and **human**-initiated merges (author != merger) stay allowed тАФ `bypass` still means "no shell *review* requirement" for those, not an open door for an agent self-merge of the covered form. This entry remains **shell-side discipline that buys visibility, not independence** (below), gated behind a deliberate, loudly-audited, non-default operator opt-out.

**Scope (cross-target).** The `permissions.allow` entry lives in this shell's own `.claude/settings.json` **and** is injected into every onboarded target via `settings.injected.json` (┬з3.2) (#591) тАФ so each target gets the classifier exception paired with the already-injected `merge-review` gate (#586), closing the asymmetric install where a target had the gate without the exception. Cross-target propagation was deferred at #587 until #584 was dogfood-proven; with that bar cleared (┬з6.0-P3 "prove-then-propagate"), the entry now ships to targets. **Blast-radius tradeoff (disclosed).** The exception applies in **every** target with **no per-target opt-out** тАФ a static allow rule cannot read per-target state. It is bounded on two sides: (a) the **exact-form matcher** covers only the single `/ship` canonical merge command (`Bash(gh pr merge --auto --merge --delete-branch)`, order-sensitive, no wildcard), so no other `gh pr merge` shape is opened; and (b) the injected `merge-review` gate remains the **real guard** in each target тАФ the entry only changes *which* guard adjudicates the covered merge (the shell's `merge-review` gate rather than the harness classifier), so it is **shell-side discipline** that buys **visibility, not independence**.

**Second exception тАФ the self-review producer (#598).** The merge entry above is inert without a passing head-pinned review to satisfy the `merge-review` gate, and under `review-gate=required` `/ship` produces that review itself by invoking `/file-review` at the confirmed head (┬з5.29, #587). On an agent-authored PR that review is a **self** `COMMENT` carrying a `verdict=approve` marker, and its submission (`gh api тАж/pulls/<n>/reviews тАж`) is a *different* command the classifier adjudicates separately; left uncovered it blocks as self-approval, so the whole sanctioned self-merge path parks at the producer step тАФ the merge entry alone is dead, because you cannot merge without the review it cannot post. The merge exception therefore requires a **paired** producer exception. But the raw POST is **dynamic** (`commit_id`, PR number, and `--field body=@<tmpfile>` all vary), so it cannot be matched by an exact wildcard-free rule, and a `gh api тАж/reviews:*` prefix would open `event=APPROVE`/`REQUEST_CHANGES` on **any** PR тАФ far past "self-`COMMENT` only." The resolution is a **fixed-form shell-owned wrapper**, `scripts/ghjig_file_review_post.sh`, invoked via the uniform `.claude/ghjig-root/` path (┬з3.2 тАФ the same convention `ac_closeout.sh` uses, so one rule resolves in the dogfood shell *and* every onboarded target): **no positional args** (it resolves the current-branch PR itself, mirroring `gh pr merge --auto`'s resolution model), the sanitized body staged **out-of-band** to a fixed path resolved via `ghjig_state_dir_cli()` (a hookrt.sh helper) by a separate writer `scripts/ghjig_file_review_stage.sh` and read by the wrapper under a **60s TTL + one-shot unlink** (fail-closed on empty / absent / stale / future-dated / malformed тЖТ no post), and `event=COMMENT` plus an **own-PR fail-closed guard** (acting identity == PR author) hardcoded inside. The `permissions.allow` surface is then the exact, order-sensitive, **wildcard-free** string `Bash(.claude/ghjig-root/scripts/ghjig_file_review_post.sh)` тАФ parity with the merge entry's "opens nothing else." The wildcard-free match still holds, but on a corrected basis: the covered wrapper is invoked **bare** тАФ no argv, no pipe, no redirect тАФ so no wildcard is forced, and the body travels **out-of-band via the state file, not on stdin**. The earlier "stdin is invisible to the permission matcher" premise was **false in the Claude Code harness**: stdin cannot be supplied to a bare covered command via the Bash tool тАФ the same limitation that already forced the file-based `ghjig_skip.sh` skip token (┬з7). The staged `head=<sha>` bind is a **staleness guard** тАФ it rejects a body staged for a superseded head after a late push тАФ **not** an anti-forge mechanism; anti-forge integrity remains at the `merge-review` gate, which binds `author.login == PR-author == merger` @ `commit_id == head` from the review object and reads only `verdict` from the marker. The wrapper *is* the capability boundary: even invoked adversarially it can only post a self `COMMENT` review тАФ never `APPROVE`/`REQUEST_CHANGES`, never another author's PR тАФ so the deferral opens exactly the shape #585/#586 already sanctioned (a self `verdict=approve` marker honored *only because a real `code-reviewer` ran*), nothing more.

**Per-target self-review policy (`.claude/state/self-review`, #598).** The wrapper's allow entry тАФ like the merge entry тАФ is **static** and injected into every target (┬з3.2), so it defers the classifier everywhere. But whether an agent self-review is *acceptable* at a given target is a **per-project** decision, and per the isolation model (┬з1.7 / MISSION "shared code, per-project state") it belongs in **per-project state**, not the shared allow rule. `resolve_self_review_policy` (`helpers/ship_mode.sh`; resolution order `$GHJIG_SELF_REVIEW` тЖТ `.claude/state/self-review` тЖТ default, read exactly as `resolve_review_gate` reads its state) returns `allow` | `deny` and **fails closed to `deny`** тАФ a garbled / absent / unknown value must never silently accept self-approval (the same safe-direction reasoning as `review-gate`'s fail-closed-to-`required`). The `merge-review` gate's **self-marker** acceptance (shape (b), ┬з6.1) additionally requires `resolve_self_review_policy == allow`; under `deny` a self-marker does **not** satisfy the gate тАФ only a native second-party `APPROVED` at head does, so the unattended self-merge path parks there. **Every context тАФ dogfood shell and onboarded target alike тАФ defaults to `deny`**; the state file is per-project and **gitignored** (┬з3.2.2), so it is never committed/shipped via git. An operator opts a project in by creating `.claude/state/self-review = allow` **locally** (the dogfood shell's operator does this to dogfood the self-merge). The injected wrapper entry moves adjudication to the shell everywhere, but self-review stays *off* until that local opt-in тАФ so the cross-target blast radius of the static entry is bounded by a per-project state gate no clone inherits by default. This is the **state-managed** answer to the merge entry's "no per-target opt-out" tradeoff above: the review *producer* is deferred everywhere, but the *policy* that decides whether the produced self-review counts is per-project state the operator controls.

Note: ┬з6.1's "direct push to protected branch blocked" hook is **not** tripped by the merge step тАФ `gh pr merge --auto` is a GitHub API call, not a `git push` to `main`.

**Directive-aware audit** (added by tracking #41 child #6, issue #47): when the merged PR's linked Issue carries a `Parent Directive: #N` marker (┬з5.2), `/ship` appends one audit line `directive-exec-count directive=#N pr=#M issue=#K` to `audit.jsonl`. The audit reads `closingIssuesReferences` тАФ so in topic-branch flow (┬з10.5), sub-task PRs (which use `Refs #N`) emit no audit line, and the audit fires only on the **consolidator PR** that closes each parented Execution Issue at the moment work reaches `main`. Informational only тАФ `/ship` does **not** auto-mark the Directive `Completed`. Completion is `/complete-directive`'s job, gated by `activation-reviewer` (┬з4.9). This preserves the ┬з1.5 invariant: generation is open, decision is gated.

**Canonical hook-enforced path** (Directive #61): `.github/workflows/dir-mode-post-merge.yml` (installed from `.claude/templates/target-substrate/workflows/dir-mode-post-merge.yml`) fires on every `pull_request.closed && merged == true` event, regardless of who performed the merge (Claude-in-loop, human via UI, CI auto-merge). The Action emits an equivalent reflection comment on the parent Directive тАФ the comment surface IS the audit surface for hook-enforced events, since the workflow runner cannot write to a per-clone `audit.jsonl`. The Markdown procedure above stays valid for Claude-in-loop runs (defense in depth); the workflow posts a marker-stamped **stub** and `/reflect` enriches it in place, the two paths deduping on the `reflect-stub`/`reflect-enriched` **content markers** rather than the shared PR URL (#329 тАФ see ┬з5.15).

### 5.7.2 Communication language vs work language

The shell separates two independent language channels (#322):

- **Communication language** тАФ the humanтЖФagent conversation. Whatever language the user writes in; the agent's chat replies stay in it. The shell never detects, configures, or translates it.
- **Work language** тАФ the single language of **durable repository artifacts**. Resolved by `resolve_work_lang` (`.claude/hooks/helpers/work_lang.sh`), defaulting to `en`.

**Per-surface classification** тАФ every shell-authored artifact is one or the other:

| Work language (durable, in the repo) | Communication language (ephemeral, in the chat) |
|---|---|
| commit messages; PR titles/bodies; issue / directive / execution bodies; acceptance criteria; changelog fragments; shell-authored code comments; audit `reason` text | the agent's conversational replies to the user |

**Pre-work context-recast step.** After the human conversation concludes and **before authoring any durable artifact**, the agent re-organizes the task context into the work language тАФ it does not transliterate the chat verbatim but re-expresses intent, decisions, and plan in the work language, then authors every work-language surface from that recast. This is the "narrowing/normalization" half of the MISSION mechanism applied to language: durable memory and the artifact-only review surface stay legible in one consistent language regardless of the conversation language.

**Resolution priority** (high тЖТ low), mirroring ┬з5.7.1:

1. `$GHJIG_WORK_LANG` env var
2. `.claude/state/work-lang` per-target file (a single language code, cwd-relative тАФ read exactly as `resolve_mode` reads `.claude/state/mode`)
3. default `en`

Any non-empty language code is accepted **verbatim** (BCP-47-style tokens such as `en`, `ko`, `fr`, `ja`, `pt-BR`) тАФ there is no closed enum, so the capability generalizes to any (communication, work) pair and is never `ko`/`en`-hardcoded. An empty / whitespace-only value resolves to `en` (the surface is named in a stderr note). `resolve_work_lang` is `set -u`-safe and makes no external calls beyond `head`/`tr`.

**Config placement** тАФ `.claude/state/work-lang`, **not** `ghjig-state/`. Work language is user-set, set-once **configuration** (the same tier as the `mode` toggle ┬з5.7.1 and the `coauthor` toggle ┬з10.2), not regenerable **ephemeral state** (`ghjig-state/` holds the audit log, caches, and registry тАФ ┬з3.2.2). Directive #322's body says "ghjig-state" but cites "the mode toggle" as the analog; the mode toggle lives at `.claude/state/mode`, so `work-lang` follows that concrete precedent (config tier, cwd-relative) rather than the mislabeled category word. Like ┬з5.7.1, `settings.json` is intentionally **not** a layer тАФ it is symlinked across targets (┬з3.2) and a work-language key would leak between unrelated projects.

Back-compat: unset тЖТ `en`, i.e. today's behavior; nothing changes for a target that never sets a work language. **Surfacing** is delivered (#325): `status_compact` emits a `work-lang:` line and `status_json` a `work_lang` key (resolved via `resolve_work_lang`), so `/status` and the per-turn statusline show the active work language alongside `mode`. **Skill integration** is delivered (#327): the artifact-authoring skills (`file-issue`, `file-directive`, `work-on`, `ship`, `complete-directive`) each carry a `## Work language` note instructing the agent to recast context and author their durable artifact in the work language тАФ co-located with the authoring step (skills-as-environment) so the instruction survives context-narrowing. Enforcement is agent-followed prose, not a hook: the *language of free prose* is not mechanically checkable (#322 success signal 2 delegates it to review); smoke grep-locks only that each skill carries the note.

### 5.8 `/adr <title>`

**ADR vs PR body Decisions**:
- **ADR** тАФ irreversible, system-level. Migrations (DB engine, schema change), external contracts (API spec, wire format), default technology choices (auth scheme, queueing model). High cost to reverse once merged.
- **PR body Decisions** тАФ reversible, PR-scoped trade-offs. Default option choice, algorithm tuning parameters, equivalent-library preference, naming choices. Explainable within this PR and not affecting other PRs.

`/adr` creates `docs/ADRs/NNNN-title.md` (from `.claude/templates/adr.md`). A `тЖТ ADR-NNNN` link is auto-added to the PR body's Decisions section. Authoring is a **reversible doc-write** (the file is editable until merged), so the high-asymmetry reviewer tier (┬з4.11) does *not* fire here тАФ it fires at the irreversible point, the PR merge carrying the ADR, in `/ship`.

### 5.9 `/audit [<filter>]`

Query `.claude/audit/audit.jsonl`. Recent blocks / escapes / warns. A frequently-escaped category is a signal to tune the hook.

### 5.10 `/file-directive`

Create a new Directive as a GitHub Issue with `directive` + `status:proposed` labels. AI-assisted authoring from `.claude/templates/directive.md` (Objective / Success signals / Non-goals / Constraints / MISSION fit тАФ MISSION.md reference replaces a separate parent-goal artifact). Routes through `activation-reviewer` (┬з4.9) before commit; verdict gates per ┬з5.7.1 mode rules (`reject` parks the proposal to `.claude/state/directive-block.log`). Audit category: `directive-file` (reason format: `directive: <Objective summary> issue=#<N> priority=P<P> confidence=<C>`). The Project Item is created and populated by `.github/workflows/issues-to-project-mirror.yml`; `/file-directive` does NOT write to the Project. **Priority encoding (#185):** the `P<P>` label (`P0`тАУ`P3`, installed in the tier-2 set by `scripts/ensure_v3_labels.sh`, ┬з0.4) is the mirror-readable projection of priority and is applied with graceful degradation тАФ present тЖТ labeled; absent тЖТ warn + file without it (never abort), per ┬з0.4. The body `## Priority` field + the `directive-file` audit line are the durable priority record; the label is the queryable/mirror projection. Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/file-directive.md`.

### 5.11 `/list-directives [--status <state>]`

List Directive Issues filtered by Status label. Read-only тАФ queries Issues directly; does NOT consult the Project (which is a derived view that may lag). `--status` accepts `Proposed | Active | Blocked | Completed | All`; default omits `Completed`. Tabular output: `# / Status / Priority / Title`. Status derivation per Issue: `status:proposed` label тЖТ Proposed; `status:blocked` label тЖТ Blocked; closed + reason=completed тЖТ Completed; open + no `status:*` label тЖТ Active. No audit emission. Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/list-directives.md`.

### 5.12 `/activate [<issue-#>]`

Promote a `Proposed` Issue (Directive **or** Execution Issue тАФ `/activate` is type-neutral) to `Active` by removing the `status:proposed` label after a fresh `activation-reviewer` (┬з4.9) pass on the current body. This is the observer-side gate of the full-symmetry lifecycle (┬з2.1): every Issue is filed `status:proposed` and becomes actionable only after `/activate` returns `pass`. `/activate` is also the **unblock** path for a Blocked Directive (┬з5.17): a re-activatable Issue carries `status:proposed` (Proposed) **or** `status:blocked` (an Active-but-Blocked Directive); only when **neither** label is present is the Issue plain Active and `/activate` errors "already Active". On `pass` it removes whichever of `{status:proposed, status:blocked, awaiting-author}` are present (each removal presence-guarded тАФ `gh issue edit --remove-label` errors on an absent label). Batch mode scans `--label status:proposed`, so it does **not** sweep Blocked Directives тАФ unblock is single-mode `/activate <N>` only (auto-unblocking would silently reverse a deliberate maintainer block).

- **Single mode** `/activate <N>`: resolve `<N>`'s type label (tri-state, matching `activation-reviewer`'s ┬з4.9 dispatch тАФ an `initiative`-labelled Issue is **refused**, not activated: Initiatives are consumed via `/consume-initiative` (┬з5.21) and live outside the ProposedтЖТActive lifecycle (┬з2.1); a bare `directive`-else-Execution split would otherwise mis-type one as Execution. The guard normally never fires because an Initiative never carries `status:proposed`), invoke `activation-reviewer` with the type context, parse the verdict, and apply it:
  - `pass` тЖТ remove the present activation labels (`status:proposed` and/or `status:blocked`, plus `awaiting-author` if present) тЖТ Active.
  - `revise` тЖТ post the findings as a comment carrying `<!-- activation-verdict: revise -->`, retain `status:proposed`, add `awaiting-author`. After **N=3** `revise` markers on the Issue, escalate to `reject`.
  - `reject` тЖТ post the verdict + structured fields with `<!-- activation-verdict: reject -->`, then apply **filer-aware handling** (verdict is content-only; handling keys on `authorAssociation` via `is_trusted_filer`): **trusted** тЖТ keep open + `awaiting-author`, never close (composes with `trusted-filer-mutate`, ┬з6.1); **untrusted + `refile-body-draft`** тЖТ close (`--reason "not planned"`) + auto-create a `discussion`-tier Issue (┬з5.19) preserving the draft + a lineage link; **untrusted, no draft** тЖТ close + brief comment.
- **Batch mode** `/activate` (no arg): scan all open `status:proposed` Issues and process each. **Loop-safety:** skip an Issue whose latest `<!-- activation-verdict: <verdict> -->` comment marker post-dates its last body/label edit (verdict already delivered, awaiting the author) тАФ independent of the `awaiting-author` label. In `attended` mode `reject` surfaces to the operator; in `unattended` it auto-applies the filer matrix.
- **Reviewer invocation** is robust to the ┬з4.9.3 session-restart caveat: the agent file is on disk and its prompt is self-describing, so a `general-purpose` fallback still behaves as the reviewer.

`/activate-directive <issue-#>` is retained as a **thin alias** delegating to `/activate <N>` for one release cycle (Directive-only ergonomics), then removed. Audit category: `activation`. The mirror workflow fires on `issues.unlabeled` and updates the Project Item's Status. Escape: see ┬з7. Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/activate.md`.

### 5.13 `/complete-directive <issue-#>`

Close a Directive Issue with `--reason completed`. `activation-reviewer` (┬з4.9) evaluates evidence тАФ the linked Execution Issues' close states / AC ticks тАФ against the success signals. **Directive completion is a high-asymmetry decision** (┬з4.11, `directive-completion`): the evidence evaluation runs as an N=3 independent majority vote of `activation-reviewer`, not a single verdict (a wrong "complete" is irreversible тАФ it closes the Directive). A non-majority leaves the Issue open. `reject` (insufficient evidence) leaves the Issue open. On `pass`, posts a closing comment listing each signal and its evidence, then closes the Issue. The `trusted-filer-mutate` hook matcher (SPEC ┬з1.5, ┬з6.1) allows `--reason completed` on trusted-filer Issues without further confirmation. Audit category: `directive-complete`. Escape: see ┬з7. The mirror workflow fires on `issues.closed` and updates the Project Item's Status. When the Directive's Execution Issues used the topic-branch flow (`/work-on --base <topic-branch>`, ┬з10.5), `/complete-directive` must run **after** the topic branch consolidates to `main` тАФ the reviewer reads closed-Execution-Issue evidence, and still-open `Refs`'d Issues yield insufficient-evidence verdicts. Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/complete-directive.md`.

### 5.14 `/link-directive <directive-#> <execution-#>`

Link an Execution Issue to its parent Directive by ensuring the `Parent Directive: #<directive-#>` line-1 body marker is set on the Execution Issue + posting cross-reference comments. Idempotent тАФ re-running on an already-linked pair no-ops with an info-level audit line. The Project Item's `Parent` field is mirrored from the body marker by `.github/workflows/issues-to-project-mirror.yml`; `/link-directive` does NOT write to the Project directly. Audit category: `directive-link`. Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/link-directive.md`.

### 5.15 `/reflect [<pr-#>]`

Post a structured reflection comment on a PR's parent Directive (when one exists) summarizing the PR's contribution toward that Directive's success signals. Run after merge; idempotent тАФ classifies the Directive's existing comments by **content marker** (#329): a `<!-- reflect-enriched pr=#N -->` comment тЖТ no-op; the hook-enforced floor's `<!-- reflect-stub pr=#N -->` тЖТ **enrich in place** (edit that comment by REST comment id); neither тЖТ post fresh. (Keying on the marker, not the shared PR URL, is what lets `/reflect` enrich the workflow's at-merge stub instead of no-op'ing against it.) Resolves the parent Directive from each closing Issue's body via the regex `^Parent Directive: #(\d+)$` (the marker `/file-issue --parent` writes on line 1, SPEC ┬з5.2) тАФ **label-aware** (#335): it climbs the marker chain to the first `directive`-labelled ancestor (depth-cap 2, cycle guard, fail-soft) rather than stopping at the first marker, so a nested-umbrella Execution Issue reflects onto the grandparent Directive, not the intervening umbrella. Audit category: `directive-reflect` (decisions: `posted` / `skipped`). Read-only on the linked Execution Issues; writes only the reflection comment on the Directive Issue. The human-readable counterpart to `/ship` step 10.5's bare `directive-exec-count` audit (SPEC ┬з5.7). Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/reflect.md` (added by tracking #41 child #6, issue #47).

**Hook-enforced floor** (Directive #61): `.github/workflows/dir-mode-post-merge.yml` posts a **stub** reflection automatically on every merged PR with a `Parent Directive:` marker (marked `<!-- reflect-stub pr=#N -->`), so the reflection trail is complete regardless of who merged. The workflow resolves the target Directive via a **sourced helper** `resolve_parent_directive.sh` (shipped alongside the workflow and read after `actions/checkout`) rather than inline run-block bash, so the resolution тАФ the label-aware climb to the first `directive`-labelled ancestor (#335) тАФ is CI-shellchecked and smoke-executed; a resolved-nothing run logs a visible no-op. The helper has three byte-identical copies (canonical `scripts/lib/`, this-repo runtime `.github/workflows/`, and the target-substrate copy installed into onboarded targets), kept in lock-step by a `cmp` smoke assertion (the same discipline that holds the three workflow YAML copies in sync). The same workflow also runs the **bare-`Refs`-to-default check** (`detect_bare_refs_directive.sh`, #337, ┬з10.5): when a merged PR's base is the live default branch, its closing set is empty, and its body carries a directive-scoped `Refs #N`, it posts a single idempotent warning comment on the PR тАФ surfacing the ┬з10.5 leak that would otherwise silently deprive the Directive of a reflection. Warn-only, fail-soft, and (unlike a `gh pr merge` hook) it fires on human UI merges too. When Claude runs `/reflect`, it produces the richer per-signal block by **editing that stub in place** (PATCH by REST comment id), swapping the marker for `<!-- reflect-enriched pr=#N -->`. The two paths dedupe on the **content markers**, not the shared PR URL (#329): a URL-keyed check would make `/reflect` no-op against the workflow's at-merge stub and the enrichment would never happen. Classification: enriched-marker present тЖТ no-op; stub-marker present тЖТ enrich in place; neither тЖТ post fresh.

**`### Learnings for the next Execution` section** (closes Directive #477 signal 3 тАФ the directive-level coding-memory loop). The enriched reflection comment carries a fourth section alongside Contribution / Success signals advanced / Next: distilled **durable coding signal** from the merged PR's Code phase тАФ codebase gotchas, conventions to follow, what to reuse vs avoid тАФ and, when the `/implement` path (┬з5.28) authored the PR, drawn additionally from the structured-return **discoveries**. **Distillation heuristic**: keep only learning that **outlives this PR** and would help a sibling Execution under the same Directive; the within-Execution **churn** (file reads, abandoned approaches, lint/smoke iterations) is the ┬з1.2 / ┬з3.7 discard boundary and is **not** transcribed. This is the *write* half of the loop `/work-on` step 4.5 (┬з5.3) reads back. **Idempotency is unchanged**: the section rides **inside** the existing reflection comment under the same `reflect-stub` / `reflect-enriched` marker (a fourth body section, not a new comment), so the step-3 classification and the PATCH-by-REST-id enrich-in-place flow are untouched.

### 5.16 `/revise-directive <issue-#>`

Replace an `Active` Directive Issue's body with a new one when scope or success signals changed, archiving the prior body as a comment for history. Procedure: (1) read the current body; (2) compute its sha256; (3) invoke `activation-reviewer` (┬з4.9) on the **new** body тАФ the same proposal checks as `/file-directive` (schema / parent-kind alignment / success-signal verifiability / scope / non-goal / active-Directive conflict); (4) on `pass`, post a `## Pre-revision body тАФ archived <ISO date>` comment with the verbatim prior body, then replace the Issue body via `gh issue edit --body-file`; (5) emit `audit_log info directive-revise reconciled "directive=#<issue-#> from-sha=<prior-sha> archive-comment=<url>"`. **No Status change** тАФ the audit-log entry + the archive comment ARE the durable evidence of revision (no transient state needed тАФ see ┬з2.1). On `revise` or `reject`, leave the body unchanged. Escape: see ┬з7. Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/revise-directive.md`.

### 5.17 `/block-directive <issue-#> --reason <why>`

Mark an `Active` Directive as `Blocked` by adding the `status:blocked` label and a `## Blocked: <reason>` comment. Procedure: (1) require the `--reason <why>` flag тАФ empty or missing reason aborts; (2) post a `## Blocked: <reason>` comment on the Issue (idempotent тАФ skip if the same `## Blocked:` marker is the latest comment AND `status:blocked` label is already present); (3) add the `status:blocked` label via `gh issue edit --add-label`; (4) emit `audit_log info directive-block created "directive: #<issue-#> reason=<short> comment=<url>"`. The Issue stays **open** on GitHub тАФ closing the Directive Issue continues to require `/complete-directive` (┬з5.13). Unblock by running `/activate <issue-#>` (the `/activate-directive` alias delegates to it): it treats `status:blocked` as a re-activatable precondition, re-invokes `activation-reviewer` on the current body, and on `pass` removes the `status:blocked` label (┬з5.12). Not reviewer-gated тАФ blocking is an annotation, not a body change. Audit category: `directive-block`. The mirror workflow fires on `issues.labeled` and updates the Project Item's Status. Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/block-directive.md`.

> **┬з5.18 `/triage` тАФ deprecated alias (#173, Directive #167).** `/triage`'s `status:proposed` substantive gate is now `/activate` (┬з5.12), and its stale-discussion surfacing (open `discussion` Issues > 14 days, formerly ┬з5.19 step 2.5) moved into `/activate` batch mode. `/triage` survives one release cycle as a thin alias delegating to `/activate`; its notice names the Phase-2 gap honestly тАФ `/activate` subsumes only the `status:proposed` half, while raw-filing classification is now handled by `auto-status-proposed.yml` (#179). Full alias body: `.claude/commands/triage.md`.

### 5.19 Discussion tier (Issue #112 substrate; Directive #109)

A distinct open-Issue tier alongside Directive / Execution / task / bug. **Purpose**: capture deliberately-ambiguous observations ("weird but not a bug", half-formed ideas, smells, RFC-style probes) without forcing premature classification. The tier exists because the other tiers each force a misclassification on such filings: `task` reads as actionable, `bug` claims a defect, and skipping filing loses the observation entirely. Discussion is the honest path. (Raw label-free filings are auto-stamped `status:proposed`+`task` by `auto-status-proposed.yml` (#179) and validated at `/activate`; deliberate ambiguity is filed `discussion` instead.)

**Labeling**: a single `discussion` label (color `#FEF2C0`, light yellow) installed by `scripts/ensure_v3_labels.sh` alongside the other dir-mode labels. Issue Form template at `.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/discussion.yml` requires only title + body тАФ no acceptance criteria, no MISSION fit, no rationale-triad prompt; the reduced-required shape is the whole point.

**Lifecycle**: develop in comments. Discussion Issues are NOT parented to Directives (no AC; nothing to roll up). The Issue's comment thread IS the development surface.

**Close paths** тАФ exactly two:

- **`promoted`** тАФ a concrete Issue (bug / task / Directive) was filed; the discussion closes referencing it (`gh issue close <N> --reason completed` plus a `^promoted to #<M>$` comment). The new Issue cross-references back.
- **`no-action`** тАФ the discussion concluded nothing needs doing (`gh issue close <N> --reason "not planned"` plus a one-line comment naming the reason). The `gh` CLI accepts only `{completed|not planned|duplicate}` тАФ the **space** form; `not_planned` (underscore) is rejected by `gh`, so the space form is canonical everywhere the value reaches `gh`.

No third path. Stale discussions surface via `/activate` batch mode (┬з5.12; relocated from `/triage` by #173); no auto-close timer.

**Tier-relationships table**:

| Tier | Label(s) | AC-bearing? | Parented under Directive? | Close paths |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Directive | `directive` + `status:*` | No (success signals instead) | No (root of the hierarchy) | `/complete-directive` (┬з5.13) тАФ Completed via reviewer ship |
| Execution | (none, or template-applied) | Yes | Optional (`--parent`) | `Closes #N` via PR merge |
| task | `task` | Yes | No | `Closes #N` via PR merge or close-as-not-planned |
| bug | `bug` | Yes | No | `Closes #N` via PR merge or close-as-not-planned |
| **discussion** | `discussion` | **No** | **No** | **`promoted` or `no-action` only** |

**Lifecycle implementation** (Issue #116; Directive #109 final slice):

- `/discuss <title>` тАФ friction-free filing; bypasses the rationale triad + `issue-reviewer` gate. Full procedure in `.claude/commands/discuss.md`.
- `/resolve-discussion <N> [--promoted-to <M>] [--no-action <reason>]` тАФ closes via exactly one of the two paths above. Idempotent. Full procedure in `.claude/commands/resolve-discussion.md`.
- Close-path enforcement тАФ hook matcher arm under `trusted-filer-mutate` (┬з6.1) blocks `gh issue close <N>` on a `discussion`-labeled Issue without `--reason completed` OR `--reason "not planned"`. The matcher tolerates both the gh-valid space form and the legacy underscore so it is never itself the blocker; the canonical emitted form is the space form. Discussion-tier classification is evaluated **first and independent of filer trust** (#236): once an Issue is recognized as `discussion`, the ┬з5.19 two-path rule governs тАФ `--reason completed` OR `--reason "not planned"` is allowed regardless of the filer's `authorAssociation`, and a bare close or `--reason duplicate` is blocked. The trusted-filer block (below) applies only to **non-discussion** Issues. Stage 1 of the close-arm two-stage check (stage 2 = trusted-filer enforcement).
- `/activate` batch mode (┬з5.12; relocated from `/triage` by #173) тАФ surfaces open `discussion`-labeled Issues older than 14 days as a maintainer-decision queue (promote / dismiss / let-incubate). Mode-independent: AI does not autonomously promote/dismiss even in unattended.
- Smoke ┬з62 тАФ 8 assertions covering skill files, hook close-path enforcement (block + allow paths, the gh-valid `"not planned"` space form + legacy-underscore tolerance + a `duplicate` negative, #216), and `/triage` extension.

**Lockstep with Directive #107**: the `discussion` label is in `/onboard-dir-mode`'s bootstrap-label set (the dir-mode label set тАФ see the canonical count in ┬з1.7's Tier 2 note). #112 (label substrate) merged first; #116 (lifecycle) merged second; #107's `/onboard-dir-mode` consumes both.

### 5.20 `/release <X.Y.Z> [--base <branch>] [--dry-run]`

Cut a versioned release by consolidating per-PR changelog fragments into a new section of `CHANGELOG.md` and opening a `release/X.Y.Z` draft PR. Implements the fragment-contract consumer side of SPEC ┬з18.

Procedure (full body in `.claude/commands/release.md`):

1. **Parse args** тАФ required `<X.Y.Z>` (semver 0.x; reject `MAJOR > 0` with explicit `SPEC ┬з3.5 / ┬з18.2 MAJOR=0 invariant` message), optional `--base <branch>` (default `main`; for maintenance-line cuts per ┬з18.3 / ┬з10.5), optional `--dry-run` (helper stages but does not commit/push/branch).
2. **Preflight** тАФ assert clean working tree on the target base, `git fetch --tags origin`, refuse if `release/X.Y.Z` branch exists on origin OR `vX.Y.Z` tag already exists (exits 0 with `already released` message тАФ idempotent retry).
3. **VERSION write-back** тАФ strip any `-dev` suffix from the top-level `VERSION` and write `X.Y.Z`. Resolution-time queries fall back to `git describe --tags`; write-back is `VERSION`-only per ┬з18.2.
4. **CHANGELOG consolidate** тАФ read every `changelog_unreleased/<category>/<N>.md`, validate (positive-integer filename stem; bullet contains `(#<N>)` matching stem), prepend a new `## [X.Y.Z] тАФ YYYY-MM-DD` section (UTC date) to `CHANGELOG.md` with `### <Category>` subheadings (Keep-a-Changelog), append `[X.Y.Z]: https://github.com/<owner>/<repo>/releases/tag/vX.Y.Z` reference link at the file footer.
5. **Fragment cleanup** тАФ `git rm` every consumed fragment file (leave the six `.gitkeep` placeholders intact).
6. **Branch + draft PR** тАФ create `release/X.Y.Z` (short-lived; covered by the existing `release/*` arm of the protected-branch matcher per ┬з6.1). Commit the VERSION + CHANGELOG + fragment-removal as a single **scopeless** `chore: release X.Y.Z` commit under the documented `SKIP_HOOKS=branch SKIP_REASON='/release initial release-branch commit'` escape (audit-logged; structurally required since the protected-branch matcher blocks all direct commits on `release/X.Y.Z` and this is the one purposeful commit). The subject is scopeless тАФ not `chore(release): тАж` тАФ because the `commit-format` matcher permits only a `(#N)` scope or no scope, and the `branch` escape does not cover `commit-format`. Push, open a draft PR titled `chore: release X.Y.Z`.
7. **Reviewer gate** тАФ in `unattended` mode, re-run `code-reviewer` (┬з4.5) against the release diff before `gh pr create` to catch malformed CHANGELOG concatenation / mismatched tag / VERSION drift. Per ┬з1.5 reviewer-substitution. Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=release-review SKIP_REASON='<why>'`.
8. **On-merge tag + Release** (documented post-merge step; **maintainer-run, not automated** per ┬з18.5 non-goals тАФ this is the one step that sits *past* the `unattended` autonomy ceiling, which terminates at `gh pr merge`/park (┬з5.7.1); the `unattended` `/release` continuation stops at the merged release PR and does **not** cut the tag/Release): after the release PR merges to the target base, the maintainer runs:
    ```bash
    MERGE_SHA=$(git rev-parse HEAD)  # on target base, post-merge
    awk '/^## \[X\.Y\.Z\]/{f=1; next} /^## \[/{f=0} f' CHANGELOG.md > /tmp/release-notes-vX.Y.Z.md
    gh release create vX.Y.Z --title vX.Y.Z --target "$MERGE_SHA" --notes-file /tmp/release-notes-vX.Y.Z.md
    scripts/release_verify.sh X.Y.Z   # post-merge verify (below)
    ```
    Re-running on an already-released tag is a no-op with a clear message. **No `--verify-tag`** (#448): the flag aborts `gh release create` unless the tag already exists, but the tag is created *together with* the Release here (from `--target`), so it would always abort on a fresh release.

    **Post-merge verify** (#471, Directive #468): `scripts/release_verify.sh X.Y.Z` is a **read-only, fail-open** confirmation run *after* the create тАФ it checks the `vX.Y.Z` tag exists and a GitHub Release with **non-empty notes** is present (one `gh release view --json tagName,body` query), printing a named advisory line on a missing tag / missing-or-empty-notes Release. It **never creates** anything and **exits 0 on every path** (gh error / offline тЖТ one advisory line), so it observes the release result without blocking тАФ the verification-only / never-false-block posture (┬з6.0 cost-asymmetry). The `unattended` `/release` continuation runs it after its post-merge create.

`/release` factors deterministic work into `scripts/release_consolidate.sh` so smoke can exercise it against throwaway repos without booting a Claude Code session (same precedent as `scripts/ac_closeout.sh` тЖФ `/ship` step 7.6). Audit category: `release` (decisions: `created`, `idempotent`, `blocked`).

### 5.21 `/consume-initiative <N>` (Issue #257; Directive #256)

The consume flow (SPEC ┬з1.7 "Initiatives тАФ the planning tier the shell consumes"): turn an upstream `initiative`-labelled Issue into Initiative-parented Directive proposals, working backward from its termination condition. A **prompt-driven skill** (`.claude/commands/consume-initiative.md`), script-less like `/file-directive` тАФ the load-bearing work (judging the contract, decomposing the termination condition, authoring Directive bodies) is LLM reasoning, not mechanizable steps. Procedure:

1. **Type/substrate check** тАФ resolve `#N`; require the `initiative` label (else error). Same-repo only (cross-repo Initiatives are out of scope, ┬з1.7).
2. **Contract gate** тАФ invoke `activation-reviewer` (Initiative rulebook, contract-evaluability I1, ┬з4.9). If the termination condition is not evaluable without code knowledge тЖТ the Initiative is under-specified: post a plain `gh issue comment <N>` surfacing it upstream and **STOP** (file no Directives). `gh issue comment` is the only Initiative write the flow performs тАФ allowed by `initiative-readonly` (┬з6.1), which blocks only `edit`/`close`/`reopen`.
3. **Extract (working backward)** тАФ restate the termination condition, decompose it into the sub-outcomes that together satisfy it, and map each to one Directive proposal. The **necessary-and-sufficient** framing is the *faithfulness criterion* the I2 gate checks (necessary тЖТ no Directive exceeds the condition; sufficient тЖТ the set covers it), **not** a deterministic decomposition algorithm тАФ the partition is judgment. Each proposal carries a line-1 `Parent Initiative: #N` marker and **no `## MISSION fit` field** (the parent-XOR is satisfied by the marker; the Initiative traces to MISSION upstream).
4. **Faithfulness gate** тАФ invoke `activation-reviewer` (extraction-faithfulness I2, ┬з4.9) over the **whole proposal set** (coverage is a set property, not per-Directive); on `revise`, refine and re-invoke (two-round backstop as `/file-directive`).
5. **File** тАФ `gh issue create --label directive --label status:proposed` for each proposal (body via `--body-file` so upstream-authored Initiative text is never interpolated into a `gh` argument position тАФ this covers the injection surface; content-trust is handled by the I1/I2 gates + human activation, not by `--body-file`). The extracted Directives are **never activated** тАФ activation stays human/reviewer-gated via `/activate` (generation-open / decision-gated, ┬з5.7). At create time `label-parent-consistency` is not matched (it is scoped to `--add-label`), so the **I2 gate is the effective parent-XOR check** for the create path (it sees the full proposal bodies before filing).

Audit category: `initiative-consume` (decisions: `extracted` with count=N, `under-specified` (contract gate stopped the flow), `revise`). The command never edits/closes/relabels the Initiative (M1.2 `initiative-readonly`); never activates the extracted Directives; never files a proposal without the `Parent Initiative: #N` marker. Escape (reviewer gate): see ┬з7.

### 5.22 `/initiative-feedback <N> {--challenge "<reason>" | --completion}` (Issue #260; Directive #259)

The **upward-feedback** flow (SPEC ┬з1.7 "Feedback is upward and non-deciding") тАФ the execution layer surfaces findings to an Initiative as structured comments, never as strategic decisions. One command, two modes (mirrors `/resolve-discussion`'s two-path shape). Both modes require the `initiative` label on `#N` (else error), operate same-repo, and write **only** a `gh issue comment --body-file` (the sole Initiative write тАФ allowed by `initiative-readonly`; `--body-file` for the injection surface). Each comment leads with a **scannable marker** (`## Initiative challenge` / `## Initiative completion`, modeled on `## AC closeout`) so an upstream consumer could parse it. These markers are projected into the `initiative:challenged` / `initiative:completion-requested` labels by the target-repo `initiative-feedback-label.yml` CI Action (#359, ┬з1.7) тАФ applied by CI, never by eng's runtime, preserving `initiative-readonly`.

- **`--challenge "<reason>"`** тАФ when execution reality contradicts the Initiative (a termination condition that looked measurable but isn't; a real dependency / measurability / implementation cost the planning layer structurally cannot have), post a `## Initiative challenge` comment carrying that **code-derived** information and **requesting re-evaluation**. It **escalates** тАФ it does NOT reject, retire, or close the Initiative (mirrors a reviewer `block` escalating rather than auto-discarding, ┬з4.9.1). The decision stays upstream; the shell does not track what happens next.
- **`--completion`** тАФ when the Directives extracted from the Initiative (`/consume-initiative`, ┬з5.21) have all landed, post a `## Initiative completion` comment carrying the **evidence** (the merged Directives / PRs) and **requesting termination assessment**. It reports the fact and requests assessment; it does NOT assert the termination condition is met and does NOT close the Initiative тАФ asserting completion is a strategic judgment that stays upstream (the same logic that forbids rejection).

Audit category: `initiative-feedback` (decisions: `challenge`, `completion`). The command never edits, closes, reopens, relabels, or retires the Initiative (M1.2 `initiative-readonly` is the runtime backstop); the only write is the structured comment. With ┬з5.22 the milestone-v2 model is **fully live** тАФ recognition (M1.1) + enforcement (M1.2) + reviewer (M2) + consume (M3) + feedback (M4) + derived-view (the mirror's Project `Parent` field for Initiative-parented Directives, #262).

### 5.23 `/changelog` (Issue #346)

The in-flow **authoring affordance** for the ┬з18.1 fragment contract тАФ the local pre-image of the remote CI gate (┬з18.6), closing the "gate enforced but no in-flow authoring surface" gap that produced repeated post-hoc `chore(#N): add changelog fragment` commits (#320, #323, #325, #327, #329, #334; root cause #300). A prompt-driven skill (`.claude/commands/changelog.md`), script-less тАФ the load-bearing work (inferring the Keep-a-Changelog category from the diff, judging skip-eligibility per ┬з18.7) is LLM reasoning. For the current PR/branch it does exactly one of:

- **Write a fragment** тАФ resolve the allow-set (the PR number тИк its `closingIssuesReferences`, computed the same way as `check-changelog.yml` тАФ referenced, never re-derived), infer the category, and write `changelog_unreleased/<category>/<N>.md` as a single-line bullet per ┬з18.1.
- **Apply `skip-changelog`** тАФ when the change is skip-eligible per ┬з18.7, `gh pr edit --add-label skip-changelog`.

`/changelog` is an **authoring** surface, not a `/changelog-check` lint surface (the ┬з18.5 non-goal): it produces the artifact or the label and **delegates all validation to the CI gate (┬з18.6)** тАФ it never re-implements the fragment-shape rules. Mode coupling (┬з5.7.1): `attended` proposes the fragment draft (or a skip) for human confirmation; `unattended` runs the decision automatically (reviewer-substitution model, ┬з1.5). Invoked standalone or by the `/ship` pre-ready arm (┬з5.7, step 7.7) when the gate is unsatisfied.

### 5.24 `/flush` (Issue #387; Directive #385)

The **flush** affordance of the context lifecycle (┬з3.7) тАФ the pre-clear distillation that makes a context clear an `active тЖТ archived` transition rather than `active тЖТ delete`. A prompt-driven skill (`.claude/commands/flush.md`), script-less тАФ the load-bearing work (judging what task-scoped state is worth archiving, curating the PR body) is LLM reasoning. Before the operator clears the working context, `/flush` distills the reconstructable core (branch / issue / PR / phase / next step тАФ the `status_compact` field set) into **at least one durable-memory artifact**:

- **PR body** тАФ curated per the PR-as-living-doc rule (┬з1.4) when a PR exists (the richest target);
- a **`.claude/state/` flush record** тАФ the always-available target (a branch may have no PR yet), carrying the `status_compact` fields.

`/flush` **does not and cannot invoke** Claude Code's native `/clear` (outside the shell boundary, ┬з3.4) тАФ it *precedes* a clear and makes it safe by guaranteeing the archive exists first; the reconstruct half is SessionStart restore (┬з6.5(b)). Trigger is **explicit only** (operator- or skill-invoked); threshold automation is deferred (┬з0.4, ┬з3.7). Mode coupling (┬з5.7.1): `attended` proposes the flush targets for confirmation; `unattended` writes them automatically. Additive тАФ no change to native `/clear`.

### 5.25 `/recall <topic>` (Issue #422)

The **selective-injection** affordance of the context dual (MISSION "The mechanism") тАФ an on-demand query into durable memory's `active тЖТ archived` half. SessionStart restore (┬з6.5(b)) re-injects only the *current* task's artifacts; `/recall` retrieves *prior, unrelated* decisions from the decision record on demand, answering "have we addressed this shape before?" A thin command file (`.claude/commands/recall.md`) delegating to `helpers/recall.sh::recall_pointers`, mirroring the `/status` тЖТ `status.sh` precedent (┬з5.5).

`recall_pointers <topic>` fans out across the decision record's substrates and merges into one **pointers-only** list:
- closed issues тАФ `gh search issues --state closed`;
- merged PRs тАФ `gh search prs --state closed`;
- ADRs тАФ title/H1 match over `docs/ADRs/*.md`.

**Pointers-only is the load-bearing narrowing safeguard** (MISSION; the same fixed-size-pointer discipline ┬з6.5(d) applies to the friction advisory): each result is one line тАФ a tag (`#` / `PR#` / `ADR-NNNN`) + number + the one-line title тАФ **never a body**. The guarantee is *structural*, not advisory: the `gh` arms project `--json number,title`, so a body is never fetched into reach (a later edit adding `body` to the projection is the one regression path тАФ smoke pins against it). The count is **bounded**: a per-substrate cap `RECALL_LIMIT` (default 5, env-overridable; 15-line worst case) so no substrate starves the others and the worst-case context cost is fixed and documented. **Fail-open**: any `gh`/grep error (offline, rate-limited, unauthenticated) yields a single `recall: decision record unavailable` line тАФ never a block, never a partial body dump.

**Two-tier design** (Issue #524). The paragraph above specifies the **light tier**; a **deep tier** extends it for the high-conviction case. The tiers share every safeguard (pointers-only, `RECALL_LIMIT`-bounded, fail-open); they differ only in *what corpus they reach* and *who may trigger them*.

- **Light tier** (today's behavior, UNCHANGED). Best-effort, pointers-only, fail-open, **assistant-auto-triggerable** at recall-shaped moments (before planning / a non-trivial decision). The `gh search` fan-out over closed issues / merged PRs / ADR titles described above. This is the reflex hot path.
- **Deep tier** (new). A **bounded comment-body search**, invoked **ONLY on explicit user intent** тАФ natural-language conviction ("search the comments", "we surely decided this") or an explicit `--deep` flag тАФ and **NEVER by the assistant's internal pre-planning reflex**. Mechanism: the deep tier runs its **own** `gh search` for a **bounded candidate set** (тЙд `RECALL_LIMIT`) that тАФ unlike the light tier тАФ **includes open issues** (a decision under active discussion is exactly the high-conviction case, e.g. an open issue's comment thread), then fetches those candidates' comments (`gh issue view <n> --json comments`) and matches them **locally with a token-aware FIXED-STRING predicate** (`grep -F` on the whole topic, else on any topic token тЙе 3 chars тАФ no regex/tokenizer), so dotted-version tokens like `3.12` that `gh search`'s server-side tokenizer drops are still found. The **candidate search itself is token-aware** (#526): it issues the whole-topic `gh search` first and, only if that returns **zero candidates** тАФ GitHub free-text applies **AND** semantics, so a multi-token natural-language phrase whose tokens do not co-occur in any single issue's title/body finds nothing тАФ **falls back** to re-querying per high-signal token (тЙе 3 chars, the *same* tokenizer the local predicate uses), merging and deduping the hits under the same `RECALL_LIMIT` bound. This makes stage 1 (the candidate gate) **symmetric** with the OR-tolerant local predicate it feeds rather than strictly narrower: without it, the local predicate's token-tolerance is unreachable for exactly the discursive queries the deep tier exists to serve, since a candidate never fetched is never matched. The fallback fires only on the 0-candidate path and only under `--deep`, and each per-token query is fail-open (a `gh` error degrades to the light-tier result, never errors, never partial-dumps a body).
