It emits **only the pointers the light tier did not already print** (deduped against the light output), so a comment match on an already-surfaced closed issue never double-prints and the deep tier's contribution is the genuinely *new* pointers (chiefly open-issue comment decisions the closed-only light tier cannot reach). **Pointers-only is preserved structurally**: the local grep is a **predicate** (match / no-match) тАФ the emitted output is only the `#<n> title` pointer, and the matched comment text is **never emitted**.

**Trigger asymmetry.** The light tier is **reflex-triggerable** by the assistant; the deep tier is **explicit-user-intent-only**. The routing contract itself is carried by the skill `description:` string on `.claude/commands/recall.md` (Claude Code matches natural-language intent against it тАФ light-recall intent to the reflex path, comment-conviction intent to the deep path) plus the CLAUDE.md recall-routing norm. The rationale is the **cost-of-miss asymmetry** (┬з6.0): the reflex is a **low-prior + cheap-miss** situation (light tier, fail-open, a wrong *allow* costs nothing тАФ so it earns auto-trigger), whereas user conviction is a **high-prior + expensive-miss** situation (deep tier justified тАФ but explicit-intent-only, so the comment fetch never spends context on the reflex hot path).

Out of scope / residual (Issues #422, #524):
- a vector/embedding store (the v0 substrate is `gh search` + `git grep` + the bounded comment fetch); changing ┬з6.5(b) injection; auto-running `/recall` without an explicit invocation (the `/work-on` pre-planning step is a deferred follow-up).
- **Deep tier is matched-issues-only.** It surfaces a comment-borne decision **when the topic reaches the candidate set** тАФ i.e. the parent issue is found via the deep tier's own (open + closed) `gh search` hit (whole-topic first, else the per-token fallback above), then one of those candidates' comments carries the token-aware fixed-string match. Two cases must be distinguished:
  - **Multi-token natural-language phrase whose tokens *do* reach candidates individually** тАФ e.g. `"ьЪ┤ьШБ ьЭ╕эД░эФДыжмэД░ 3.12 vs 3.14"`, where `ьЭ╕эД░эФДыжмэД░` / `3.14` each appear in some issue's title/body but the AND-joined whole phrase matches none. This was a **stage-1/stage-2 asymmetry bug** (the whole-topic candidate search returned 0 and the OR-tolerant local predicate never ran) and is **fixed** by the per-token candidate fallback (#526): each high-signal token re-queries the candidate set, so the parent issue is reached and its comment matched.
  - **No-shared-token residual (accepted, v0).** A decision recorded in a comment on an issue whose **title and body share no token with the query** тАФ the token-tolerant candidate fallback still finds nothing, because *no* token reaches any candidate. Closing this fully requires the semantic / full-corpus search that is out of scope, and leaving it open is consistent with ┬з5.25's fail-open / bounded / best-effort ethos. A bare dotted query like `3.12` is the limiting sub-case: it is a single тЙе3-char token, so the fallback *does* re-query it, but `gh search`'s server-side tokenizer drops the dotted form, so it still yields zero candidates unless a co-occurring token (e.g. `python`) brings the parent issue into the set.

**Routing disposition** (positive enforcement, ┬з6.0) тАФ distinct from, and *not* a reversal of, the deferred forced auto-run just above. The agent **reaches for `/recall` at recall-shaped moments**: both **user-asked** ("have we addressed X before?", "what did we decide about Y?") and **self-identified** тАФ an internal "have we decided this shape before?" beat before planning or a non-trivial decision. This is a **judgment-based** nudge laid generously, not a gate: a missed recall is recoverable (the wrong *allow* costs nothing), which is exactly why it earns the positive face тАФ whereas a *forced* injection on every phase has the opposite cost-asymmetry (a wrong forced inject spends context that cannot be un-spent) and so **stays deferred**. The disposition above is the **light tier**; the **deep** comment sweep is deliberately outside it тАФ reachable by explicit user intent only, never the pre-planning reflex тАФ **with one bounded escalation** (#528): when a light `/recall` the assistant ran *for a user-asked substantive / answer-seeking question* returns **no matches (empty)**, the assistant **escalates once** to `--deep` as a single follow-up sweep, without the user having to type `--deep` or "search the comments". This is **not a reversal** of "explicit-user-intent-only" but a refinement that stays inside the cost-of-miss asymmetry (┬з6.0; "Trigger asymmetry" above): deep fires **only after the cheap tier has already missed**, and **only on the high-conviction user-asked branch** тАФ the **self-identified pre-planning** beat still **never auto-escalates** (that would be the forbidden deep-as-reflex, and the wrong-forced-inject cost that keeps it deferred). An empty light result on a substantive user ask is itself the high-prior signal the deep tier was built for, so paying its cost there is the *cheap-miss-already-realized* case, not a speculative spend. The lever is the trigger-oriented `description:` frontmatter of `.claude/commands/recall.md` (Claude Code matches natural-language recall intent to the skill on it) plus the CLAUDE.md recall-routing norm. The disposition never fetches a body тАФ the pointers-only safeguard holds (both tiers) тАФ and following a pointer is a separate targeted read, only if relevant.

### 5.26 `/replan-check` (Issue #427)

The **in-loop correction** of the selective-injection half тАФ a checkpoint that keeps the Plan (a task-scoped injection manifest, MISSION "The mechanism") reflecting truth as execution proceeds. `planner` is one-shot (then `plan-reviewer`); without this, a Plan the actual diff has outgrown silently stops being a faithful manifest, eroding PR-as-living-doc (┬з1.4). A thin command (`.claude/commands/replan-check.md`) delegating mechanical fact-gathering to `helpers/replan_check.sh`, with the divergence **judgment** kept in the skill (LLM) тАФ the `/recall`тЖТ`recall.sh` split.

`replan_check.sh` surfaces only the mechanical facts, fail-open: the actually-touched files (`git diff --name-only <base>...HEAD`, `<base>` from `gh pr view --json baseRefName`, default `main`), the linked issue's AC checkboxes, and the PR-body `## Plan` / `## Checklist` / `## Key context` / `## Out of scope` (a touched file the Plan declared out-of-scope is a strong structural signal). The skill then applies the **structural-vs-cosmetic discriminator**:

- **Structural тЖТ re-invoke `planner`** (mirroring `/work-on` step 6; in `unattended`, a clean `plan-reviewer` re-substitutes for approval): EITHER (a) the diff touches a **load-bearing** file/area the Plan/Checklist/Key-context never anticipated (a new module, a schema/contract surface, an un-named subsystem) тАФ *not* a mechanical incidental; OR (b) an **AC is rendered unreachable** тАФ the approach taken closes off a path a linked-issue acceptance criterion required.
- **Cosmetic тЖТ no trigger** (a one-line advisory at most): files that are the **direct mechanical consequence** of a planned change (a regenerated TOC, a changelog fragment, the SSOT-coupling the Plan already implies тАФ e.g. the ┬з8 tree bump for a planned helper), in-scope reordering/renaming, or any change leaving every AC reachable.

The threshold is **asymmetric by design** (┬з6.0): re-invoking `planner` is expensive and the judgment is fallible, so it **fails toward not-triggering** тАФ when in doubt, emit the advisory, do not re-plan. This is **positive enforcement** (a guiding checkpoint), not a hard gate; a missed nudge is recoverable, a wrong forced re-plan is not. `/sync-pr` (┬з5.4) references it as a post-sync advisory step (the body was just curated тАФ the natural cadence to compare it against the diff); `/ship` inherits the reference transitively (┬з5.7 step 5). Trigger is explicit/invoked тАФ the auto-on-every-phase-commit variant is deferred (parallel to ┬з5.25's auto-`/recall` deferral).

### 5.27 `/reconcile-spec` (Issue #464; Directive #455)

The **judgment + action** half of code-vs-SPEC drift reconciliation тАФ the consumer of the measure-first detector `scripts/spec_drift_candidates.sh` (┬з6.5(d), #462). The detector surfaces code-ahead drift *candidates*; `/reconcile-spec` reads the relevant SPEC section(s) and the drifted commits/code and classifies each candidate into **exactly one of three dispositions, before any SPEC edit**:

- **spec-ahead** тАФ SPEC leads, the code is still being implemented тЖТ **track, no edit**.
- **code-ahead-correct** тАФ the code is right and SPEC is stale тЖТ **propose a SPEC update to match the code**, applied **only after explicit user approval**.
- **code-wrong** тАФ the code is a bug and SPEC is right тЖТ **never edit SPEC**; route to a code fix / file a bug.

**The load-bearing invariant (Directive #455): the shell never silently rewrites SPEC to match possibly-buggy code.** Disposition `code-wrong` *never* edits SPEC, and `code-ahead-correct` edits it *only* after explicit user approval тАФ the correction is human judgment, never the shell's autonomous act. **Operating mode**: in `attended` the command surfaces the classification + proposed edit and pauses for approval before applying; in `unattended` it **never auto-applies** a SPEC correction (a SPEC-to-match-code edit is a content/direction change, and the directing layer never autonomously sets direction тАФ ┬з1.7) тАФ it surfaces/parks the candidate instead. Classification *correctness* is agent judgment (mirroring `/onboard`'s SSOT-drafting half), not a mechanically-verified property.

Each handled candidate is audit-logged under the **`spec-reconcile`** category with its decision: `applied` (a `code-ahead-correct` SPEC edit, after approval), `tracked` (`spec-ahead`), `routed` (`code-wrong` тЖТ code fix / bug), or `parked` (surfaced in `unattended`, not applied). Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/reconcile-spec.md`. Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=<cat> SKIP_REASON='<why>'` per ┬з7.

### 5.28 `/implement` (Issue #486; Directive #477)

The **default Code-phase author** тАФ runs Phase C (Code) in the write-capable `implementer` subagent (┬з4.12) instead of the main loop, so the within-Execution authoring churn (file reads, abandoned approaches, lint/smoke iterations) stays out of the main assistant's context. `/implement <issue#>` is the action-form of the ┬з1.2 / ┬з3.7 discard-boundary-at-Execution principle.

**Default-with-opt-out invariant (Directive #477 signal-4).** The Code phase routes here **by default** тАФ `/work-on` step "Phase C" dispatches `/implement`. The **opt-out** is for trivial / one-line / glue edits and the orchestrator's own glue (Directive #477 Non-goal 2), which the main assistant authors directly. The default-flip descopes the original A/B measurement gate: the context-narrowing hypothesis is adopted as operating policy on circumstantial evidence (the convergent mainstream pattern + the native subagent context-discard), hedged by **fail-open reversibility** тАФ a missing implementer path degrades to main-loop authoring and the documented opt-out makes the default revertible тАФ rather than by a measured non-worse result. Auto-routing lives in the `/work-on` doc procedure only, **never** in a Stop / PostToolUse hook.

**Manifest contract (input the command assembles).** The subagent has no access to the conversation, so the command gathers the explicit manifest first: the **Plan** (PR-body `## Plan` / `## Checklist`, the planner output ┬з4.1), the **failing Phase-B test** + the exact command to run it, and the **named relevant file paths** (PR-body `## Key context`). A missing Plan or failing test means the manifest is incomplete тАФ finish Phase A/B first. Before spawning, the command also **surfaces/warns on a dirty working tree** (`git status`): a clean tree is expected once the Phase-A Doc and Phase-B Test commits have landed, so a dirty tree signals uncommitted glue the implementer's path-scoped add (┬з4.12) must not sweep in. This is a **surface/warn, not a hard block** тАФ a legitimately dirty tree must not stall the flow, and the fail-open posture is unchanged.

**Structured-return contract (output the command absorbs).** Spawn `subagent_type: implementer` on the manifest; absorb **only** its structured return тАФ (a) commit/diff ref(s), (b) plan-deviations, (c) discoveries тАФ never the working churn. A **structural** plan-deviation (out-of-plan load-bearing file, an AC rendered unreachable) follows the `/replan-check` discriminator (┬з5.26): re-invoke `planner`, then `/sync-pr`; a cosmetic deviation needs at most a one-line advisory.

**┬з4.9.3 session-restart caveat.** A freshly-added `subagent_type: implementer` falls back to `general-purpose` until the next session restart; `implementer.md`'s self-describing prompt makes the fallback functionally complete (only the Type-aware tool restriction is lost), restart is canonical. The implementer authors its commit in the **work language** (┬з5.7.2). Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/implement.md`.

### 5.29 `/file-review <pr>` (Issue #585; Directive #584)

The **verdict-materializer** тАФ runs `code-reviewer` (┬з4.5) on a PR and posts its verdict as a **first-class GitHub review**, `commit_id`-pinned to the reviewed head. `/file-review <pr>` is a **general capability** (any PR, any time) *and* the **producer** the #586 merge-review gate will consume. It is **producer-only**: it adds/changes/removes **no** merge gate. The gate + `review-gate` state (#586) and the `permissions.allow` entry + ┬з5.7.1 clause + `/ship` integration (#587) are explicitly **out of scope** here.

**Ownership branching (GitHub self-review constraint).** Resolve the acting identity (`gh api user --jq .login`) and the PR author (`gh pr view <pr> --json author --jq .author.login`). On **another author's PR** (author тЙа authed user) the review is posted as a **native review** тАФ `APPROVE` / `REQUEST_CHANGES`. On the **authed user's own PR** GitHub 422s a self `APPROVE`/`REQUEST_CHANGES`, so the review is posted as a **`COMMENT`** review carrying the machine-readable marker (below).

**Verdict тЖТ review-type map** (over `code-reviewer`'s `ship` / `ship after fix` / `block` grammar, ┬з4.5):

| code-reviewer verdict | others' PR | own PR |
|---|---|---|
| `ship` | `APPROVE` | `COMMENT` (marker `verdict=approve`) |
| `ship after fix` / `block` | `REQUEST_CHANGES` | `COMMENT` (marker `verdict=block`) |
| unconfirmed / unresolvable head | **post nothing** тАФ audit `invalid`, abort | **post nothing** тАФ audit `invalid`, abort |

The **unconfirmed-head arm fails closed to silence, not to a block**: if the reviewer's `reviewed-head:` (┬з4.5) cannot be blind-compared equal to the private PR head, `/file-review` posts **nothing** and audits `invalid` тАФ it never posts a `block` / `REQUEST_CHANGES` on a head it could not confirm (an unearned negative verdict on an unknown artifact).

**`commit_id`-pinned submission via REST тАФ not `gh pr review`.** The review is submitted with the head SHA bound as `commit_id`:

```
gh api repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/<n>/reviews \
  -f commit_id="$HEAD_SHA" \
  -f event=<APPROVE|REQUEST_CHANGES|COMMENT> \
  --field body=@<tempfile>
```

`gh pr review` is **deliberately not used**: it cannot pin a `commit_id`, so a push concurrent with the review would rebind an `APPROVE` to an unreviewed head тАФ the exact ┬з4.5 head-pin failure. Binding `commit_id` to the independently-confirmed head means a racing push leaves the review pinned to a now-stale commit (which #586 then correctly reads as not-current), closing the false-approve race. The **body is passed via a written, sanitized temp file** (`--field body=@<file>`), **never** an inline `--body`, with **whole-body `@mention` neutralization** тАФ the same idiom as `activate.md` / `reflect.md`. `<pr>` is **validated** (`^[0-9]+$` or a trusted `github.com/<owner>/<repo>/pull/<n>` URL) before use. **Repo-scope guard:** the PR must target the **origin** repo (`gh repo view --json nameWithOwner`); a cross-repo target is **confirmed in `attended`** and **refused (fail-closed) in `unattended`**.

**Own-PR / current-branch submission routes through the wrapper (#598).** When the reviewed PR is the acting identity's own PR **and** is the current branch's PR тАФ the `/ship` self-merge case, where the raw `gh api тАж/reviews` POST is blocked by the auto-mode classifier as self-approval (┬з5.7.1) тАФ the `COMMENT` submission is issued via the fixed-form wrapper `.claude/ghjig-root/scripts/ghjig_file_review_post.sh` instead of a direct `gh api` call. The sanitized body is **not** fed on stdin (stdin cannot be supplied to a bare covered command in the Claude Code harness); it is staged **out-of-band** to a fixed path resolved via `ghjig_state_dir_cli()` by a separate writer `scripts/ghjig_file_review_stage.sh`, and the wrapper reads it under a **60s TTL + one-shot unlink**, failing closed on an empty / absent / stale / malformed body (тЖТ no post). The wrapper is invoked **bare** (no argv, no pipe, no redirect), so it is the single `permissions.allow`-covered surface that lets an unattended `/ship` post its own head-pinned review (┬з5.7.1); it resolves the current-branch PR + head itself, **fails closed unless acting identity == PR author**, and hardcodes `event=COMMENT` (never `APPROVE`/`REQUEST_CHANGES`). The general path is **unchanged** тАФ another author's PR (native `APPROVE`/`REQUEST_CHANGES`), or a manual self-review of a **non-current** PR, keeps the direct `gh api` REST call above; only the classifier-blocked own-current-PR `COMMENT` reroutes. Whether the produced self-review is then *honored* by the merge gate is governed by the per-target `resolve_self_review_policy` (┬з5.7.1, #598), not by `/file-review`, which remains **producer-only**.

**Marker contract** (own-PR `COMMENT` review **body only** тАФ never the PR body or a PR comment). The exact token:

```
<!-- file-review verdict=<approve|block> head=<HEAD_SHA> reviewer=code-reviewer -->
```

is emitted **only inside the `COMMENT` review object**, so #586 can bind the marker to the GitHub-attested review author. **#586's authoritative fields are the review OBJECT's, not the marker text:** #586 sources `commit_id` (the current-head check) and `author.login` (the author == merger check) from the attested review object; only **`verdict`** is read from the marker text, because GitHub's `COMMENTED` state cannot itself encode approve-vs-block. The marker's `head=` is **redundant human/grep convenience** that must equal the review's `commit_id`; `reviewer=code-reviewer` records the engine. `verdict=approve` derives **only** from a real `code-reviewer` `ship` and is **never hand-written**.

**Audit.** Category **`file-review`** (event-info; free-form reason text, **not** under `_audit_validate_format`'s strict arms). Decisions: `posted` / `invalid` / `aborted`. Reason shape: `pr=#<N> verdict=<approve|block> commit_id=<sha> ownership=<self|other> event=<APPROVE|REQUEST_CHANGES|COMMENT>`.

Full procedure lives in `.claude/commands/file-review.md`.

---

## 6. Hook enforcement

### 6.0 Enforcement style

The action-axis principle of MISSION "The mechanism" тАФ enforcement has a *negative* face (block a wrong action) and a *positive* face (supply the right next one), and both are necessary тАФ lands here as the design rule for every matcher, command, and reviewer the shell adds. The ┬з6.1 **Framing** paragraph below states the negative side's posture (a mistake-prevention guardrail, not a sandbox); this section is the cross-cutting rule that decides, for any given discipline, *which* face to give it and *where* to put it. Of the rules below, **P1, P3, and P4 derive from** that MISSION principle; **P2 is SPEC-local** тАФ an engineering-physics rule about *where* a given enforcement runs (local hook vs remote backstop), with no MISSION parent.

**P1 тАФ Cost-asymmetry selects the face (the criterion).** Choose negative vs positive by the cost of being *wrong*, not by how important the rule feels. Where a wrong *allow* is irreversible or corrupts shared history тАФ a force-push onto a protected branch, a leaked secret, a destructive `rm` тАФ the rule is a hard negative gate that **fails safe toward blocking**; the force-push matcher (┬з6.1) reasons exactly this way (a wrong allow clobbers shared protected history тАФ irreversible; a wrong block costs naming the branch тАФ recoverable). Where a wrong *nudge* is simply ignored at no cost тАФ a `next:` hint, a scaffolding command тАФ the rule is positive and is laid generously. Corollary: **negative gates are narrow and precise, positive guidance is broad and abundant**, because the two failure costs are asymmetric (the type-aware carve-outs of ┬з6.1 are negative gates being made *more precise* to avoid false blocks, not weaker).

**P2 тАФ Enforcement physics: pick the layer for the bypass model.** A local PreToolUse hook fires pre-action but is **bypassable** (eval, `bash -c`, dynamic construction тАФ see ┬з6.1 Framing); a remote gate (CI, branch protection) fires later but is **unbypassable** and runs regardless of who acts. An irreversible rule therefore cannot rely on the local hook alone тАФ it needs a remote backstop, with the local hook as its **pre-image** (the in-flow, fast-feedback copy of the remote check; e.g. the local changelog presence check is the pre-image of the `check-changelog` CI gate, ┬з18). Reversible / hygiene rules can live at the local layer only.

**P3 тАФ The face is not fixed; it migrates with trust.** A rule is typically born **advisory** (a reviewer or skill recommendation), **hardened** into a hook once the pattern proves out (e.g. #199 promoted the advisory #197 labelтЖФparent layer into the `label-parent-consistency` matcher тАФ ┬з6.1), and **narrowed** again if it starts fighting the prescribed flow (the force-push matcher was relaxed from a blanket block to allow the named-branch force-push of the ┬з13 rebase-pull tail). This migration is the action-axis form of "the shell improves under use" (MISSION). The two directions were historically **not equally observable**: narrowing pressure shows in the audit log (escape clustering on one category/reason тАФ ┬з7; the MISSION success signal "the escape hatch stays narrow"), surfaced by `scripts/narrowing_candidates.sh`. Promotion pressure once left no audit trace тАФ an ignored advisory was invisible тАФ but the reviewer-reject reason-class trail (#361) now records each non-pass reviewer verdict (issue-/plan-/activation-reviewer) with a categorized token, and `scripts/promotion_candidates.sh` aggregates those into advisoryтЖТhook promotion candidates above a threshold. Both directions are thus observable; the narrow/promote decision still stays human / reviewer judgment (the consumers **surface** candidates, they do not act тАФ tracking #41 principle #3). **The audit log is a *dual-positive* channel (Directive #356):** a block's in-band message is its immediate positive face (it names the alternative, P4), and the line it appends to `audit.jsonl` is a *deferred* positive face тАФ but that line is only **latently** positive: it becomes an actionable positive channel solely once a consumer is wired to read the aggregate (the two scripts above). An unconsumed log is an inert record, not a positive channel; wiring the consumer is what completes the deferred positive face. **That consumer is now wired (#398, Directive #391):** the SessionStart ┬з6.5(d) friction advisory triggers the two readers (plus the `unattended-park` park-frequency signal bridged in by ┬з5.7.1) once per session, TTL-gated and fail-open, surfacing accumulated friction as a one-line pointer without a human remembering to run a script тАФ so the deferred positive face is no longer latent. A third reader, `scripts/ceremony_candidates.sh` (#401), extends the same surface to **ceremony** mis-sizing тАФ mined from commit history rather than `audit.jsonl` (the ceremony signal is not recorded there) тАФ and is itself **born advisory**: it observes whether ceremony mis-sizing recurs *before* any ┬з1.2 weight model or relaxation gate is hardened against it, the P3 order applied to the device's own roadmap. The narrow/promote decision still stays human / reviewer judgment (the advisory **surfaces**, it does not act тАФ tracking #41 principle #3).

**P4 тАФ Pair the faces; never ship a bare gate.** A negative gate names its positive alternative in the block message (a `status:proposed` branch attempt is blocked with "run `/activate <N>`"; a bare force-push is blocked with "name the target branch") тАФ a block that only says "no" is half a rule. Defaults reinforce the pairing: enforcement **fails open** (a missing helper warns and proceeds, never locks the developer out тАФ see the ┬з6.1 fail-policy table) and the **escape hatch is always open but audited** (┬з7). A reviewer is the paired form inside one agent тАФ it produces an artifact (positive) and gates on a verdict (negative), a *generative gate* (┬з1.5). Evaluate any enforcement proposal against this: a hard block with no named alternative, or guidance with no gate behind it, is the one-sided regression MISSION warns of.

**Reviewer invariant-preservation gate (a P1 application, Directive #567).** A reviewer that substitutes for human review in `unattended` mode (`plan-reviewer` ┬з4.8, `activation-reviewer` ┬з4.9) is itself a load-bearing gate, so P1's cost-asymmetry test applies to *its own verdict*: a wrong *allow* that ships a plan / activates a Directive silently **deferring, weakening, or measurement-gating a definitional/mandatory invariant** is high-asymmetry and irreversible (the guarantee is gone from the shipped artifact), whereas a wrong *block* costs one revision round (recoverable). By P1 that warrants a **hard negative pass/fail gate sequenced *ahead of* the soft axis contest** (plan-reviewer) / evidence judgment (activation-reviewer) тАФ a mandatory invariant is not a trade-off to be weighed inside the contest, so an axis win (simplicity / cost / effort) bought by dropping one does not dominate; the candidate is **disqualified regardless of axis score**. The manifest of mandatory invariants is **derived at dispatch from existing SSOT** (issue AC / MISSION / ADRs / the affected-component contract тАФ ┬з4.8.1), never invented by the reviewer (which would be the reviewer manufacturing requirements тАФ an authority overreach). **The empty-manifest case is P1's mirror hazard, resolved by affirmative attestation, not a hard block:** the reviewer must *state the invariant set it checked against* (including "none declared"), because hard-blocking a plan whose manifest is empty would be **over-enforcement of a mere visibility concern** тАФ a one-sided regression, a bare gate laid on a no-cost nudge (the P4 anti-pattern) тАФ while a silent no-op would **under-enforce** and reproduce the motivating incident (a deferred definitional guarantee accepted as a soft trade-off). Attestation is the paired-face resolution: it makes the check visible (positive) and gates only on a *positively-declared* dropped invariant (negative). This is a contract shape, not a token change тАФ the verdict sets are unchanged (`ship`/`refine`/`block`; `pass`/`revise`/`reject`) and no new subagent role is added. The full gate + guard contract is the reviewer-prompt SSOTs (`.claude/agents/plan-reviewer.md`, `.claude/agents/activation-reviewer.md`); ┬з4.8/┬з4.9 reference them (┬з9). **Sibling P1 application (Directive #570 / #571):** the same cost-asymmetry governs the judge's *dismissal of a challenger* тАФ a wrong `A-stands` that buries a real large weakness (even one outside the declared invariant manifest) by *outweighing* it with A-advocacy is the same irreversible wrong-allow, so `plan-reviewer` carries a **dismissal evidence-burden** guard (refute, don't outweigh; scaled to the challenger's claimed magnitude; ┬з4.8), likewise held in the reviewer-prompt SSOT and not restated here (┬з9).

### 6.1 PreToolUse тАФ block

**Framing**: Hooks are a **mistake-prevention guardrail**, not a security boundary. An adversarial user can bypass them via shell features the matcher doesn't model (`eval`, `bash -c`, `python -c`, heredoc-spawned shells, dynamic command construction via parameter expansion). The hook's job is to stop honest mistakes тАФ typos, autopilot moments, the wrong tab тАФ not to be a sandbox. Patterns that suggest a bypass attempt are not blocked but are **audit-logged as warnings** so the trail is preserved for review.

Implementation note: command strings are **normalized** before matching тАФ backslash-continued multiline (`\\\n`) collapses to single-space, internal newlines become spaces, multi-space whitespace collapses. So `git \\\n  push \\\n  --force-with-lease` matches the same blocked pattern as the single-line form. Normalization also **re-separates a glued unquoted command separator** (`&&`, `||`, `;`, `|`, and a lone background `&`) into a space-padded segment boundary, so an operator glued to an adjacent token тАФ `git commit -m "x"&&git push --force origin main`, no space before `&&` тАФ does not get folded into a single token by the `parse_env_prefix` shlex round-trip and dissolve the following `git push` verb (the entry-grep keys on `git push`, so a destroyed verb is a **false-negative** on the force-push/protected gate тАФ ┬з6.0 P1, #446). Only separators **outside** quoted string values are split: a `&&`/`;`/`|`/`&` *inside* a quoted `-m`/`--message` value is data, not a boundary, and is never re-separated (no invented boundary тАФ composes with the #440 message-value elision). A lone `&` that is part of a **redirect** (`>&`, `&>`, `N>&M`, `<&`, `&>>` тАФ i.e. immediately adjacent to `>` or `<`) is a redirect operator, not a background separator, and is **never** re-separated, so a legitimate `git push --force origin feature 2>&1` is not over-blocked (#476). `push_segments` splits on the same set (incl. `&`), so a glued `&` cannot collapse a sibling clause's protected-looking token into the `git push` segment (#437 sibling-isolation parity). The glued and spaced forms of every separator are therefore treated identically by every downstream git matcher.

**Git option-prefix tolerance**: every `git <subcommand>` matcher accepts standard git-level options between `git` and the subcommand: `-c <key>=<value>`, `-C <path>`, `--git-dir=<path>`, `--work-tree=<path>`, `--no-pager`, `--literal-pathspecs`, `--exec-path[=<path>]`, `--namespace=<ref>`. So `git -c commit.gpgsign=false commit -m "тАж"` and `git -C /some/repo push --force` both fire the same downstream checks as the bare `git commit` / `git push` forms тАФ the option prefix can no longer be used (intentionally or not) to slip past the matcher.

**Type-awareness** (introduced alongside dir-mode, ┬з1.7; matchers wired by tracking #41 child #5, issue #46): the engineering-flow matchers below тАФ branch-from-issue, AC-closeout, PR-link / `Closes #N` checks, default `gh issue list` wrappers тАФ **do not apply their engineering-flow gate to a `Type=Directive` Issue**. Directive Issues are gated by `/complete-directive` + `activation-reviewer` (┬з4.9), not by AC checkboxes or `Closes #N` semantics. (For **AC-closeout** specifically the carve-out is **all-or-nothing**, not per-item: the `gh pr merge` gate is skipped only when **every** closing Issue is a Directive тАФ a mixed PR closing both a Directive and an Execution Issue still gates on the Execution Issue's unchecked AC; see the AC-closeout matcher row below.) The `proposed-protect` matcher in the table is the inverse: it actively blocks engineering-flow actions (most prominently `/work-on`) when the target Issue is **either** `status:proposed` (any type тАФ not-yet-activated work, generalized by #171) **or** a Directive (any status тАФ Directives never branch, ┬з10.5). The two conditions guard distinct invariants (lifecycle vs type) that share one branch-creation trigger; `proposed-protect` subsumes the former `directive-protect` rather than replacing it (a status-only check would let an Active Directive become branchable тАФ a ┬з10.5 regression). The implementation predicates (`is_directive_issue <issue-#>`, cached; and `is_proposed_issue <issue-#>`, uncached because the `status:proposed` label is volatile under `/activate`) and the `safe_source` fail-policy entry live in `helpers/issue_type.sh` (#46, #171).

| Trigger | Check | Escape category |
|---------|-------|----------------|
| `git commit` pattern | If on a protected branch (`main`/`master`/`release/*`), block. Detached HEAD on the tip commit of any protected branch is treated the same тАФ the matcher resolves `HEAD` against `refs/heads/{main,master}` and `refs/heads/release/*` and blocks when they share a SHA. **Case-insensitive name match (#555 A7):** the branch-*name* test (`is_protected_branch`) matches `main`/`master`/`release/*` case-insensitively, parity with the force-push arm's `grep -qiE` тАФ so a `Main`/`MASTER` checkout on a case-insensitive filesystem (which resolves to the same ref) is recognized as protected rather than silently slipping past the commit/edit gates. | `branch` |
| `git commit -m "..."` | Conventional Commits format. Issue # required per type (┬з6.1.1) | `commit-format` |
| `git commit` | Secret scan over staged diff. On hit, emits `<file>:<line>: <pattern-id>` per location (no body content) plus the legacy summary line. Honors `.shellsecretignore` at the target repo root: gitignore-narrow (glob, prefix-match for trailing `/`; no negation, no `**`). The default file at the shell-repo root lists component-aware test/example globs (`tests/`, `test/`, `*_test.*`, `*.test.*`, `*-test.*`, `*test_*.*`, `examples/`, `example/`, `*-example.*`, `*_example.*`, `*.example.*`), plus `docs/` and `*.md` тАФ the file is the authoritative set. `.shellsecretignore` is the SPEC ┬з7 tuning mechanism for path-based false positives тАФ repeated `SKIP_HOOKS=secret` escapes on fixture paths mean an allow-list entry is needed, not a normalized bypass. | `secret` |
| `git commit` | Quick lint/format check, bounded by `GHJIG_LINT_TIMEOUT` (default 30 s; "quick" enforced) | `format` |
| `git commit --allow-empty` | **No carve-out** тАФ an empty commit goes through the same four gates as any commit (branch + commit-format + secret + lint). An empty commit is still a protected-branch write and still carries a subject; the secret and lint checks are harmless no-ops on an empty staged set. (Closed the `--allow-empty` matcher-entry bypass, #209.) | `branch`/`commit-format`/`secret`/`format` |
| `git commit --amend` | **Block only when the commit is already on upstream.** Local amend allowed | `amend` |
| `git commit --no-verify` | Block | `no-verify` |
| `git push` with a force variant (`--force`/`-f`/`--force-with-lease`) | **Allowed only to an explicitly-named non-protected branch** (`git push --force-with-lease origin <branch>`) тАФ the normal tail of the rebase-pull motion when the base advances (┬з13), so blanket-blocking it fought the prescribed flow. **Blocked** in two cases: (a) a **protected** branch (`main`/`master`/`release/*`) named in the force-bearing `git push` **segment** (block message names "protected"); (b) a **bare or remote-only** force-push with **no explicit target branch** тАФ the block message instructs the user to name the target (`git push --force-with-lease origin <branch>`). **Segment isolation (#437):** like the protected-push (`branch`) arm (#366), the force-push arm now heredoc-strips the command and isolates the actual `git push` segment(s) via `push_segments`, then re-confirms the force flag, the protected token, the `--mirror/--all/--branches` refset, and the explicit-target positional count **per force-bearing push segment** тАФ so a force flag, protected token, or target named in a **sibling non-push segment** (`git push --force-with-lease origin <feat> && gh pr create --base main`) or a **heredoc body** no longer false-trips the gate. If the force flag turns out to live only in a non-push sibling, the command is not a force-push and is allowed. **Multi-push-segment:** blocks if **any** force-bearing push segment is protected/refset/bare (fail-safe). **Heredoc-only strip** (not quote-stripping) preserves zero false-negatives on a genuine quoted protected force-push, and a strip failure / missing `python3` returns the command unstripped (segmentation only ever drops non-push segments) тАФ so a real protected force-push always still matches. **Message-value strip (#440):** the arm uses `strip_command_data`'s `message` mode тАФ it additionally elides the *argument values* of `-m`/`--message`/`-F`/`--file` (commit-message data, in `=`-glued/quoted/bareword form) before segmenting, so a force/protected literal documented inside a commit **message body** (`git commit -m "тАж git push --force тАж main тАж"`) is treated as data, not a command, and no longer false-trips. The elision is anchored strictly to the message-flag token, so a quoted push **target** (`origin "main"` тАФ no preceding message-flag) is never removed; an unclosed message quote fails closed to unstripped (today's recoverable false-trip, never an over-strip that drops a genuine target). **Why the bare form is blocked rather than HEAD-resolved (fail-safe on ambiguity):** a no-refspec push's real destination is config-dependent (`push.default`, the branch's configured upstream, `remote.*.push` refspecs), so the current branch *name* is not a reliable proxy for what gets written тАФ a feature branch whose upstream is `origin/main` would otherwise let a bare force-push clobber `main`. The hook cannot verify a bare push's true target, so it fails safe to block and tells the user to make the target explicit. **"Verified target" definition:** a push with an explicit positional refspec тАФ `origin <branch>`, `origin HEAD`, or `origin HEAD:<ref>` тАФ counts as a named target (the positional-argument count sees it) and is allowed when non-protected; only a **no-positional** bare/remote-only form (`git push --force`, `git push --force origin`) is blocked. `HEAD` is accepted as explicit-named even though its *remote* destination is, like a bare push, config-dependent тАФ the asymmetry is a deliberate choice: a user who typed `origin HEAD` has named the source ref explicitly (the common rebase-pull-tail form, ┬з13), whereas a no-positional push has named nothing, so only the latter is treated as unverifiable. Cost asymmetry justifies it: a wrong allow clobbers shared protected history (irreversible); a wrong block costs naming the branch or one audited `SKIP_HOOKS=force-push` escape (recoverable). **Bundled short-force detection (#555 A4):** the force-flag test (both the entry pre-filter and the per-segment re-confirm) recognizes a **bundled short cluster** тАФ `git push -uf` / `-fu` тАФ via a token-start-anchored `(^|space)-[A-Za-z]*f[A-Za-z]*` pattern, not only an isolated `-f`; pre-fix a bundled `-uf` carried no `-f\b` token so a **bare bundled force-push** slipped past the fail-safe entirely. The token-start anchor keeps a branch **name** containing `-f` (`my-feature`) from being misread as a force flag (no over-block). | `force-push` |
| `git push origin main`, etc. | Direct push to a protected branch blocked. **Push-target resolution (#366):** detection scans the **`git push` command segment(s)** for a protected token, not a resolved destination. The command is first **heredoc-stripped** тАФ heredoc bodies removed via the shared `strip_command_data` helper (`heredoc` mode; factored from #340's `is_pr_merge_command`) тАФ then **split on unquoted `&&`/`;`/`\|`/newline**, keeping only segments that contain a `git push` token; the protected-token grep runs per push segment. So a protected token that appears only inside a **heredoc body** (`cat <<EOF тАж git push тАж main тАж EOF`) or in a **sibling non-push segment** (`git push origin <feat> && gh pr create --base main`) no longer false-trips the gate. **Quoted string literals are deliberately NOT stripped on the push arm** (unlike the `gh pr merge` arm): the push *target* is a positional that may legitimately be quoted, so quote-stripping could drop a genuine quoted protected target (`git push origin "main"`) and miss a real push тАФ heredoc-only stripping preserves the zero-false-negative guarantee. **Fail-closed (zero false-negatives for genuine pushes):** a heredoc-strip failure or missing `python3` returns the command unstripped, and segmentation only ever *drops* non-push segments тАФ so a real `git push origin main` (bare, `-u`, `HEAD:main` refspec, env-prefixed, in a non-first `&&` segment, or with a quoted target) always still matches. **Not caught here:** a bare push whose configured upstream is protected with no token in the command text тАФ remote branch protection and the force-push arm are the backstops (out of scope, #366). **Accepted residual:** a protected token inside a *standalone* feature-branch slug (`git push origin release/x`) still trips тАФ fail-safe-to-block, escapable via `SKIP_HOOKS=branch`. **Alias-rename residual (#503):** `git -c alias.<x>=push <x> origin main` invokes the gated verb under an alias *name*, so the `${GIT_PREFIX}push` verb grep never sees `push` тАФ a contrived bypass of the same class as the `eval`/`bash -c` row below, left as a documented residual. (The *realistic* gap тАФ an UNLISTED valid leading global flag such as `--no-lazy-fetch` dropping the whole verb match тАФ IS closed: GIT_PREFIX carries a generic trailing `--long[=v]` / `-X` alternative, ┬з6.1 `git_matcher.sh`, so only the alias-rename and a space-separated value of an unlisted flag remain residual.) **Message-value strip (#440):** this arm also uses `message` mode, so a protected token documented inside a commit **message body** is elided as data (the strip is anchored to the `-m`/`-F` flag, so a quoted push target is preserved; unclosed message quote тЖТ fail-closed unstripped). | `branch` |
| `/work-on <N>` (or equivalent branch-creation referencing Issue `<N>`) | Block when Issue `<N>` is `status:proposed` (any type) **or** `Type=Directive` (any status, ┬з1.7). `status:proposed` тЖТ *"Issue is `status:proposed` тАФ run `/activate <N>` (once available) to validate it before branching."* Active Directive тЖТ *"Directive Issue тАФ Directives do not branch directly into PRs; use `/file-issue --parent <N>`."* (#46 landed the Directive arm; #171 generalized to the `status:proposed` arm.) | `proposed-protect` |
| `rm`/`mv`/`cp` carrying a force **or** recursive flag with args pointing outside registry (e.g. `rm -rf ~/.claude`, `rm -rf /`, `rm -rf ${HOME}/x`) | Block. The entry pre-filter recognizes the flag in **any** surface form тАФ clustered (`-rf`), separated (`-r -f`), long (`--force`, `--recursive`), non-first (`-i -rf`), **or placed after operands** (`rm <path> -rf`, valid GNU syntax тАФ #277) тАФ spanning operands between the verb and the flag but **stopping at a pipeline boundary** (`;` `|` `&`) so a flag belonging to another pipeline command does not trigger it (#212 cross-command anchoring preserved; the flag is matched as a whole token, so a `-rf` inside a filename is not a false trigger). Arg parsing is shell-aware (quotes preserved, no glob expansion via the hook); recognizes `~`, `$HOME`, and `${HOME}` forms; bare relative names are resolved against PWD and routed through `path_in_scope`. **Flagless `mv`/`cp` (#505):** a flagless `mv`/`cp` carrying an operand also enters `check_destructive_args` (every operand is scope-checked), so `mv in /out` clobbering an out-of-registry **dest** is now gated; `rm` is intentionally NOT broadened (an unforced single-file `rm` stays un-gated, #212). **Residual (#505):** `find тАж -delete` / `find тАж -exec rm`, `truncate`, and `>`/`>>` redirect clobbers to out-of-registry paths are NOT gated тАФ shell-feature breadth of the same class as the `eval`/`bash -c` warn-only residual, left documented rather than modeled. **`--` end-of-options guard (#555 A3):** the flagless `mv`/`cp` entry arm skips an optional leading `--` before its operand test, so `mv -- <src> <out-of-registry>` still ENTERS `check_destructive_args` instead of evading both arms (the raw operand test saw the `--` and bailed); `--` is treated as a flag (skipped) by the operand scan, so an all-in-scope `mv -- a b` still passes. **Command-position skip (#555 A5):** `check_destructive_args` skips the verb/wrapper words (`rm`/`mv`/`cp`/`sudo`/`doas`/`time`/`env`) ONLY in the leading wrapperтЖТverb prefix тАФ pre-fix it skipped ANY token equal to those words regardless of position, so an OPERAND literally named `env`/`time`/etc. (`mv <in-scope> env`) skipped `path_in_scope` entirely; every operand after the verb is now scope-checked. | `out-of-scope` |
| `eval`, `bash -c`, `sh -c`, `python -c`, heredoc-spawned shells (`bash <<EOF`) | Don't block. Audit-log as `warn` with category `bypass-suspect` so the trail exists. Hooks are guardrails, not sandboxes. | (warn-only) |
| `git reset --hard` | Block. **Message-value strip (#555 A2):** like the push arms, the reset arm strips `-m`/`--message`/`-F`/`--file` values (`strip_command_data` `message` mode) before the `reset --hard` grep, so a `git reset --hard` mentioned only inside a commit **message** (`git commit -m "note git reset --hard"`) is data, not a command, and no longer false-blocks; a real invocation still blocks (the strip never removes a genuine command verb). | `destructive` |
| `git clean` with a force-flag cluster (`-f`, `-df`, `-xdf`, `-ff`, тАж тАФ the matcher is `clean\s+-[A-Za-z]*f`, so any short-flag cluster containing `f` blocks, not only the bare `-f`) | Block. Like the push arm (#366), the command is **heredoc-stripped** (`strip_command_data` `heredoc` mode) before the `clean -тАжf` grep, so the token appearing only inside a `cat <<EOF` body does not false-trip; a real `git clean -f`/`-fd` invocation still blocks. (Heredoc-only, not quote-stripping, by parity with the push arm тАФ keeps a real `-f` flag undroppable.) **Message-value strip (#555 A2):** the clean arm's refinement now uses `message` mode (тКЗ heredoc), additionally eliding a `-m`/`-F` commit-message value, so a `git clean -f` documented inside a commit message no longer false-blocks; a real `-f` flag is never a message value, so this cannot under-block. | `destructive` |
| `git merge <protected>` (e.g. `git merge main`, `git merge origin/main`, `git merge release/v1`) on a non-protected branch | Block as a **backmerge**. The recommended motion when the base advances is `git pull --rebase origin <base>` per ┬з13; merging the base into the feature branch makes a noisy bubble that muddies the per-PR commit graph. Allowed when currently on the protected branch itself (e.g. merging a PR locally on `main`). | `backmerge` |
| Edit/Write target path outside the registry (except `$GHJIG_ROOT/` prefix = shell self-modification; and `$HOME/.claude/` prefix = user-global auto-memory tier, issue #91) | Block. **Carve-out path normalization (#555 A1):** the two carve-out prefix matches run against a **lexically-normalized** `$target` (made absolute against cwd, then a pure-string collapse of `.`/`..` segments тАФ **no** `pwd -P`/`realpath`/filesystem access), not the raw path тАФ so a `..`-laden absolute path (`$GHJIG_ROOT/../../etc/passwd`) can no longer borrow a carve-out prefix to skip the out-of-scope gate; a traversal that escapes the root normalizes outside it and falls through to the block. Lexical (not physical) is required because an Edit/Write routinely targets a **not-yet-existing** path and a carve-out ancestor may be **absent** (e.g. `$HOME/.claude` on a fresh CI runner) тАФ a physical resolve there falls back to the raw path and the bypass re-opens, so the normalization must hold regardless of what exists on disk. A genuine in-root edit still normalizes under the root and is carved out (no over-block); the sensitive-file check fires under both carve-outs regardless (#210). | `out-of-scope` |
| Edit/Write on `.env`, `.env.*`, `*.pem`, `*.pem.*`, `credentials*`, `id_rsa*`, `id_ed25519*` | Block (applies regardless of carve-outs тАФ the sensitive-file check fires under **both** the `$GHJIG_ROOT/` and `$HOME/.claude/` carve-outs; #210). **Case-insensitive basename match (#501):** the basename is lower-cased before the glob test, so `.ENV`/`KEY.PEM` block as `.env`/`*.pem` do. The set carries **both** an exact/dotfile form (`.env`, `*.pem`) **and** a suffixed form (`.env.*`, `*.pem.*`) so an environment-suffixed or double-extension variant тАФ `.env.example`, `.env.local`, `key.pem.txt` тАФ is caught, not only the bare `.env`/`.pem`. Matches the lexical basename **and**, when the final path component is a symlink, the `python3`-realpath-resolved basename тАФ so a symlink with an innocuous name pointing at a sensitive target is blocked too (#234); `python3` absent/unresolvable тЖТ lexical-only (fail-soft). TOCTOU and hardlinks are out of scope. | `sensitive` |
| Edit/Write on a protected branch (except when the file path is under `$GHJIG_ROOT/` = shell self-modification; or `$HOME/.claude/` = user-global auto-memory, issue #91 тАФ those have no relationship to the repo's branch state) | Block | `branch` |
| `gh pr merge` when the PR's `closingIssuesReferences` includes any issue whose body has unchecked AC items (any task-list bullet family тАФ `-`/`*`/`+` or an ordered `N.`, and indented forms тАФ not only `- [ ]`; #500) and no **trusted-filer** comment (author association тИИ OWNER/MEMBER/MAINTAINER/COLLABORATOR тАФ a drive-by non-trusted comment does **not** unlock the gate; #500) matching the **canonical marker** `^## AC closeout (resolved by PR #N)` (a comment that merely starts with `## AC closeout` no longer satisfies the gate; #500) has been posted yet. Closes the gap where `Closes #N` auto-closes an issue but leaves its AC list reading as "nothing was done." The helper `scripts/ac_closeout.sh <pr-num>` is idempotent and satisfies the gate by construction; `/ship` runs it as step 7.6. Fail-open with `audit_log warn` when `gh` calls time out or return malformed JSON (5-second per-call bound; SPEC ┬з6.1 framing тАФ guardrails, not punishment for transient network issues). Also fail-open with `audit_log warn ac-closeout helper-missing` when `.claude/hooks/helpers/ac_closeout_gate.sh` is absent from the working tree at hook-fire time (e.g., a running session predates the helper's introduction тАФ see the **session-restart caveat for hook-spec changes** below). The helper-source is presence-checked and a `gate_loaded` flag gates the downstream helper calls; an unloaded helper writes a warn and the merge proceeds тАФ silent fail-through is treated as a regression. **Merge detection is on command words, not a raw substring** (#340): the shared `is_pr_merge_command` predicate strips heredoc bodies and quoted string literals before testing for the `gh тАж pr тАж merge` words, so `gh pr merge` appearing only as data (a heredoc body, a quoted `--body`/`-m` value, a commit message) no longer false-triggers the gate; it is fail-closed (any parse uncertainty / `python3` absence / helper miss тЖТ treated as a merge), and a merge wrapped in an executed quoted string (`bash -c "gh pr merge тАж"`) is a deliberate, documented non-detection. | `ac-closeout` |
| `gh pr merge` to the **default branch** without `--merge` тАФ `--squash` / `--rebase` / a **bare** merge (no strategy flag, which the repo's `squashMergeAllowed` default resolves to a squash) тЖТ block; `--merge` (including `--auto --merge`, the `/ship` form) тЖТ allow. Enforces SPEC ┬з5.7.1's no-ff merge mandate: a squash collapses the DocтЖТTestтЖТCode arc (┬з1.2's load-bearing artifact) into a single commit on the trunk, erasing on `main` the very evidence the flow produces. Keyed on the **live default branch** (`gh repo view --json defaultBranchRef`), NOT `PROTECTED_BRANCH_PATTERN` тАФ so a squash into a **non-default** base (a topic branch consolidating sub-PRs, ┬з10.5) is **allowed** (the arc-preservation argument is about the trunk). Strategy and PR are parsed by a **gh-flag-aware token walk** (`parse_gh_merge_argv`, shell-aware via `shlex` with a `read -ra` fallback, #290): the strategy is the explicit strategy **flag token** тАФ `--merge`/`-m` тЖТ merge, `--squash`/`-s` тЖТ squash, `--rebase`/`-r` тЖТ rebase, none тЖТ bare тАФ **not a substring**, so a `--merge` appearing inside a `--body`/`--subject` *value* is not mistaken for the strategy (#290 A) and the short `-m` is correctly recognized as compliant (#290 C); the PR is the first **positional** token (or a `.../pull/N` URL's N), skipping value-taking flags' values (`--body`/`-b`, `--body-file`, `--subject`/`-t`, `--match-head-commit`, `--author-email`, `--repo`/`-R`) so a flag value is never read as the PR (#290 B). Strategy is evaluated **first**: an explicit `--merge` is allowed **silently** (`mark_allow`, no audit record) with no base resolution at all; only a non-`--merge` strategy triggers the base + default-branch lookup. Fail-open with `audit_log warn` if the PR base or the default branch can't be resolved (`gh` down / no auth; 5-second per-call bound), parity with `ac-closeout`. The PR falls back to the current branch's PR when the command names none. Independent of the `ac-closeout` arm (separate `should_skip` category; both fire on `gh pr merge` and each reaches its own decided state). The coarse entry grep is refined by the same `is_pr_merge_command` predicate as `ac-closeout` (#340), so `gh pr merge` text in a heredoc body / quoted argument / commit message does not engage this gate either (fail-closed on parse uncertainty). Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=merge-strategy SKIP_REASON='<why>'`. (#288, #290, #340) | `merge-strategy` |
| `gh pr merge` when the **local branch is strictly ahead of its pushed remote head** тАФ unpushed local commits exist that the merge would leave behind тЖТ **block**. **git-only, no `gh`**: resolve the local HEAD and the branch's pushed remote-tracking head, then block **only** in the strictly-ahead state тАФ local HEAD descends from the remote head **and** the two SHAs differ (`git merge-base --is-ancestor <remote> <local>` true **and** `<remote>` тЙа `<local>`). Every other state тЖТ **allow**: behind (remote ahead of local), diverged (neither is an ancestor of the other), an absent local or remote-tracking ref, a detached HEAD, or no configured upstream тАФ the guard is a **positive** strictly-ahead detection, so any ambiguity falls to allow (a merge that races a re-push is caught instead by the `merge-review` staleness logic below тАФ a review at a superseded head no longer pins the current head тАФ and the ┬з5.7 merge-time re-pin). Prevents merging a **stale remote head that lacks unpushed work** (handol #244) тАФ so the reviewed/attested local state actually reaches the trunk rather than a behind-remote head. Block message names the positive alternative: **"push your local commits first"**. Independent arm тАФ its own `should_skip` category and `decided`/`mark_allow`/`block`/`pass_through_trace` terminal state, mirroring the `ac-closeout` and `merge-strategy` arms (both fire on `gh pr merge`, each reaches its own decided state). Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=push-parity SKIP_REASON='<why>'`. (#544, #244) | `push-parity` |
| `gh pr merge` when the PR has **no passing GitHub review pinned to the current head** тЖТ **block** (#586, replacing `merge-attestation`). Resolve the PR number from the merge argv (`extract_pr_from_merge_cmd`), the current head via `gh pr view <n> --json headRefOid`, and the review objects via `gh api repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/<n>/reviews` (the object exposes `state`, `commit_id`, and `author.login` per review тАФ `gh pr view --json reviews` does **not** expose `commit_id`). **Aggregation rule (verbatim):** *latest APPROVED-or-CHANGES_REQUESTED review per author wins; COMMENTED/PENDING/DISMISSED ignored тАФ mirrors GitHub reviewDecision.* Concretely: filter the reviews to `state тИИ {APPROVED, CHANGES_REQUESTED}`, then take each author's latest surviving review; `reviewDecision` itself is **not** consulted (it is `null` on non-branch-protected repos тЖТ would fail open). **Allow** in exactly two shapes: **(a) native** тАФ a review with `state==APPROVED` and `commit_id==head`, and no author's filtered-latest is `CHANGES_REQUESTED`; **(b) self-marker** тАФ a `COMMENTED` review with `commit_id==head` carrying **exactly one** `verdict=approve` marker where the review's `author.login == PR-author == merger`, bound to **one** review object, and no author's filtered-latest is `CHANGES_REQUESTED` (the self-marker COMMENT is parsed separately, so the APPROVED/CHANGES_REQUESTED filter does not drop it) тАФ **and** `resolve_self_review_policy` (┬з5.7.1, #598) yields `allow`; under `deny` the self-marker is **not** accepted (only shape (a), a native second-party `APPROVED` at head, satisfies the gate), the per-target policy that keeps the cross-target self-review producer exception (┬з5.7.1) off by default in onboarded targets. **Block** on: no review; only stale reviews (`commit_id != head`); an author's filtered-latest is `CHANGES_REQUESTED`; a marker `verdict=block`; conflicting or multiple markers; a self-marker while `resolve_self_review_policy == deny` (#598); an empty head. **Fail-closed** on any lookup failure тАФ PR unresolvable, `gh` error/timeout/down, malformed JSON, or a `safe_source` helper miss тЖТ **block** (the deliberate divergence from the retired attestation arm's fail-open staleness leg; the safe direction for a merge gate is to require a review, ┬з5.7.1). **Bypass:** when `resolve_review_gate` (┬з5.7.1) yields `bypass`, the gate is skipped with a **loud** `audit_log warn merge-review bypass` тАФ **except** it still **blocks** a covered-form (`gh pr merge --auto --merge --delete-branch`) **agent self-merge** (PR author == merger), fail-closed on the author/merger lookup (#592), so the static `permissions.allow` (┬з5.7.1) is never the sole guard for that exact form. Only `verdict` is read from marker text; identity and head come from the review object (bounds a prompt-injection-flipped verdict тАФ a marker is honored only when `author.login == PR-author == merger` at `commit_id==head`). **Threat model:** a GitHub review at the head is stronger evidence than the retired forgeable local attestation file, but hooks remain mistake-prevention, not a security boundary тАФ same status as a `SKIP_HOOKS` escape. Independent arm тАФ its own `should_skip` category and terminal `decided` state, parity with `ac-closeout`/`merge-strategy`/`push-parity`. Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=merge-review SKIP_REASON='<why>'`. (#586, #585, #544, #246, #543) | `merge-review` |
| `gh pr merge` of a **`feat`/`fix` PR** whose merge diff touches **zero source files** (test/doc-only) тЖТ emit an **advisory warn**, **never a block**. The **positive completeness face** of the `merge-review` arm above (#544): the origin case is handol #244, where an implementation commit was never pushed and only the Phase-B test reached the head тАФ so the merge would land a test with no code. **Independent advisory arm**, sequenced **after** the `merge-review` arm on the same `gh тАж pr merge` entry-grep. **PR type** is resolved from the **branch name** (`<user>/(feat\|fix)/тАж`) with a **PR-title conventional-commit** fallback (`featтАж:` / `fixтАж:`); any other type тЖТ no warn. **Source-vs-test/doc classification reuses the `.shellsecretignore` allow-list** via `secret_scan_path_allowed` (the ┬з6.1 `secret` arm's classifier) тАФ a path is "not source" **iff** it matches the `.shellsecretignore` test/doc/example globs; **no new glob list** (┬з9 reference-not-restate тАФ the `.shellsecretignore` set is the documented heuristic SSOT, not restated here). "**Zero source**" = the merge file list is **non-empty AND every path is allowed**. **One bounded** `gh pr view <pr> --json headRefName,title,files` call feeds **both** the type resolution and the file list. **Fail-open throughout:** PR# unresolvable / `gh` down / empty file list тЖТ **no warn, no block, no hard error**. On a positive detection it writes `audit_log warn merge-completeness` + a **one-line stderr notice**; it **never** calls `block` / `exit 2`. **NOT a SKIP/escape category (AC4):** being warn-only, there is **nothing to skip** тАФ there is **no** `should_skip merge-completeness`, so it is deliberately **absent** from the ┬з7 escape categories **and** from the ┬з1.9 machine-derived hook tally (┬з116 parity counts `should_skip` categories, which this arm has none of). **Accepted residual (coupling):** because classification reuses `.shellsecretignore`, a future secret-allow-list edit shifts completeness classification too тАФ a bounded, accepted residual whose **entire blast radius is a single spurious/missing advisory warn, never a block**. (#548, #244) | `merge-completeness` (advisory; warn-only, no `should_skip`) |
| `gh issue close <N>` against a trusted-filer (OWNER / MEMBER / MAINTAINER / COLLABORATOR per `authorAssociation`) **non-discussion** Issue without `--reason completed` (i.e., the close is `not planned` or `duplicate`). Filer-aware invariant per ┬з1.5 тАФ mode-independent, applies in both `attended` and `unattended`. **Discussion-tier is classified first and independent of trust** (#236): a `discussion`-labeled Issue follows the ┬з5.19 two-path rule (`--reason completed` / `"not planned"` allowed regardless of filer; bare/`duplicate` blocked) and never reaches this trusted-filer check. The issue selector is matched in all gh-accepted forms тАФ bare number, quoted number, and `https://тАж/issues/<N>` URL тАФ and **normalized to the pure issue number** before the `is_trusted_filer` / discussion-label lookups and the block message (#223; `is_trusted_filer` requires a bare number, so an un-normalized URL/quoted selector would silently fail-open). When the selector is a **URL**, the lookups are **repo-aware** тАФ filer-trust and the discussion label resolve against the URL's `owner/name` (via `--repo`), not the current directory's repo, so a foreign-repo close is evaluated against the foreign repo's issue rather than a same-numbered local one (#231). When the selector is a **bare number but an explicit `--repo owner/name` (or `[HOST/]owner/name`) flag тАФ or `gh`'s `-R` short alias тАФ is present**, that flag's repo is parsed and used for the same repo-aware lookups (#237 for `--repo`, #242 for `-R`, both completing #231) тАФ `gh` accepts both `{<number>|<url>}` selectors and a `--repo`/`-R` flag, so the flag form is closed against the same cross-repo fail-open as the URL form. A bare-number selector with no `--repo`/`-R` flag keeps current-repo behavior; an unparseable URL or flag value fails soft to the current repo. **`owner/name` validation (#555 A6):** the resolved cross-repo target (URL- or flag-derived) is validated for a `.`/`..` path segment and the GitHub owner/repo charset тАФ the prior parses checked segment *count* only, so a `.`/`..` segment (`../../evil`, `owner/..`) could redirect the trust/discussion `gh issue view --repo` lookup to an attacker-chosen repo; a rejected value falls back to the current repo (fail-soft), tightening the trust check. Fail-open if `is_trusted_filer` can't resolve. Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=trusted-filer-mutate SKIP_REASON='<why>'`. | `trusted-filer-mutate` |
| `gh issue edit <N> --remove-label directive` against ANY filer (trusted or not). Removing the `directive` label declassifies a Directive and bypasses dir-mode review; human confirm required always. Matches **both** separator forms тАФ `--remove-label directive` and `--remove-label=directive` (optionally quoted) тАФ **and** a comma-joined value list where `directive` is any element (`--remove-label other,directive`; gh removes every listed label), with a word-boundary tail so a longer label like `directive-foo` does not over-match (#211). The issue selector is matched in all gh-accepted forms тАФ bare number, quoted number, and `https://тАж/issues/<N>` URL (#223). Same matcher and escape as the close-arm above. | `trusted-filer-mutate` |
| `gh issue edit <N> --add-label {execution\|task\|bug}` when the label contradicts the Issue body's line-1 `Parent Directive: #N` marker (the canonical resolver, ┬з5.2): `execution` with **no** marker (an `execution` Issue requires a parent, ┬з1.7), or `task`/`bug` **with** a marker present (standalone types must not be parented тАФ the marker is a type smell). Blocks the contradictory relabel and names the fix (set/clear the line-1 marker first, then relabel). Converts the **advisory** #197 reviewer/skill layer into runtime enforcement тАФ fires regardless of which agent or path applies the label, the "hooks-as-environment an agent cannot drift past" mechanism (MISSION). Scoped to the `--add-label` edit path only; the `gh issue create` path is already labelтЖФmarker-consistent via `/file-issue` (post-#197) and is **not** gated. The gated label is detected in both separator forms and **anywhere in a comma-joined value list** (`--add-label other,execution`; #212), terminated at a **true label boundary** тАФ comma / whitespace / quote / end тАФ so a hyphen- or underscore-suffixed custom label (`directive-foo`, `task_old`) that merely *starts with* a type token does **not** over-match it (#278 Theme C; a letter-suffixed `executionish` was already excluded). **Selector normalization (#276):** the issue selector is resolved via the shared `resolve_gh_issue_target` helper (`helpers/issue_type.sh`), tolerant of selector **form** (bare / quoted / URL тАФ closing the A1 URL-form bypass) and flag **order** (the positional issue arg need not immediately follow `edit` тАФ A2); a `-R`/`--repo owner/name` (or URL-embedded) target is threaded into the marker/label predicates so a **cross-repo** `--add-label` edit resolves against the command's target repo, not the cwd (A3 тАФ the predicates' optional `repo` arg also keys the per-session cache by `owner/name`, so a foreign `#N` never poisons the current repo's same-numbered entry). The helper tokenizes **shell-aware** (`shlex`, mirroring `check_destructive_args`) so a quoted flag value's interior digits (`--body "fixes 99 things"`) are not mistaken for the positional issue, and normalizes a `[HOST/]owner/name` repo to `owner/name` (#283). **Also (#251):** blocks `--add-label initiative` on a `directive` Issue and `--add-label directive` on an `initiative` Issue (the two tier type-keys are mutually exclusive, keeping `is_directive_issue`/`is_initiative_issue` coherent); and blocks `--add-label directive` when the Directive body lacks **exactly one** parent kind тАФ a `## MISSION fit` field (via `issue_has_mission_fit_field`) XOR a line-1 `Parent Initiative: #N` marker (via `issue_has_initiative_parent_marker`), i.e. both-present or neither-present (the parent-XOR, ┬з1.7). Fail-open if the Issue body can't be resolved (`gh` down / no auth / not found / predicate undefined) тАФ the block fires only on a positively-resolved contradiction (parity with `proposed-protect` / `trusted-filer-mutate`). Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=label-parent-consistency SKIP_REASON='<why>'`. | `label-parent-consistency` |
| Mutating `gh issue edit` / `close` / `reopen` (incl. `--add-label` / `--remove-label` / `--body` / `--title`) targeting an `initiative` Issue. An Initiative is **read-only to the shell except for appended comments** (┬з1.7) тАФ the shell *consumes* Initiatives and never edits, closes, relabels, or retires them; strategic decisions stay upstream. `gh issue comment` is not a mutating verb and is always allowed. The issue selector is resolved via the shared `resolve_gh_issue_target` helper (#276; bare / quoted / URL forms + flag-order tolerance), then `is_initiative_issue` resolves it against the **current** repo. This matcher deliberately **does not** honor a `-R`/`--repo` cross-repo target (unlike `label-parent-consistency`): **cross-repo Initiatives are out of scope** (┬з1.7 тАФ they would reintroduce the cross-repo-trust surface of the `trusted-filer-mutate` close arm), so the matcher governs only same-repo Initiatives; a foreign-targeted `gh issue edit` resolves against the cwd repo (and, if that is not an Initiative, `mark_allow`s). Fail-open if the predicate can't resolve. **Precedence over `trusted-filer-mutate`:** for `gh issue close <initiative>`, the two matchers give opposite verdicts тАФ a trusted-filer close *with* `--reason completed` is *allowed* by `trusted-filer-mutate`, but *any* close on an `initiative` Issue is *blocked* here. `initiative-readonly` wins: an Initiative is **never** closed by the shell, even `--reason completed` by a trusted filer (the shell consumes Initiatives, never retires them тАФ termination is an upstream decision surfaced via `/initiative-feedback`, ┬з5.22). The block holds by the **block-is-terminal** rule, not by matcher ordering: `trusted-filer-mutate` actually evaluates *first* in `pre_tool_use.sh` but only `mark_allow`s a `--reason completed` close (non-terminal тАФ `decided=1; return 0`); `initiative-readonly` evaluates *later* and calls `block` (`exit 2`). Because any `block` terminates the hook while `mark_allow` never short-circuits a subsequent matcher, the block wins regardless of the two matchers' relative order. Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=initiative-readonly SKIP_REASON='<why>'`. (#251) | `initiative-readonly` |
| A GitHub **close keyword** (`close`/`closes`/`closed`/`fix`/`fixes`/`fixed`/`resolve`/`resolves`/`resolved`, case-insensitive, optional `:`) followed by `#N` where Issue `#N` is a **Directive**, in either (a) the inline `--body`/`-b` value of `gh pr create` / `gh pr edit`, or (b) a commit message (`-m`/`--message` values + heredoc body, scanned inside the commit-format umbrella arm). | GitHub auto-closes a referenced Issue at merge when such a keyword + `#N` appears anywhere in a PR body **or** any commit message. For an **Execution** Issue this is correct (its merge resolves it); for a **Directive** it bypasses the `/complete-directive` signal-evidence gate (N=3 vote, ┬з5.13) тАФ a Directive must close ONLY through that gate (live regression: PR #489's body `closes #477 signal 3` auto-closed Directive #477 while signal 4 was still pending). The shared detector `directive_close_violation` (`helpers/git_matcher.sh`) extracts ALL keyword + `#N` pairs and calls `is_directive_issue` **per `#N`**, blocking on the FIRST Directive; **Execution Issues are never blocked** (`Closes #<execution>` is the normal resolving trailer) and a non-close mention (`Refs #N`, `advances #N`, prose) never matches the close-keyword grammar, so it passes. **Per-`#N` fail-open**: an unresolved type (gh down / no auth / non-numeric) skips that `#N` (parity with `proposed-protect`/`initiative-readonly`). The PR vector reads the **inline** `--body`/`-b` value only тАФ `--body-file`/`-F` (incl. the `-F -` stdin form `/ship`/`/sync-pr` use) is a **documented residual** (reading an arbitrary file path adds an IO/path-resolution/TOCTOU surface disproportionate to the vector); `owner/repo#N` and full-URL close-forms are likewise a residual (this shell authors bare `#N`). ┬з6.0: a wrong *allow* irreversibly evades the completion gate and corrupts governance history (high-cost тАФ P1 hard negative gate failing safe toward block); a wrong *block* costs renaming to `Refs #N` (recoverable), and the block message names that positive alternative (P4). Escape: `SKIP_HOOKS=directive-close SKIP_REASON='<why>'`. (#490) | `directive-close` |

**`gh` entry-anchor tolerance (#499).** The `gh`-command matchers above (`ac-closeout`, `merge-strategy`, `push-parity`, `merge-review` on `gh тАж pr merge`; the trusted-filer / initiative / label-consistency arms on `gh тАж issue close`/`edit`) anchor on the subcommand through a **leading global-flag run**, not on `gh` immediately followed by the subcommand тАФ so `gh --repo o/r pr merge`, `gh -R o/r pr merge`, `gh --repo=o/r issue close` all still match. Each leading token is a `-X`/`--xxx[=val]` flag with an optional non-flag value (`o/r`); the subcommand pair (`pr merge`, `issue close`/`edit`) must stay **adjacent** after the run, so the word `merge` buried in a `gh pr create` body/title is not over-matched. Without this widening a global flag placed before the subcommand would slip the whole command past the gate.

**Session-restart caveat for hook-spec changes.** Claude Code binds its hook routing from `.claude/settings.json` + the working tree at session start. Adding a *new* helper file under `.claude/hooks/helpers/` (or any path referenced by an existing hook via `.`/`source`) does not retroactively become reachable to a session that started before the file existed. Such a session continues to execute the *updated* `pre_tool_use.sh` (re-read per invocation), but a `. "$SHELL_ROOT/.claude/hooks/helpers/<new-helper>.sh"` line silently fails тАФ and any function defined only in that helper is undefined, so downstream calls return rc=127 and matchers can fall through without ever reaching their block / warn arms. **The fix is to start a fresh `ghjig` session after pulling a hook-spec change that introduces a new helper file.** The hook-side mitigation is the **`safe_source`** utility (hosted in `.claude/hooks/hookrt.sh` тАФ the "hook runtime" bootstrap that also hosts `audit_log`): every helper source line тАФ both **hook-to-helper** (the 5 hook files under `.claude/hooks/` sourcing helpers) and **helper-to-helper** (a helper under `.claude/hooks/helpers/` sourcing another helper from the same directory, e.g. `branch_guard.sh` тЖТ `git_matcher.sh`) тАФ goes through `safe_source <helper-path> <audit-category>`, which presence-checks the file, sources it, and on miss emits `audit_log warn <category> helper-missing "<path>"` and returns 1. The one documented exception is the **bootstrap-to-runtime shim** at `helpers/log.sh:6` тЖТ `hookrt.sh`: that source line can't go through `safe_source` because `safe_source` lives in the file being sourced (chicken-and-egg), so it falls back to a primitive `.` and is stderr-only on miss. The scope predicate for "in scope of the `safe_source` invariant" is: the source target is under `.claude/hooks/helpers/`, NOT directly under `.claude/hooks/` (i.e. `hookrt.sh` and the 5 hook entry-point files are exempt тАФ they are the runtime, not helpers). The shape this closes тАФ one site warning while a sibling source-site of the same helper fails silently, hiding the second consumer тАФ was the regression #36 surfaced. The hook continues to **fail-open** (matcher arm short-circuits, command proceeds) so a missing helper is recoverable, not a developer-lockout тАФ but the failure mode is visible in `audit.jsonl` instead of silent. Existing helpers that the running session already loaded (e.g. `helpers/coauthor.sh`) are unaffected тАФ their function bindings persist across invocations of the parent hook. Cross-reference ┬з3.2.1 (hook command path resolution).

**`safe_source` fail-policy table** (per-helper audit category and on-miss behavior; **all entries fail-open** with a category-typed warn тАФ future PRs may flip individual entries to fail-closed with their own SPEC ┬з1.4 justification):

| Helper | Audit category | On-miss notes |
|---|---|---|
| `hookrt.sh` (the runtime itself) | (n/a тАФ primitive bootstrap) | Hook exits 0 with one-line stderr warn; cannot audit-log itself |
| `helpers/log.sh` (compatibility shim тЖТ `hookrt.sh`) | `audit` | Stderr warn only; downstream `audit_log` unavailable |
| `helpers/escape.sh` | `escape` | `SKIP_HOOKS` machinery degrades to "always block"; documented |
| `helpers/cwd_guard.sh` | `out-of-scope` | `in_scope` undefined тЖТ hook exits 0 anyway |
| `helpers/branch_guard.sh` | `branch` | **Security-relevant** тАФ protected-branch enforcement off; warn carries a "not enforced" suffix |
| `helpers/secret_scan.sh` | `secret` | **Security-relevant** тАФ secret enforcement off; warn carries a "not enforced" suffix |
| `helpers/conventional_commit.sh` | `commit-format` | Hygiene, not security |
| `helpers/detect_stack.sh` | `format` | Lint/format detection off |
| `helpers/git_matcher.sh` | `commit-format` | Constants source; downstream matchers degrade together |
| `helpers/ac_closeout_gate.sh` | `ac-closeout` / `merge-strategy` | Already-shipped per #31/#32. Matcher-scoped: `safe_source`d on the `gh pr merge` path under the `ac-closeout` category (AC-closeout arm) **and** independently under the `merge-strategy` category (the `parse_gh_merge_argv` strategy/PR token walk, #290, lives here too). **Also hosts (folded in, #544) the merge-parity gate function** `local_ahead_of_pr` (`push-parity` arm), and (folded in, #586) the `merge-review` gate-acceptance function `review_gate_accepts` (the retired `write_review_attestation` + `attestation_matches` functions are **deleted** with the `merge-attestation` arm). **Also hosts (folded in, #548) the `merge-completeness` advisory helpers** тАФ the branch/title type resolver and the `.shellsecretignore`-reusing zero-source classifier тАФ same fail-open posture (a helper miss тЖТ no warn, matching this arm's throughout-fail-open contract). On-miss, the `merge-strategy` and `push-parity` arms **fail-open** (allow) with a category-typed warn, same posture as the `ac-closeout` arm. The `merge-review` arm is the deliberate exception тАФ it **fails CLOSED** (block) on a helper miss, mirroring its fail-closed posture on every other lookup failure (┬з5.7.1: the safe direction for a merge integrity gate is to require a review, not skip it). |
| `helpers/status.sh` | `status` | Informational only; no enforcement impact |
| `helpers/issue_type.sh` | `proposed-protect` | Type-awareness + lifecycle predicates (`is_directive_issue`, `is_initiative_issue`, `is_proposed_issue`, `issue_has_parent_marker`, `issue_has_initiative_parent_marker`, `issue_has_mission_fit_field`) (┬з1.7); on miss the AC-closeout Type-aware skip, the `proposed-protect` matcher, the `label-parent-consistency` matcher (incl. its initiative/directive + parent-XOR arms), the `initiative-readonly` matcher, and the `directive-close` matcher (which calls `is_directive_issue` per `#N`) all fail-open (engineering hooks revert to non-Type-aware behavior; an undefined predicate is treated as "not blocked by that arm") |
| `helpers/issue_filer.sh` | `trusted-filer-mutate` | Filer-trust predicate (┬з1.5 filer-aware invariants); on miss the `trusted-filer-mutate` matcher fails-open (the close / declassify proceeds under the regular attended/unattended rules тАФ protection layer is best-effort, not blocking) |
| `helpers/reviewer_audit.sh` | `reviewer-reject` | `reviewer_reject_audit` emission for non-pass reviewer verdicts (#361, Directive #356 signal 3); on miss the skill's reject-audit record is skipped (fail-open тАФ the reviewer verdict still gates the flow; only the observability trail is best-effort, never the gate) |
| `helpers/blast_radius.sh` | `reviewer-tier` | `is_high_asymmetry` high-asymmetry decision classifier (┬з4.11); on miss the gated decision degrades to a **single reviewer** with an `audit_log warn reviewer-tier` record тАФ never a lockout (a wrong degrade loses redundancy on one decision; a lockout would block all shipping тАФ the asymmetry that picks fail-open) |
