**`helpers/ship_mode.sh` is intentionally absent from this table** тАФ it is *not* reached through `safe_source`, so the scope predicate above ("under `.claude/hooks/helpers/`, reached through `safe_source`") does not govern it. `ship_mode.sh` (`resolve_mode` + `ship_park_pr`) is loaded by the `/ship` and `/status` **command** surfaces via a direct `.`, and by `helpers/status.sh` via a manual `[ -f тАж ] && . тАж` guard (not `safe_source`) because `resolve_mode` there is **informational** (it populates the status projection's mode field, with no enforcement decision riding on it) тАФ an absent helper already fails open to an empty mode string, and `/ship`'s own preflight handles a missing helper on the enforcement path. Its on-miss posture is therefore fail-open by construction, consistent with every table entry; no row is added because a row would assert a `safe_source` source-site that does not exist.

**`helper-missing` audit-event shape** тАФ the on-miss line emitted by `safe_source` is:

```json
{"ts":"<RFC3339>","event":"warn","category":"<from-table>","decision":"helper-missing","reason":"<absolute-path-to-missing-helper>","cwd":"<pwd>","source":"<live|test>"}
```

`reason` and `cwd` are JSON-escaped per SPEC ┬з7. `decision` carries the constant token `helper-missing`. **`helper-missing` audit categories are a superset of `SKIP_HOOKS` categories** тАФ for example, `status` is a valid audit category for an informational helper but is NOT a `SKIP_HOOKS` category. The escape-hatch list in ┬з7 stays unchanged; the audit categories enumerate what `safe_source` can emit, which is broader.

**Matcher pass-through audit contract.** PR #32 surfaced a class of bug where a matcher entered (its `grep -qE 'pattern'` matched) but no terminal arm fired тАФ the matcher silently exited with no audit record. This made "matcher entered but produced no audit" indistinguishable from "matcher never matched the command" тАФ a structural blind spot in the audit trail. The contract closes that gap:

> **For every matcher in `pre_tool_use.sh`, if the matcher entered (`grep` matched), `audit.jsonl` MUST gain exactly one record whose `category` field matches the matcher's category in this hook invocation.**

The terminal arm fires that record (or marks it as decided without emission):
- A `block` decision emits `audit_log block <cat> deny <reason>`.
- A `warn` decision emits `audit_log warn <cat> <decision-token> <reason>` (`decision-token` тИИ {`notice`, `helper-missing`, `pass-through`, ...}). Note `bypass-suspect` is a *category* (with decision-token `notice`), not a decision-token.
- A **high-frequency happy-path** arm (e.g., every clean `git commit`, every in-scope `rm -rf`, every local `--amend`) calls `mark_allow <cat>` (in `hookrt.sh`). This sets the caller's `decided` flag with NO audit emission тАФ the matcher's contract is satisfied (it entered, evaluated cleanly, allowed) without per-action audit noise. Distinct from the explicit-`notice` warn path, which is used for low-frequency designed-allow cases where an audit record is desired.
- If no other arm fires by the matcher's tail, the helper `pass_through_trace <cat> "<cmd>"` (also in `hookrt.sh`) emits `audit_log warn <cat> pass-through "<truncated-cmd>"`. This is the anomalous case тАФ the matcher decided to do nothing without naming why, which we treat as a soft regression worth flagging.

Implementation pattern (per Bash-branch matcher in `pre_tool_use.sh`):

```bash
if printf '%s' "$cmd" | grep -qE 'pattern'; then
  decided=
  # ... terminal arms set `decided=1` ...
  [ -z "$decided" ] && pass_through_trace <cat> "$cmd"
fi
```

The `decided=` flag is reset at the head of each matcher block so state cannot leak across matchers. Smoke (`scripts/test/smoke.sh` ┬з39) asserts the invariant:
- **┬з39a**: for each matcher, a synthesized benign-but-entering command produces exactly one new audit record with the expected category.
- **┬з39b**: structural awk-grep over `pre_tool_use.sh` тАФ every `if printf '%s' "$cmd" | grep -qE ...; then` block ends with either an explicit `decided=1` audit-emitter or a `pass_through_trace` tail.
- **┬з39c**: negative тАФ a command that enters no matcher (e.g. `ls -la`) produces zero new audit records.

**Decision-token vocabulary** (`decision` field in `audit_log`):

| Token | Used by | Meaning |
|---|---|---|
| `deny` | `block` | Hook refused the command; `exit 2` follows. |
| `notice` | `audit_log warn` | Soft signal тАФ degraded enforcement (gh timeout, indeterminate state, explicit allow with reason). |
| `helper-missing` | `safe_source` on miss | A hook helper was absent; matcher arm short-circuited. |
| `bypass-suspect` | bypass-suspect matcher | Command looks like an eval/heredoc bypass (warn-only, not a block). |
| `pass-through` | `pass_through_trace` | Matcher entered but no terminal arm fired тАФ anomalous; treat as a soft regression. |
| `skip` | `audit_log escape` | `SKIP_HOOKS=` was honored; categorized as `escape`. |
| `reject` | reviewer-reject audit (#361) | A reviewer subagent returned a non-pass verdict; the `reason` carries `class=<reason-class> issue=#<N>`. |

The token list is intentionally short and stable; future arms add new tokens here, not new `event`-type kinds.

**Event-kind set.** The `event` field is one of `block` / `warn` / `escape` / `info`. `info` is an **informational** record тАФ not a refusal тАФ e.g. the AC-closeout Type=Directive skip (`pre_tool_use.sh`) and the dir-mode lifecycle notices (`audit_log info directive-*`, ┬з5.10+), typically carrying the `notice` decision token. This four-member set is the stable one the "not new `event`-type kinds" rule above refers to: arms add new `decision` tokens, not new event kinds.

**Audit `source` field** (live/test origin discriminator, #361 / Directive #356 signal 1). Every `audit_log` record carries an additive top-level `source` field тАФ `live` for real sessions, `test` for test-harness fixture fires. It is the **last** field in the JSON object (after `cwd`), so it does not perturb the `reason`-anchored ┬з50a format scan or `_audit_validate_format` (which inspects only `category`/`decision`/`reason`, never the record shape). The value resolves from a single harness-owned environment marker: `source=test` **iff** `GHJIG_AUDIT_SOURCE` is exactly the token `test`; **any** other value тАФ unset, empty, `smoke`, `live`, or arbitrary тАФ resolves to `live` (fail-safe-to-`live`). The field is additive and append-only-safe: historical lines written before #361 have no `source` key (`.source == null` under `jq`); consumers treat an absent value as legacy/unknown (fail-open on absence).

**Anti-reclassification invariant** (Directive #356 Constraint тАФ a `live` action must never be silently reclassifiable to `test`/`smoke` to dodge a friction signal). The marker is read from the **hook subprocess environment**. Per ┬з7, the live Claude Code Bash tool consumes a leading `VAR=val` as the *spawned command's* own environment тАФ it never lands in `tool_input.command`, and the hook subprocess does not inherit it тАФ and shell state does not persist between Bash-tool calls. So a real action cannot inject `GHJIG_AUDIT_SOURCE=test` into the hook subprocess that writes its audit record; only the process that **launches the session** (e.g. `scripts/test/smoke.sh`, which `export`s the marker before driving the hooks directly тАФ mirroring the `GHJIG_STATE_DIR_OVERRIDE` test seam, ┬з3.2.2) can set it. Smoke pins the invariant: a fixture fire with the marker unset records `source=live`, and one with a *forged* `GHJIG_AUDIT_SOURCE=smoke` (a non-`test` value) still records `live`. A query can therefore partition the log by origin (`jq 'select(.source=="live")'` vs the all-records count) to exclude test-fixture noise from the existing backlog тАФ the observability surface Directive #356 signal 1 requires (the forward noise source itself was already removed by #357's whole-run state isolation).

**Reviewer-reject reason-class vocabulary** (#361 / Directive #356 signal 3). When the three reviewer subagents (`issue-reviewer`, `plan-reviewer`, `activation-reviewer`) return a non-pass verdict (`refine`/`revise`/`reject`/`block`), the invoking skill flow emits a categorized audit record via the `reviewer_reject_audit` helper (`helpers/reviewer_audit.sh`): `audit_log warn <category> reject "class=<reason-class> issue=#<N>"`. The `<category>` is the reviewer's audit category тАФ `issue-review` (`/file-issue` тЖТ issue-reviewer), `plan-review` (`/work-on` тЖТ plan-reviewer), or `activation` (`/activate` and `/complete-directive`, which both drive activation-reviewer). These are **audit-emission** categories, **not** `SKIP_HOOKS` escape categories тАФ they are not reachable via `should_skip` and so are deliberately absent from the ┬з7 escape list (the `helper-missing`/audit-category set is a superset of the escape set). The `<reason-class>` is one of a small controlled vocabulary the skill maps the reviewer's free-text reason onto (nearest token): `schema-incomplete`, `unverifiable-ac`, `scope-bleed`, `mission-misfit`, `conflict`, `evidence-insufficient`. This produces the per-reviewer ├Ч reason-class trail that a promotion-candidate report (Directive #356 signal 4, a sibling Execution Issue) aggregates. The mapping is a skill-side judgment (the same free-textтЖТtoken summarization `/activate` already performs); the helper only formats and emits.

Tests are run by `/ship` (┬з5.7). During the draft PR's commit/push, only quick lint/format runs. A commit-time test gate would force WIP/share commits to escape every time, polluting the audit log тАФ so we don't add one.

**Lint timeout**: the commit-time lint invocation is bounded by `GHJIG_LINT_TIMEOUT` (seconds, default 30) so a misconfigured or slow linter cannot hang the commit. Timeout fires as a `block format` decision, escapable via `SKIP_HOOKS=format`. If neither `timeout(1)` (coreutils) nor `gtimeout(1)` is on `PATH`, the lint runs unbounded with an `audit_log warn lint-timeout-absent` entry (decision token `notice`) recording the missing dependency тАФ the hook neither hangs the user nor silently downgrades enforcement. `lint-timeout-absent` is an **audit-emission** category (like the reviewer-reject categories above), not a `SKIP_HOOKS` escape category, so it is deliberately absent from the ┬з7 escape list.

#### 6.1.1 Conditional issue # enforcement

| commit type | issue # required | Rationale |
|-------------|------------------|-----------|
| `feat`, `fix`, `docs`, `refactor`, `perf` | Required | External surface / behavior change |
| `test`, `style`, `build`, `ci`, `chore`, `revert` | Optional (passes without it) | Internal change |

Structural regex:
```
# required group
^(feat|fix|docs|refactor|perf)(\(#[0-9]+\))!?: .+$
# optional group (issue # optional)
^(test|style|build|ci|chore|revert)(\(#[0-9]+\))?!?: .+$
```

Subject length is measured in **codepoints (1..72)**. Byte-based measurement (`wc -c`, `${#var}`) is forbidden тАФ under multibyte locales it mis-truncates Korean/CJK. The choice of tool is an implementation detail.

**Subject extraction across `-m` forms**: the hook accepts both the plain quoted form and the command-substitution + heredoc form that the harness uses for multi-line bodies (`Co-Authored-By`, etc.).

| `-m` form | Subject |
|-----------|---------|
| `-m "feat(#1): subject"` / `-m 'feat(#1): subject'` | The quoted text (its first line) |
| `-m "feat(#1): subjectтПОтПОbody"` (embedded newlines, single `-m`) | The **first line** of the value only тАФ extracted from the **raw** command (whitespace normalization flattens the newlines, so a normalized-command parse would capture subject+body as one over-length blob) |
| `-m "subject" -m "body"` (multiple `-m`, git's multi-paragraph form) | The value of the **first** `-m` (not the last) |
| `-m "$(cat <<'TAG'` тАж `TAG)"` (heredoc body inside the `-m` value) | The first non-blank, non-tag line of the heredoc body тАФ **but only when the value's own first non-blank line is not already a valid Conventional-Commit subject** (line-1 precedence, below) |
| `-m "feat(#1): subjectтПОтПОтАжbody mentioning `<<EOF`тАж"` (normal body that merely contains a `<<TAG` token) | The **line-1 subject** тАФ a `<<TAG` appearing as prose in the body does **not** make it a heredoc message |
| `-F <file>` / `--file <file>` (no inline `-m`/heredoc message) | **Empty** тАФ the message lives in a file the hook cannot read; the format check is **skipped** (fail-open) |

The heredoc tag may be single-quoted (`<<'EOF'`), unquoted (`<<EOF`), or indent-stripping (`<<-EOF`); the extractor returns the first body line that is not blank and not the closing tag, leading whitespace stripped, before the Conventional-Commits regex runs.

**Line-1 precedence** (#383): the heredoc walk is entered **only when the `-m` value's first non-blank line is not itself a valid Conventional-Commit subject**. The genuine substitution form's first line is the `$(cat <<TAG` opener тАФ never a valid subject тАФ so it falls through to the heredoc body as before. But a plain single `-m` whose first line *is* a valid subject and whose body merely mentions a `<<TAG` token (common when the change is *about* shell/heredocs) returns line-1 directly, rather than mis-reading a body line as the subject. This is fail-safe: line-1 is returned only when it passes the Conventional-Commits regex, so a malformed line-1 always falls through to the existing over-extracting (block-leaning) behavior.

**Extraction is bounded to the `git commit` command and operates on the raw command** (before whitespace normalization): it scans from the `commit` token onward, so a heredoc or `-m` belonging to a **sibling** command in a compound invocation тАФ e.g. a `cat > file <<EOF тАж EOF` redirect or another tool's `-m` chained before the commit тАФ is never mistaken for the subject. A heredoc is treated as the subject **only** when it is the commit's own `-m "$(cat <<TAG)"` message value, not any heredoc elsewhere in the command line. python3 drives the primary parse; the legacy heredoc-walk + single-line `sed` is the fallback when python3 is absent (degrading toward the prior, over-extracting behavior тАФ which fails toward *blocking*, never toward letting a malformed subject through).

Implementations expose a single helper (`extract_commit_subject`) consumed by `pre_tool_use.sh`'s commit gate. An empty return (no `-m`/heredoc message in the commit segment) makes the gate skip the format check (fail-open); the gate only ever blocks a subject it positively extracted and found malformed.

### 6.2 PostToolUse тАФ supplementary

| Trigger | Action |
|---------|--------|
| After `Edit/Write/MultiEdit` | Auto-format the changed file with the detected formatter (failures don't block) |
| `Bash` matches `git commit` | Print a "remember to update the matching PR body checklist item" reminder (warn-only) |
| `Bash` matches `git push` | If a PR exists, check `gh pr checks` and notify the user |
| `Read` of a whole file (neither `offset` nor `limit`) above the line threshold (`GHJIG_READ_NUDGE_THRESHOLD`, default 200) | Nudge toward a targeted `Read --offset/--limit` or `explorer` delegation (warn-only, always `exit 0`). The positive narrowing affordance of ┬з1.8 тАФ a missed nudge is ignorable at no cost (┬з6.0 P1), so it guides, never blocks. Fires only inside a registered scope (the hook's `in_scope` gate) and only when `jq` is available. |

### 6.3 Stop тАФ recommendation after each response

Claude Code's `Stop` hook fires **after every model response**, not at session end. To avoid noise, suggest only once every N responses:

- uncommitted changes + no recent review тЖТ suggest `/review`
- recent commit + PR body checklist out of sync тЖТ suggest `/sync-pr`

Suggestions print one line to stderr (no blocking). Throttling is a simple modulo of N (default 5, overridable via `$GHJIG_STOP_THROTTLE`) тАФ no per-category state file.

Session-level cleanup (branch tidy, temp files) is a **deferred capability** (┬з0.4) тАФ neither a `SessionEnd` hook nor a `/wrap` command is specified or built today.

### 6.4 UserPromptSubmit тАФ context injection

Before each user message, inject the **compact status** as system context тАФ `status_compact` (`helpers/status.sh`, the same projection ┬з5.5 describes): current branch, the issue / PR one-liners, phase, `next:` hint, mode, shell-root, state, and work-lang. This is a small per-turn refresh, not a full context reload.

The heavier one-time injection тАФ the full current-PR body, the referenced-issue body, and the MISSION summary тАФ is **SessionStart's** job (┬з6.5(b) Session restore), loaded once when a session resumes in-scope, not re-injected every turn (CLAUDE.md is loaded whole natively by Claude Code, not part of this injection). Keeping the per-turn surface to `status_compact` is the narrowing half of the MISSION mechanism (┬з1, "as small and relevant as possible"); SessionStart selective-injection is the dual.

### 6.5 SessionStart тАФ shell sync check + session restore + SessionStart banner + friction advisory + SSOT-presence health

At session start, do five things:

**(a) Shell sync check**
- Is the shell repo behind origin/main? If so, warn (no auto-pull; sudden behavior changes are risky).
- The `git fetch` is gated by a stamp file at `.claude/state/last-shell-fetched`. The fetch runs only when the stamp is older than `SESSION_START_FETCH_TTL` seconds (default 21600 = 6 h) or absent. Most sessions therefore skip the network call тАФ the `git rev-list --count HEAD..@{u}` still runs against locally-known refs, so the "behind" warning is correct relative to whatever was last fetched (up to 6 h stale, which matches the warning's polite-not-critical role).
- The fetch is wrapped in `timeout $SESSION_START_FETCH_TIMEOUT` (default 5 s) so a hung network does not stall session startup. If `timeout(1)` / `gtimeout(1)` is unavailable the fetch runs unbounded, matching SPEC ┬з6.1 / `GHJIG_LINT_TIMEOUT`'s fallback pattern.

**(b) Session restore** тАФ to seamlessly resume the previous session, inject once:
- The current branch's full PR body (if any)
- Full referenced issue body (if any)
- Target `MISSION.md` head (`head -n 20 MISSION.md`)
- One `/status` snapshot

`.claude/CLAUDE.md` is **not** hook-injected here тАФ Claude Code natively loads it whole every session. Because it is an always-on injected surface it is held to the ┬з9 thin-pointer discipline + 12000-byte budget (smoke ┬з104).

Subsequent turns only refresh the short status summary from ┬з6.4.

**(c) SessionStart banner**

One silent-no-op state evaporates the ┬з0.1 enforcement guarantee with no operator signal: the runtime that hosts enforcement is missing. SessionStart surfaces it via a primitive inline `printf` stderr banner, debounced to one fire per session and independent of `hookrt.sh` / `audit_log` / `safe_source` (the runtime that is itself the missing piece).

**Inject-consistency banner тАФ removed (#318, Directive #311).** This banner is **gone**, not re-conditioned. Its premise died with the #312 binding: it fired when the shell-root env var (then `$GHJIG_SHELL_ROOT`; retired as an input by #537) was unset and `settings.local.json` was an injected symlink, warning "every hook will no-op". Post-#312 that is the **normal working state** тАФ a plain `claude` in an injected target resolves hooks via the per-project binding symlink `${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}/.claude/ghjig-root/...` and `session_start.sh` self-locates + exports `$GHJIG_ROOT` (┬з3.2.1), so enforcement is fully on. The banner only false-fired. And the *genuine* residual no-op (the binding symlink missing/broken тАФ and post-#537 no ambient env can substitute for it, ┬з3.2.1) is **structurally undetectable from SessionStart**: the SessionStart hook command itself traverses that binding (`settings.injected.json`), so a broken binding means `session_start.sh` never runs and the banner inside it can never fire тАФ the banner would sit behind the very link it claims to check. No condition can both detect the failure and execute in it; the honest fix is removal. The forward-looking detector lives at **launch** time instead: `bin/ghjig <dir>` warns (non-blocking) when an injected target's `.claude/ghjig-root` binding is missing/dangling, before `exec claude` тАФ it runs *before* the session and resolves the dir directly, so it is the one place that can surface the broken-binding no-op (#334, ┬з3.5).

**Registry-zeroed detector** (#502, Directive #498) тАФ the per-project scope-guard registry (`ghjig-state/registry.txt`, ┬з3.2.2) going **empty** silently turns ALL enforcement off, because the global `in_scope` gate fails open on an empty/absent registry (by design, ┬з3.2.2 / ┬з773). An audit found this *zeroing* is reachable by an innocuous single command тАФ `: > registry.txt`, `truncate`, or a flagless delete-then-touch тАФ and was previously **traceless**. `session_start.sh` now detects a **present-but-EMPTY** registry (the distinguishable "armed-then-disarmed" signal; an *absent* registry is the normal pre-registration / unregistered-cwd transparent case and does **not** fire) and emits the same once-per-session banner + an `audit_log warn registry-zeroed` record. The detector **mirrors the reader's back-compat resolution order** (┬з767, `cwd_guard.in_scope`/`path_in_scope`): when the per-project `ghjig-state/registry.txt` is **absent**, it stats the legacy shared `$GHJIG_ROOT/.claude/state/registry.txt` instead тАФ otherwise an empty *legacy-shared* file (the fallback the reader still consults) would silently disable enforcement while the banner stayed mute, the exact blind spot the detector exists to close (#554). **This is a ┬з1.4 decision, NOT a fail-openтЖТfail-closed flip:** the empty-registry transparency is the deliberate guardrail-not-sandbox posture (┬з6.1 Framing) and is unchanged тАФ the detector only makes the disarmed state **observable**, satisfying the "no enforcement-disable that is both innocuous-command-reachable AND traceless" bar. **Documented residuals (accepted, not closed):** (a) the redirect/`truncate` *write itself* is still un-gated at fire time (the ┬з6.1 destructive `find -delete`/`truncate`/`>` residual, #505) тАФ detection is at the *next* SessionStart, not real-time block; (b) the **binding-symlink repoint** тАФ repointing `.claude/ghjig-root` at an attacker-controlled tree with a neutered `hookrt.sh` disables the session and is **structurally undetectable from within** (this detector, like the whole SessionStart hook, is reached *through* the binding), extending the missing/dangling-binding residual above; the launch-time `bin/ghjig` check (┬з3.5) catches a missing/dangling binding but not a repoint-to-a-valid-but-neutered tree. Both residuals are the documented "anyone who can write `ghjig-state` / repoint the binding can bash around the hook" posture (┬з6.1 / ┬з7), not a new exposure.

**Hookrt-missing banner** (#37) тАФ the shell root resolved (self-location, ┬з3.2.1), but `.claude/hooks/hookrt.sh` is absent (corrupt checkout, conflict-stashed file, manual `rm`). Each of the 5 hooks has a primitive check for the runtime and emits a per-invocation WARN to stderr before silently exiting 0; that per-invocation line trains operators to ignore "WARN hookrt-missing" as background noise, exactly when they shouldn't. The banner is the once-per-session actionable signal layered on top of that per-invocation diagnostic floor.

- **Trigger**: the resolved `$GHJIG_ROOT` is non-empty **AND** `$GHJIG_ROOT/.claude/hooks/hookrt.sh` is absent.
- **Action**: emit one stderr line naming the failure mode (`hook enforcement OFF until restored`) and the concrete fix тАФ inspect tree state via `git -C $GHJIG_ROOT status`, then restore via `git -C $GHJIG_ROOT checkout -- .claude/hooks/hookrt.sh`. Non-blocking; SessionStart still exits 0 immediately after (no helpers can load without the runtime).
- **Idempotency**: a stamp file under `$TMPDIR/ghjig-banner-hookrt.${CLAUDE_SESSION_ID:-$PPID}` debounces to one banner per session. The `-hookrt` suffix is retained for stamp-name stability across sessions (it predates the #318 removal of the sibling inject-consistency banner).
- **Diagnostic floor**: the existing per-invocation WARN at `session_start.sh:23` (and equivalent at the other 4 hooks' bootstrap blocks) stays тАФ it is the script-grep-friendly log-scraper-stable diagnostic that survives the banner's stamp-creation failure modes (hostile `$TMPDIR`, low-disk). The banner adds operator-facing actionability without removing the diagnostic floor.
- **Position**: runs **after** the shell-root self-location (the trigger needs the resolved root, ┬з3.2.1) and **before** the `. "$hookrt"` source line at `session_start.sh:37` тАФ co-located inside the existing `if [ ! -f "$hookrt" ]` block, since it shares the trigger condition and immediate `exit 0` tail.

**Shell-root env banners** (#537) тАФ two arms in the same once-per-session, mkdir-stamp-debounced family, the observability half of the ┬з3.2.1 ambient-never-consulted contract (a clean cut with no deprecation shim needs a signal, not a shim):
- **Legacy/mismatched-ambient arm**: an ambient `GHJIG_SHELL_ROOT` is set, **or** an ambient `GHJIG_ROOT` differs from the self-located root тЖТ one stderr line: `GHJIG_SHELL_ROOT retired (#537): the ambient shell-root env is IGNORED тАФ hooks self-locate via BASH_SOURCE and export GHJIG_ROOT internally. Fix: unset the stale export (legacy var or mismatched GHJIG_ROOT) from your shell profile.` The stale export is functionally ignored on the hook path; this arm is what keeps that ignore from being silent.
- **Override-seam arm**: `GHJIG_ROOT_OVERRIDE` is set in a live session тЖТ one stderr line naming the active test-only seam and the tree hooks are loading from: `test-only seam active; hooks loading from <path>`.

Both arms are non-blocking observability surfaces, not gates.

**(d) Friction-candidate advisory** (#398, Directive #391)

This is the **trigger** that completes the deferred-positive-face loop of ┬з6.0 P3: the friction-candidate readers (`scripts/narrowing_candidates.sh`, `scripts/promotion_candidates.sh`, and the git-history reader `scripts/ceremony_candidates.sh` тАФ #401) plus the new `unattended-park` park-frequency signal (below) are aggregated into a **one-line, non-blocking advisory** so the shell surfaces its own accumulated friction without a human remembering to run a script. It is the always-on counterpart described in MISSION:16 ("the log becomes the channel through which the shell sees its own friction") тАФ a consumer wired to read the aggregate.

- **Face**: **positive, never a block** (┬з6.0 P1 тАФ a missed friction nudge is ignorable at no cost). It is a single advisory line pointing to `/audit` and the three reader scripts; it **never dumps** their output into context (MISSION:14 narrowing constraint тАФ the per-session surface stays a fixed-size pointer, not a variable-length report).
- **Trigger condition**: emitted only when the readers surface at least one above-threshold candidate cluster, **or** when the audit aggregate contains `unattended-park` records. When nothing clusters, **no line is emitted** (the advisory is falsifiable тАФ smoke ┬з105 pins both the fires-when-candidates and suppressed-when-none arms).
- **Cost control**: gated by a stamp at the `ghjig_state_dir`-resolved `.../state/last-friction-surfaced` (with the `$GHJIG_ROOT/.claude/state/...` fallback, parity with the ┬з6.5(a) fetch stamp). The compute runs only when the stamp is older than `SESSION_START_FRICTION_TTL` seconds (default 21600 = 6 h, sharing the ┬з6.5(a) sync-check cadence) or absent, so most sessions skip it. The reader invocation is wrapped in `timeout $SESSION_START_FRICTION_TIMEOUT` (default 3 s; unbounded fallback when `timeout(1)`/`gtimeout(1)` is absent, matching ┬з6.5(a)). The stamp is touched only after a successful compute.
- **Fail-open**: any error (missing/empty audit log, reader non-zero, absent script, timeout) degrades to **silence** тАФ the advisory never blocks, stalls, or fails session startup (SessionStart still reaches the prompt). It reads the per-project audit aggregate via `ghjig_state_dir` (keyed on `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR`, not cwd), so it runs **before** the `in_scope || exit 0` gate like the ┬з6.5(a) sync check.
- **Park-frequency line**: the `unattended-park` records (emitted by `ship_park_pr`, ┬з5.7.1) are read **directly** by the advisory тАФ neither candidate script matches a `warn`/`parked` record (`narrowing_candidates.sh` keys `event==escape`, `promotion_candidates.sh` keys `event==warn`+`decision==reject`), so park frequency is surfaced as its own grep, leaving both scripts untouched.
- **Ceremony-mismatch line** (#401, Directive #401): `scripts/ceremony_candidates.sh` is a **measure-first** reader (┬з6.0 P3). Unlike the two audit-log readers it mines **commit history** тАФ the ceremony signal (commit `type` + the DocтЖТTestтЖТCode phase arc + changed-file count) lives in `git log`, not `audit.jsonl`, and the Directive forbids adding an author-facing field to record it there. It groups commits by `#<issue>` and surfaces **both directions**: *under-ceremony* (a `feat` group spanning >1 file with no `test`/`docs` phase commit) and *over-ceremony* (a тЙе3-commit phase arc over a single file). It emits the same indented `тАж | тАж =N` cluster shape the advisory greps, so it adds **no new surface**, and it runs `git -C` against the project repo through the advisory's `timeout тАж || true` envelope so a non-repo cwd / missing base degrades to silence. **Honest limits** (surfaced, not corrected): a batched single-commit PR collapses the phase arc and can false-positive as under-ceremony; over-classification is only weakly detectable. **Measure-first**: it observes whether ceremony mis-sizing is real and recurring; hardening into a ┬з1.2 weight model or a relaxation gate is a deferred follow-up Directive **gated on this consumer's evidence** (the P3 born-advisory-then-harden order applied to the device's own roadmap).
- **Spec-drift line** (#462, Directive #455): `scripts/spec_drift_candidates.sh` is a fourth **measure-first** reader (┬з6.0 P3) joining the family. Like the ceremony reader it mines `git log` (not `audit.jsonl`): it greps `SPEC.md` for the repo paths it references, then flags **code-ahead drift** тАФ a commit that touched a referenced path **without** co-touching `SPEC.md` ("code moved, SPEC didn't"). It emits the same indented `тАж | тАж =N` cluster shape (`  <path> | drift-commits=N`), so it adds **no new surface**, and fails open (non-repo cwd / absent or empty `SPEC.md` / no candidates тЖТ a sentinel line, exit 0). **Detection only**: the three-way classification (spec-ahead / code-ahead-correct / code-wrong) and the user-gated SPEC correction are the sibling `/reconcile-spec` flow (┬з5.27). The reader **is wired into the advisory above** (#466): it joins the `_session_friction_advisory` reader set under the same `timeout` envelope + once-per-session `last-friction-surfaced` stamp, and when candidates exist the advisory line reports the outstanding **drift-candidate count** (`N spec-drift candidate(s)`) тАФ the once-per-session surface that makes the drift signal consumed without a human running the script. **Honest limits** (surfaced, not corrected): a batched commit touching both code and `SPEC.md` for unrelated reasons masks a real drift, and the path-token grep is coarse тАФ it over-surfaces by design, to **measure** the real signal before any reconciliation machinery is hardened.

**(e) SSOT-presence health line** (#460, Directive #454)

A once-per-session, zero-network glance at the target's SSOT presence тАФ the recurring counterpart to the one-time `/onboard` SSOT check, so a repo that drifts into (or was never given) a `SPEC.md` is re-surfaced each session rather than flagged only at adoption. `SPEC.md` is the **required behavioural SSOT** for any code-carrying repo (┬з1.3); this line keeps that expectation visible.

- **Single source**: the presence facts come from `scripts/lib/onboard_checks.sh --dry-run` (filtered to its `ssot:MISSION.md` / `ssot:SPEC.md` lines) тАФ **not** a reimplemented `[ -f SPEC.md ]` (┬з9 single-source; the same script `/onboard` and `setup.sh` consume).
- **No per-session `gh` call**: `--dry-run` short-circuits `onboard_checks.sh`'s `gh_usable()` **before** any `command -v gh`, so the path is purely filesystem (`ssot:*` are two `[ -f ]` facts). The gh-dependent checks (fork / permission / branch-protection) stay one-time in `/onboard` тАФ this surface is the cheap glance, not the full report.
- **Render**: both present тЖТ one unobtrusive line `SSOT: MISSION.md тЬУ SPEC.md тЬУ`; `SPEC.md` absent тЖТ a prominent **SPEC-first nudge** pointing the user to author it before other work (the shell scaffolds the slot from `.claude/templates/spec.md`, never authors the contract content тАФ the MISSION boundary).
- **Cadence тАФ every session, not TTL-debounced**: unlike the ┬з6.5(d) friction advisory (whose 6 h TTL debounces an *expensive* compute), the SSOT check is two stats, so it fires **every** session start to satisfy the "once per session" contract тАФ a nudge suppressed for 6 h would under-deliver it. It therefore lives in the in-scope section (alongside the ┬з6.5(b) branch banner, **after** `in_scope`), so it reports only for a registered target's cwd (no false "SPEC.md absent" in an arbitrary directory) and needs no second stamp.
- **Fail-open**: any error (script absent, unreadable output, indeterminate status) degrades to **silence** тАФ never blocks or stalls session startup.

### 6.6 Stack-aware behavior

`helpers/detect_stack.sh` picks an active stack for `/ship`'s test runner, the commit-time lint gate, and the PostToolUse formatter. Detection is by sentinel file at PWD:

| Stack | Sentinel | Test (used by `/ship`) | Lint (commit gate) | Format (PostToolUse) |
|-------|----------|------------------------|--------------------|----------------------|
| node | `package.json` | `npm test` (if `test` script) | `npm run lint` (if `lint` script) | `prettier --write` |
| python | `pyproject.toml` / `setup.py` / `requirements.txt` | `pytest` | `ruff check .` | `ruff format` or `black` |
| go | `go.mod` | `go test ./...` | `go vet ./...` | `gofmt -w` |
| rust | `Cargo.toml` | `cargo test` | `cargo check` | `rustfmt` |
| ruby | `Gemfile` | `bundle exec rspec` | тАФ | тАФ |
| godot | `project.godot` | `godot --headless тАж` (GUT if present, otherwise parse-only) | `gdlint .` (if installed) | `gdformat` (.gd) |

Notes for godot:
- Test: when `addons/gut/gut_cmdln.gd` is present, `/ship` invokes GUT via `godot --headless --path . -s res://addons/gut/gut_cmdln.gd -gexit`. Otherwise a parse-only check runs (`godot --headless --path . --quit-after 1`) тАФ confirms the project loads.
- Lint / format: `gdlint` and `gdformat` ship in the `gdtoolkit` PyPI package. Helpers only invoke them when on PATH; absence is silent (no false-positive block).
- Scene and resource files (`.tscn`, `.tres`, `.import`) are not auto-formatted тАФ they are editor-managed and any rewrite risks corrupting binary subresources.
- The C# variant of Godot (`project.godot` + `*.csproj`) still resolves to `godot` (script-level tooling). Mixed-language CI is the project's call, not the shell's.

**Formatter invocation safety**: `detect_format_cmd` shell-quotes the file path via `printf '%q'` before interpolating it into the returned command string. The PostToolUse hook can therefore safely `eval` the result тАФ filenames containing spaces, `;`, `$(...)`, backticks, or other shell metacharacters do not change the executed command. (PostToolUse is best-effort and silent on failure; SPEC ┬з6.2.)

A target with no recognized sentinel resolves to `unknown`; `/ship` reports "no test runner detected" but does not block. Adding a stack means extending `detect_stack` plus the corresponding `detect_test_cmd` / `detect_lint_cmd` / `detect_format_cmd` branches.

**Version-field location** (the ┬з18.2 release manifest-match preflight, #469, Directive #468): `detect_version` (in `helpers/detect_stack.sh`) is the **single-source** per-stack locator that reads the project's native version field, for a verification-only `/release` preflight тАФ the field is read, **never written** (write-back stays the shell's own `VERSION`, ┬з18.2):

| Stack | Version field |
|-------|---------------|
| node | `package.json` тЖТ `.version` |
| python | `pyproject.toml` тЖТ `[project] version` |
| rust | `Cargo.toml` тЖТ `[package] version` |
| go / ruby / godot | тАФ (no universal manifest version field тЖТ skip) |

An unrecognized stack, an absent manifest, or an unparseable field returns empty тЖТ the preflight **degrades to a graceful skip** (never a false block), mirroring `detect_stack`'s `unknown` fail-open. The locator lives only here; `/release` does not duplicate per-stack version knowledge (┬з9).

### 6.7 Local git-hook enforcement tier

The PreToolUse hooks of ┬з6.1 fire only on the *agent's* tool calls; a human at the terminal, an editor's git integration, or a script bypasses them entirely. This section adds a second **local** enforcement tier тАФ committed `.githooks/` adapters activated per-clone via `core.hooksPath` тАФ that extends the *same* checks to **any local git operation**, whoever the actor.

**Three-tier model** (ordered by breadth of actor coverage and bypass model тАФ the ┬з6.0 P2 physics rule):

1. **CC PreToolUse hook** (┬з6.1) тАФ fires on the agent's Bash/Edit/Write tool calls only, in-loop, before the action; the fast-feedback advice tier for work the agent drives.
2. **Local git-hook tier** (this section) тАФ fires on any local git op regardless of actor. Like tier 1 it is **advice, not authority**: it folds to `--no-verify` by design.
3. **Server-side ruleset** тАФ GitHub branch protection / rulesets, the non-bypassable authority covering all actors regardless of local state. This tier is a **deferred follow-up (┬з0.4), out of scope here** тАФ named only to close the model.

The tiers are complementary, not redundant: tier 1 covers only the agent, tier 2 extends the same checks to every local actor, and tier 3 is the unbypassable backstop neither local tier can be (┬з6.1 Framing тАФ a local hook is always bypassable).

**Reuse-only, single-source (invariant).** The adapters **source the existing `.claude/hooks/helpers/` functions and call them** тАФ they copy **no** check logic. No secret pattern, commit-subject regex, or `PROTECTED_BRANCH_PATTERN` is duplicated into `.githooks/`; the helper stays the one source (┬з9). A shared `.githooks/_lib.sh` holds the self-location + `safe_source` prelude every adapter sources first.

**Per-adapter reuse boundary:**

| Adapter | git input | Reuses | Blocks |
|---------|-----------|--------|--------|
| `pre-commit` | staged diff (`git diff --cached`) + current branch | `is_protected_branch` (branch_guard.sh) + `scan_staged_secrets` (secret_scan.sh) | a direct commit to a protected branch; a staged secret |
| `commit-msg` | the message-file **path** git passes as `$1` | `check_commit_subject` (conventional_commit.sh) on **line 1** of that file | a non-conventional commit subject |
| `pre-push` | one **stdin line per ref**: `<local-ref> <local-oid> <remote-ref> <remote-oid>` | `is_protected_branch` on each remote-ref (`refs/heads/` stripped) | a direct push to a protected ref |

- `commit-msg` does **not** use `extract_commit_subject` тАФ that helper parses a *command string*, and there is no command string at the git layer, only the message file git hands the adapter. It reads line 1 of that file and calls `check_commit_subject` directly.
- `pre-push` iterates **all** ref lines with a `while read` loop: a single `read` would inspect only line 1 and miss a violation on line 2+, so the loop is load-bearing, not stylistic.
- **Force-push coverage is by subsumption, intentionally.** The `pre-push` protected-name block **subsumes** the force-push-to-protected case тАФ a force-push to a protected ref is blocked *because the ref is protected*, the force nature being irrelevant. A force-push to a **non-protected** feature branch is a legitimate PR-branch rebase and is **allowed**, matching the tier-1 rule "force allowed to an explicitly-named non-protected branch" (┬з6.1 force-push row). There is therefore **no separate non-fast-forward detection facet** тАФ a deliberate design choice, not a coverage gap.

**Corollary тАФ the command-string matcher bug class cannot arise here.** Every git-hook input is git's own **structured data** тАФ the stdin ref tuples, the message-file path, the staged diff тАФ never a shell command string. The data-as-token / heredoc-segmentation matcher bug class the tier-1 command-string matchers must defend against (#366 / #403 / #446 / #476 / #605) therefore **cannot occur at this tier**. This is a second, independent reason the command-string helpers (`git_matcher.sh` `push_segments` / `strip_command_data`) are not reused: they solve a problem this tier does not have.

**Self-location.** `_lib.sh` resolves the shell tree via the ┬з3.2.1 binding-symlink idiom тАФ `GR="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/.claude/ghjig-root"` тАФ then sources `hookrt.sh` and `safe_source`s the needed helper. A **missing or dangling binding тЖТ exit 0**: this is an advice tier, so a broken shell link must never wedge the user's git. Each adapter pins its interpreter with `#!/usr/bin/env bash`.

**Evidence routing.** Under terminal context `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` is unset, so a plain `ghjig_state_dir` (via `audit_log`) would fall back to the legacy shared audit path. `_lib.sh` closes this by seeding `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` from the git top-level (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`) before sourcing `hookrt.sh` тАФ the same derive-from-top-level rule `ghjig_state_dir_cli` (hookrt.sh, #602) embodies тАФ so `audit_log`'s subsequent `ghjig_state_dir` resolves the target's per-project state dir and terminal-originated evidence lands in the per-project audit log, not the shared path (┬з3.2.2).

**`git config` is repo-local only.** Activation sets `core.hooksPath` with a **repo-local** `git config` тАФ **never** `--global`/`--system`. The shell never touches user-global state (┬з3.4 boundary); a per-clone repo-local setting reverts with a single `git config --unset core.hooksPath`.

**Fail-open honesty + drift detection.** `.githooks/` is *committed*, but activation is a per-clone `git config` тАФ a fresh clone has `core.hooksPath` **unset**, so the tier is **inert** until installed (a per-clone bootstrap gap). This gap is surfaced, not hidden: a **SessionStart drift arm** calls `scripts/install_git_hooks.sh --check` (mirroring the ┬з6.5(e) `onboard_checks.sh --dry-run` single-sourced-predicate idiom) and, when the tier is inert, emits a once-per-session advisory naming the installer. The arm must **detect**, not silently pass тАФ an unactivated tier that never says so would evaporate the coverage guarantee with no operator signal (the ┬з6.5(c) silent-no-op hazard).

**Bypass honesty.** State plainly: this tier **folds to `--no-verify`** by design. It is mistake-prevention / advice for the human, exactly as tier 1 is for the agent (┬з6.1 Framing) тАФ **not** authority. Anyone who intends to bypass can; the tier's job is to stop honest mistakes at the local layer for every actor. Authority stays with the deferred server-side ruleset (tier 3).

---

## 7. Escape hatch

Three forms, chosen by where the escape needs to be read. The **file-token channel** (below) is the **primary in-agent recourse**; the two in-command forms are verbatim-delivery forms (a real shell, the smoke harness) тАФ they do **not** land in-harness.

> **Observed caveat (this harness, 2026-06; the harness is a moving floor тАФ re-verify, ┬з1.9):** in the live Claude Code Bash tool **both** in-command forms are **stripped before the hook reads `tool_input.command`** тАФ the leading env-prefix is consumed as the spawned subprocess's environment, and the trailing sentinel comment is stripped too. The parsers are correct (they set the tokens when fed the literal string in isolation, e.g. the smoke harness), but the harness does not deliver either to the hook, so **neither in-command form takes effect in-harness** (#478). The working in-agent channel is the **file-based skip token** below (#479): it is written to per-project state and read by the hook *at fire time*, so the harness has nothing to strip. The **fallback** for a sanctioned in-agent guarded op remains a **real terminal** (no PreToolUse hook fires there) or doing the work on a non-protected branch and renaming.

**File-based skip token (primary in-agent channel, #479)** тАФ a one-shot, category-scoped token the hook reads at fire time from per-project state, so it survives the harness (unlike the two in-command forms above):

- **Location**: one file per category at `$(ghjig_state_dir)/escape/<category>.token` (per-project state dir, ┬з3.2.2; gitignored under `ghjig-state/`). Per-category isolation makes category-scoping **structural** тАФ a `branch.token` can only ever disarm `branch`.
- **Format**: `KEY=VALUE`, one per line, exactly these four keys тАФ `category`, `reason`, `cmd_fingerprint`, `created` (epoch seconds). **Strict allow-list parse**: an unknown key or a missing key тЗТ malformed тЗТ **not honored**.
- **Reader**: pure bash тАФ **no `python3`/`jq`** тАФ so there is no interpreter-absent failure mode; the reader is strictly fail-safe. It is integrated into `should_skip <cat>`: after the existing `$SKIP_HOOKS` check, `should_skip` consults `<cat>.token`. The hook exports `ESCAPE_BIND_CMD=$raw_cmd` (the current command) for the fingerprint check.
- **Honored only if ALL hold**: the file exists and is readable; all four keys present with no unknown keys; the `category` field equals the requested category equals the filename; `cmd_fingerprint` is non-empty **and a substring of the current command** (`ESCAPE_BIND_CMD`); `created` is numeric **and** `now тИТ created тЙд 60` (the **TTL**, 60 seconds); the bind-cmd is non-empty.
- **On honor**: `audit_log escape <category> skip "<reason>"` (parity with the `SKIP_HOOKS` escape audit) тЖТ **consume (delete) the token** тЖТ skip that one category.
- **One-shot / consume-on-read**: the token is deleted on honor **and** deleted on a stale/malformed reject (poison cleanup) тАФ a token never survives a `should_skip` call that examined it.
- **Fail-safe-to-block**: **any** doubt тАФ absent, unreadable, malformed, category-mismatch, fingerprint-not-a-substring, stale, future-or-non-numeric `created`, empty bind-cmd тАФ leaves enforcement **armed** (the matcher blocks). Never a spurious skip.
- **Binding weight (read this correctly).** The real AC-5 guards are **consume-once + the 60s TTL**: a token is single-use and self-expires. The `cmd_fingerprint` substring binding and the writer's min-length refusal are **footgun-reducers** тАФ they stop a *stale or pre-written* token from disarming an *unintended* command тАФ **not a security mechanism**. The threat model (┬з6.1) is unchanged: hooks are mistake-prevention, not a security boundary; anyone who can write `ghjig-state/` can `bash -c` around the hook, so **no crypto/signature is used or needed**. Choose a **high-entropy distinguishing** fingerprint тАФ the commit subject / version / branch name тАФ **not** a bare verb like `git commit`.
- **Writer affordance**: `scripts/ghjig_skip.sh <category> <cmd_fingerprint> [reason]` тАФ the fingerprint is **required** (it refuses to write without one, and refuses a fingerprint shorter than 8 chars as a footgun-reducer); the **category** is interpolated into the token path, so it is constrained to `^[A-Za-z0-9,_-]+$` тАФ a value outside that charset (e.g. a `../`-traversal attempt) is refused with no token written (#551); the write is atomic, per-category, under `ghjig_state_dir` (the writer resolves the same project dir the hook reads тАФ deriving it from the git top-level when `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR` is unset for a Bash-tool subprocess тАФ so writer and reader always agree, #483). The Write tool to `$(ghjig_state_dir)/escape/<cat>.token` (e.g. `.claude/ghjig-state/escape/<cat>.token`) is a documented **fallback** writer (the `.claude/` Edit/Write carve-out, ┬з6.1).
- **Bash-only boundary (R1, by design тАФ not an oversight).** The channel works only on the **Bash** tool path, where `ESCAPE_BIND_CMD=$raw_cmd` is set. The **Edit/Write** protected-branch arm has **no command string**, so it cannot carry a token and the in-agent escape does **not** cover Edit/Write тАФ consistent with ┬з5.0 step 2, which already routes the bootstrap MISSION/README authoring through a Bash `cp` precisely because "there is no command string to carry [a sentinel]."

The two in-command forms below remain defined (they land verbatim in a real shell and the smoke harness); they are no longer the in-agent recourse.

**Trailing sentinel** тАФ read from the trailing edge of the raw command:
```bash
<command>  # ghjig:skip=<category>[,<category>...] reason=<reason>
```

**Leading env-prefix** тАФ read from the leading edge of `tool_input.command`; works only where the prefix arrives *inside* the command string (a real shell that passes it verbatim, and the smoke harness):
```bash
SKIP_HOOKS=<category>[,<category>...] SKIP_REASON='<reason>' <command>
```

The PreToolUse hook parses the leading `SKIP_HOOKS=тАж`/`SKIP_REASON=тАж` tokens from the leading edge of `tool_input.command`, **and** a `# ghjig:skip=тАж reason=тАж` sentinel from the trailing edge of the raw command. Two forms exist as defense in depth across execution environments where one or the other arrives verbatim (a real shell, the smoke harness). **In the live Claude Code Bash tool, however, neither lands in `tool_input.command`:** the leading `VAR=val` is consumed as the spawned subprocess's own environment (the hook subprocess does not inherit it either тАФ ┬з6.1), and the trailing `#`-comment is **stripped before the hook reads the command** too тАФ so in-harness the recourse above (real terminal / non-protected branch + rename) applies, not these in-command forms. Both forms export the recognized tokens into the hook before downstream matchers run, then strip them from the command for the matcher pass (so a `reason=` containing a blockable substring cannot bleed into another matcher); **if both are present, the leading form wins.** Recognized tokens: `SKIP_HOOKS`/`SKIP_REASON` (leading) and `ghjig:skip=`/`reason=` (trailing) only тАФ any other ALLCAPS `K=V` leading token (`PATH=`, `LD_PRELOAD=`, тАж) halts the leading scan and is left as an ordinary argument. The sentinel is parsed from the **raw** command before whitespace-normalization (the normalization + `shlex` pass would otherwise mangle the `#`), is namespaced (`ghjig:skip=`) so an ordinary trailing comment is never mistaken for an escape, and is **one-shot** тАФ it travels with the single command, so there is no persistent bypass state. The sentinel is honored **only when its `#` is a genuine unquoted shell comment token** тАФ a `#` that the executed shell itself treats as the start of a comment. A `#` sitting inside a quoted argument (e.g. `gh pr comment 5 --body "see note # ghjig:skip=all reason=x"`) is argument text, not a comment: the shell runs the whole command intact, so the hook must **not** read it as an escape (doing so would let ordinary quoted text тАФ a commit message, a PR-body paste, audit output quoting the sentinel тАФ silently disarm every matcher with a falsified audit reason). The comment-token boundary is resolved with the same `python3`/`shlex` machinery the leading env-prefix uses; if `python3` is absent the trailing sentinel is **not** honored тАФ a fail-safe no-op (enforcement stays armed), never a spurious skip. The sentinel must sit on the command's **final line** (the match is confined to a single line via `[[:blank:]]`/non-control-char classes plus a newline guard) so a line-1 sentinel can never strip or disarm a dangerous *later* line тАФ such a command falls through to the matchers and blocks. **Scope:** like the leading env-prefix, the trailing sentinel is **command-scoped** тАФ it disarms its named category (or `all`) across **every** line/clause of the command, not only the line it sits on. It remains **category-scoped**: a tail sentinel naming category X does not disarm a category-Y matcher (that command still blocks). So an `escape` audit record proves *which* category was skipped with a stated reason тАФ read it as "category X was skipped for this command," not "this exact line was approved"; the reason text need not describe the specific operation disarmed. When run in a real terminal where neither form reaches a hook (there is no PreToolUse hook outside the harness), the command simply runs; the escape only matters when a hook is in the path.

Categories:
- `all`
- **eng-flow hook matchers:** `secret`, `branch`, `commit-format`, `format`, `force-push`, `amend`, `no-verify`, `destructive`, `sensitive`, `out-of-scope`, `backmerge`, `ac-closeout`, `merge-strategy`, `push-parity`, `merge-review`
- **type-aware / dir-mode hook matchers (┬з6.1):** `proposed-protect`, `trusted-filer-mutate`, `label-parent-consistency`, `initiative-readonly`, `directive-close`
- **command-level reviewer-gate escapes:** `directive-review` (the `activation-reviewer` gate on `/file-directive` / `/activate` / `/revise-directive` / `/complete-directive` / `/consume-initiative`, ┬з4.9/┬з5.10тАУ┬з5.22), `release-review` (the `code-reviewer` gate on `/release`, ┬з5.20)

This list is the complete set of `SKIP_HOOKS` categories the runtime honors (the hook matchers via `should_skip <cat>` in `pre_tool_use.sh`; the reviewer-gate escapes via the command/skill prose). It is kept in sync with the matchers/commands by the doc-consistency smoke check (┬з17 / #267) тАФ a new `should_skip <cat>` or reviewer-gate escape that is not listed here fails smoke.

**Audit parity for the reviewer-gate escapes.** The hook-matcher escapes are audit-logged by `should_skip`, which emits `audit_log escape <cat> skip "<reason>"` on the skip path. The command-level reviewer-gate escapes (`directive-review`, `release-review`) are **not** read by any PreToolUse hook тАФ no `should_skip` fires for them тАФ so the escape record is not auto-emitted. To keep the "every skip is recorded" guarantee true for these prose-enforced escapes, the command that honors `SKIP_HOOKS=directive-review` (`/file-directive`, `/activate`, `/revise-directive`, `/complete-directive`, `/consume-initiative`) **must itself emit** `audit_log escape directive-review skip "<why>"` (sourcing `hookrt.sh` first) on the bypass path тАФ parity with the `should_skip` escape audit. A reviewer-gate escape doc that claims "audit-logged" without carrying this emission instruction is a broken guarantee (┬з17-enforced).

(`issue-ref` is folded into `commit-format` тАФ not a separate category. `format` is the commit-time lint/format gate. `out-of-scope` covers paths outside the registry (┬з6.1). `backmerge` covers `git merge <protected-base>` on a feature branch (┬з6.1). `ac-closeout` covers `gh pr merge` when a linked issue has unchecked AC and no `^## AC closeout` comment тАФ see SPEC ┬з6.1 row + ┬з5.7.1 step 7.6 for the rule (step 7.5 is the unrelated checklist audit); `scripts/ac_closeout.sh <pr-num>` is the canonical fixer. `merge-strategy` covers `gh pr merge` to the default branch without `--merge` тАФ see SPEC ┬з6.1 row + ┬з5.7.1 (squash erases the DocтЖТTestтЖТCode arc on the trunk); squash is allowed on a non-default base. `push-parity` covers `gh pr merge` while the local branch is strictly ahead of its pushed remote head (unpushed commits, git-only, #244) and `merge-review` covers `gh pr merge` lacking a passing GitHub review pinned to the current head тАФ skipped, stale-head, or an outstanding CHANGES_REQUESTED (#586, #543) тАФ see SPEC ┬з6.1 rows + ┬з5.7; `merge-review` is `bypass`-toggleable per ┬з5.7.1 (`push-parity` is not). Tests are run by `/ship`, not a hook, so there's no `tests` category.)

Every skip is recorded in `.claude/audit/audit.jsonl`:
```json
{"ts":"2026-05-19T...","event":"escape","decision":"skip","category":"format","reason":"flaky lint JIRA-1234","cwd":"...","source":"live"}
```

The `reason` and `cwd` fields are JSON-encoded via `jq -Rs .` (or an inline `\n`/`\r`/`\t`/`\\`/`\"` escape when jq is absent). Newlines and control characters in `SKIP_REASON`, and shell metacharacters in PWD (legal in POSIX paths), therefore do not break the "one JSON object per line" invariant тАФ every `audit.jsonl` is parseable by `jq -c '.'` regardless of input contents. Other fields (`event`, `category`, `decision`, `ts`, `source`) are internal-constant or RFC 3339-shaped and need no encoding (`source` is the `live`/`test` enum, ┬з6.1).

Policy:
- Skips should be temporary.
- A skip with no `SKIP_REASON` is logged as `unspecified` тАФ review target.
- `all` is for emergencies.
- A category that gets skipped repeatedly means the hook is misconfigured тАФ open a fix PR.

Audit logs rotate as appropriate (exact threshold is an implementation choice), but the diff body is never written тАФ only path, line, category metadata.

---

## 8. Directory structure (final)

This tree is **authoritative and drift-guarded by smoke ┬з103**: the flat leaf-list directories (`agents/`, `commands/`, `helpers/`, `docs/`) are count-checked against disk, so a PR that adds or removes one of those files must update this block in the same PR. `templates/` and `scripts/` carry summarized subtree nodes (their leaves churn independently); the guard asserts those subtree nodes are present rather than counting their leaves. Regenerate this block when the flat-dir contents change.

```
GHJig-Claude/
тФЬтФАтФА README.md
тФЬтФАтФА README.ko.md
```
