```
тФВ   тФЬтФАтФА install_git_hooks.sh          тЖР sets repo-local core.hooksPath to .githooks/; --check verifies activation (┬з6.7, ┬з5.1, ┬з6.5)
тФВ   тФЬтФАтФА lint.sh                       тЖР pinned+SHA256-verified shellcheck; per-file lint + Linux peak-RSS flag (┬з11, #545)
тФВ   тФЬтФАтФА lint_bash_idioms.sh           тЖР born-advisory, non-gating bash idiom checker; reuses lint.sh's shellcheck + policy greps (┬з4.5.1, #546)
тФВ   тФЬтФАтФА migrate_v3.sh
тФВ   тФЬтФАтФА narrowing_candidates.sh       тЖР clusters escape records тЖТ narrowing candidates (┬з6.0 P3)
тФВ   тФЬтФАтФА onboard_target.sh
тФВ   тФЬтФАтФА promotion_candidates.sh       тЖР aggregates reviewer-reject classes тЖТ advisoryтЖТhook promotion candidates (┬з6.0 P3)
тФВ   тФЬтФАтФА spec_drift_candidates.sh      тЖР clusters code-ahead code-vs-SPEC drift тЖТ measure-first candidates (┬з6.0 P3, ┬з6.5(d))
тФВ   тФЬтФАтФА register.sh                   тЖР register / inject a target (┬з3.2.1, ┬з3.6)
тФВ   тФЬтФАтФА release_consolidate.sh        тЖР consolidates changelog fragments (┬з5.20, ┬з18)
тФВ   тФЬтФАтФА release_verify.sh             тЖР post-merge tag+Release-notes verify (read-only, fail-open; ┬з18.2)
тФВ   тФЬтФАтФА setup.sh                      тЖР single host-side entry: deps тЖТ register/clone тЖТ onboard pre-flight тЖТ dir-mode gate (┬з3.5)
тФВ   тФЬтФАтФА setup_project.sh
тФВ   тФЬтФАтФА lib/                          тЖР shared script libs: audit_log_path, detect_bare_refs_directive, dir_mode_project_resolve, inject, resolve_parent_directive, self_register
тФВ   тФФтФАтФА test/
тФВ       тФФтФАтФА smoke.sh                  тЖР smoke suite (┬з16 verification; numbered ┬з-sections)
тФВ
тФЬтФАтФА workspace/                        тЖР .gitignored body
тФВ   тФЬтФАтФА .gitkeep
тФВ   тФФтФАтФА README.md
тФВ
тФФтФАтФА docs/                             тЖР 7 thin-pointer digests (┬з9); count-guarded (smoke ┬з103)
    тФЬтФАтФА CONFIG.md
    тФЬтФАтФА DIR_MODE_FLOW.md              тЖР dir-mode flow digest
    тФЬтФАтФА ENGINEERING_FLOW.md           тЖР flow diagram + step details
    тФЬтФАтФА ESCAPE_HATCH.md
    тФЬтФАтФА HARNESS_OVERLAP.md            тЖР harness-overlap classification pointer (┬з1.9)
    тФЬтФАтФА SUBAGENTS.md                  тЖР eleven-agent usage guide
    тФФтФАтФА TROUBLESHOOTING.md            тЖР common blocks + fixes
```

---

## 9. Template specifications

Each `.claude/templates/` file is read by a command and variable-substituted at use time. Single source of truth.

**`docs/*.md` and `.claude/CLAUDE.md` are thin pointers, not parallel content.** The human-facing `docs/*.md` digests (e.g. `ENGINEERING_FLOW.md`, `DIR_MODE_FLOW.md`, `SUBAGENTS.md`) exist as a readable on-ramp to a SPEC section тАФ they must **lead with a "Full details/spec in SPEC ┬зX" reference and carry no parallel or detailed contract content** that could silently drift from the SPEC. SPEC is the single source; a digest that restates a contract becomes a second copy to keep in sync by hand (the divergence hazard ┬з1.3's single-file principle exists to prevent). Smoke enforces the lead-with-a-SPEC-reference rule (┬з91). When a digest would need detail to be useful, link to the SPEC section instead of duplicating it.

The same discipline binds `.claude/CLAUDE.md`. Unlike the `docs/*.md` digests, `.claude/CLAUDE.md` is an **always-on injected surface** тАФ Claude Code natively loads it whole every session тАФ so it must point to SPEC for contract detail and carry no detailed contract content that could drift. It is held to a size budget: `wc -c .claude/CLAUDE.md` must stay **тЙд 12000 bytes** (drift-guarded by smoke ┬з104). The always-on injected floor is task-independent context loaded before any task is known, so an unbounded always-on surface is "bloat past the task" (MISSION:20); keeping `CLAUDE.md` a thin pointer-index is the always-on counterpart to ┬з6.4's per-turn `status_compact` narrowing.

### 9.1 `mission.md` (draft for target's `MISSION.md`)

Draft body for a target's `MISSION.md`, offered by `/onboard` (┬з5.1) and `/bootstrap-repo` (┬з5.0) when absent; authoritative body in `.claude/templates/mission.md` (substitutes `{{ today }}`). Fixed sections: `## What this exists for` (one paragraph тАФ what breaks without this project), `## Success looks like` (3тАУ5 observable metrics/scenarios), `## Explicitly NOT goals`, `## Stakeholders`, `## Last reviewed:`. The shell scaffolds the slot; it never authors the contract content (┬з5.1).

### 9.2 `issue.md`

Draft body for `gh issue create`, enforced by `/file-issue` (┬з5.2); authoritative body in `.claude/templates/issue.md` (no substitution vars). Fixed sections: `## What`, `## Why` (names the `MISSION.md` item/metric served), `## Acceptance criteria` (тЙе1 verifiable `- [ ]` condition), `## Out of scope`, `## Notes`. The MISSION reference, acceptance criteria, and a priority are the ┬з5.2 rationale-triad `issue-reviewer` gates on.

**Title principle.** The issue title states the issue's need as **explicitly and simply as possible** тАФ a plain problem statement. Because a GitHub artifact is the shell's durable-memory substrate (MISSION), the title is the primary index into the issue as a record for recall/triage, so it should read as a *problem*, not a *change*. It is **NOT** a commit/PR subject: the `<type>(#N):` conventional-commit form (┬з10.2 commits, ┬з10.3 PR titles) is **not** used for issue titles тАФ that form conflates the change with the problem, and a leading `#N` reads as a spurious parent-directive indicator. This is a **guiding norm, not a rigid format and not a hard lint/gate** тАФ free-form titles remain fine; only the clarity principle and the anti-commit-form note are stated (the `feat(#570):`-style drift on #575/#573 is the motivating anti-pattern). No title lint or `issue-reviewer` title block is added; a soft advisory nudge is a possible future harden only if drift recurs.

### 9.3 `pr_body.md`

Draft body for `gh pr create --body-file`, authored by `/work-on` (┬з5.3) and curated as the PR-as-living-doc (┬з1.4); authoritative body in `.claude/templates/pr_body.md` (substitutes `{{ closes_or_refs }}`, `{{ issue }}`). `{{ closes_or_refs }}` becomes `Closes` (single or final PR) or `Refs` (intermediate PR) per ┬з10.3 тАФ `/work-on` defaults to `Closes`, the user adjusts on split. Sections тАФ Goal, How this serves the mission, Plan, Alternatives considered, Key context, Checklist, Out of scope, Risks, Open questions, Decisions, Test plan, Docs touched, Ship gate тАФ and who fills each are the ┬з9.3.1 contract below.

#### 9.3.1 Section owners

| Section | Filled by | When |
|---------|-----------|------|
| `{{ closes_or_refs }} #<N>` | `/work-on` (default `Closes`), user adjusts on split | PR create / split decision |
| Goal | `/work-on` (one-line summary of issue title, user confirms) | PR create |
| How this serves the mission | planner | PR create |
| Plan | planner | PR create |
| Alternatives considered | planner (mandatory; forced-choice acceptable) | PR create |
| Key context | planner + (if needed) explorer enrichment | PR create / during work |
| Checklist | planner (Doc/Test/Code order) | PR create / ticked during work |
| Out of scope | planner | PR create |
| Risks | planner | PR create |
| Open questions | planner | PR create / all resolved before merge |
| Decisions | main assistant (`/adr` auto-links ADRs) | during work |
| Test plan | test-writer | Phase B |
| Docs touched | doc-writer | Phase A |
| Ship gate | fixed (template); `/ship` verifies and ticks | PR create / `/ship` |

### 9.4 `adr.md`

Draft body for an Architecture Decision Record, authored by `/adr` for irreversible decisions; authoritative body in `.claude/templates/adr.md` (substitutes `{{ number }}`, `{{ title }}`, `{{ today }}`, `{{ pr }}`). Fixed sections: a header (`# ADR {{ number }}: {{ title }}` + Date / `Status` / Context PR lines), `## Context`, `## Decision`, `## Alternatives considered` (each with why-rejected), `## Consequences`, `## Notes`. `Status` follows the lifecycle `Proposed` тЖТ `Accepted` тЖТ `Superseded by ADR-<M>` (the file seeds `Proposed`). Linked from the PR body `## Decisions` section (┬з9.3).

### 9.5 `pr_template_for_target.md`, `issue_template_for_target.md`

Standard templates the target repo can install into `.github/`. `/onboard` suggests these when absent.

The shell repo **dogfoods its own scaffold** (#320, SPEC ┬з17): `.github/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md` is `pr_template_for_target.md` with the leading install-hint HTML comment stripped тАФ so a human/web-UI PR against the shell opens with the same Doc/Test/Code + Ship-gate checklist the shell mandates everywhere else. Smoke asserts the two stay in sync (the PR template equals the target template minus its comment line), so an edit to one without the other fails CI. (The `/ship` skill path is unaffected тАФ it authors PR bodies from `pr_body.md` via `gh pr create --body-file`; the GitHub template only scaffolds manual PRs.)

### 9.6 `directive.md`

Read by `/file-directive` (┬з5.10) and variable-substituted into a Directive Issue body; the body is then reviewer-gated by `activation-reviewer` (┬з4.9.1). Fixed section set (every section required): `## Objective` (must name a concrete artifact-level boundary тАФ file paths / issue counts / AC ticks / merge events, not "improve" without a target), `## Success signals` (2тАУ5 objectively-testable conditions), `## Non-goals` (тЙе2 explicit exclusions), `## Constraints` (тЙе1 invariant to preserve), `## MISSION fit` (names the `MISSION.md` section/criterion served), `## Priority` (`P0`/`P1`/`P2`/`P3`, default `P2`), `## Confidence` (0тАУ100). The `priority=P<N>` value feeds the `directive-file/created` audit record validated by `_audit_validate_format` (`hookrt.sh`).

### 9.7 `spec.md`

Draft for a target's `SPEC.md`, copied by `/bootstrap-repo` (┬з5.0) and suggested by `/onboard` (┬з5.1) when absent. Substitutes `{{ project }}`. Ships a machine-generated **Table of contents** block (the START/END markers `build_toc.sh` regenerates) followed by a broad section skeleton тАФ `## 1. Overview`, `## 2. Contracts`, `## 3. Non-goals` тАФ that the target grows section-by-section. Carries the single-file-SSOT guidance in its header blockquote (consult the ToC, `Read --offset` the section; split into a per-subsystem directory only when the file grows too large to read whole).

### 9.8 `readme_for_target.md`

Draft for a target's `README.md`, copied by `/bootstrap-repo` step 2 (┬з5.0). Substitutes `{{ repo_name }}`. Sections: a one-paragraph description, `## Status` (records the stage-0 bootstrap + the `/onboard` next step), `## Getting started` (build/run/test, filled as the project takes shape), `## Documentation` (links to `MISSION.md` and the rest of the SSOT set).

---

## 10. Convention summary

### 10.1 Branch naming

```
<gh-username>/<type>/[<issue#>-]<slug>

# required-issue-# group (feat/fix/docs/refactor/perf) тАФ always includes <issue#>-
ilgyu/feat/42-oidc-login
ilgyu/fix/57-null-pointer
ilgyu/docs/89-update-architecture

# optional group (chore/style/build/ci/test/revert) тАФ issue # may be omitted
ilgyu/chore/typo-readme
ilgyu/chore/89-update-deps    тЖР if an issue exists, you can include it
```

Types: `feat | fix | docs | style | refactor | perf | test | build | ci | chore | revert`

`/work-on <issue#>` always has an issue, so it always includes `<issue#>-` regardless of group. Issueless ad-hoc branches in the optional group are created by the user with plain `git checkout -b`.

### 10.2 Commit messages

```
<type>(#<issue>)[!]: <subject тЙд 72 chars>

<body тАФ one blank line>

Closes #<N>     тЖР last commit, or single-PR consolidator
Refs #<N>       тЖР intermediate commit
Co-Authored-By: Claude <noreply@anthropic.com>   тЖР optional trailer; toggleable
```

Phase prefixes:
- `docs(#42): describe OIDC callback flow`
- `test(#42): add failing tests for /auth/oidc/callback`
- `feat(#42): implement OIDC callback handler`

**Co-Authored-By trailer toggle**: the `Co-Authored-By: Claude тАж` line is a convention, not a contract. It is included by default but can be disabled per-target. Resolution priority (high тЖТ low, mirroring SPEC ┬з5.7.1's mode pattern):

1. `$GHJIG_COAUTHOR` env var (`on` / `off`).
2. `.claude/state/coauthor` per-target file (one of `on` / `off`, no other content).
3. Default `on`.

Unknown values fail-safe to `on` and emit a stderr warning naming the offending source. The helper `.claude/hooks/helpers/coauthor.sh` exposes `coauthor_trailer` (prints the line when enabled, empty when disabled); `/work-on`'s commit template sources it. The line is **version-agnostic** тАФ `Co-Authored-By: Claude <noreply@anthropic.com>`, with no model version (#294) тАФ so it never re-drifts at a model bump (it was previously pinned to `Opus 4.7` and went stale once the model advanced to 4.8). The toggle covers the default behavior of `/work-on` flows only тАФ the trailer remains free to be added or omitted manually in any specific commit.

**`ghjig_commit` slot-assembly helper** (Issue #436; ADR-0002 GO target): the positive-enforcement face (┬з6.0) of the commit-subject contract тАФ the agent *fills slots* instead of hand-rolling `git commit -m "<type>(#N): тАж"`. `.claude/hooks/helpers/ghjig_commit.sh` exposes `ghjig_commit <type> <issue> <subject> [body-paragraphтАж]`: it assembles `<type>(#<issue>): <subject>`, validates it via `check_commit_subject` (format + 1..72 codepoints) **before** committing тАФ on rejection it errors `ghjig_commit: тАж` with a nonzero rc and **does not commit** (the failure surfaces with full context, not as an opaque post-hoc hook block). It then commits via a **bash argv array** `git commit -m "<subject>" -m "<body-para>"тАж ` (one `-m` per body paragraph, `coauthor_trailer` appended as a final `-m` when enabled):

- The **first `-m` carries only the assembled subject**, so the `commit-format` matcher *sees and accepts* it on the happy path тАФ `ghjig_commit` does **not** rely on the `-F` fail-open bypass (git's `-m`/`-F` are mutually exclusive anyway, and an `-F`-only commit makes the matcher extract an empty subject and skip the check тАФ a bypass, not a guarantee).
- The **array argv** (no `eval`, no string re-quoting) makes multibyte and multi-paragraph bodies round-trip losslessly тАФ the inline-`-m` quoting pitfall is a string-construction hazard, absent when argv is assembled programmatically.

**Offered, not forced**: `ghjig_commit` is positive guidance with the `commit-format` hook retained as the mandatory net (┬з6.0 P4); skills *offer* it (e.g. `/work-on`'s commit step) but the hand-roll path remains valid. The caller passes the `Closes #N` / `Refs #N` trailer as a body paragraph (the trailer choice is base-dependent, ┬з10.3/┬з10.5 тАФ the caller's decision, not the helper's).

**Relationship with Conventional Commits (conscious choice)**: we reuse the standard CC `scope` slot for the issue # marker. Consequences:

- Passes default `commitlint` rules (with `(#42)` allowed in scope).
- Tools like `conventional-changelog` / `semantic-release` parse `(#42)` as scope, so changelog scope columns will show `#42`. We don't carry both a domain scope (e.g. `auth`) and issue # тАФ issue # wins.
- If a domain scope is essential, put it in the commit body via a `Scope: auth` trailer.

### 10.3 PRs

- Always start as draft.
- `Closes #N` or `Refs #N` is required. If a single issue spans multiple PRs, intermediates use `Refs #N` and the final uses `Closes #N`. Checklist distribution is planner/user's call.
- **Base**: PRs default to `main`. For experimental or long-lived feature work, `/work-on --base <branch>` opens the PR against an alternate base тАФ see ┬з10.5. Non-`main`-base PRs default to `Refs` (the issue closes only when the work reaches `main`).
- Body follows `.claude/templates/pr_body.md`.
- Curate the body right after each commit.
- `/ship` transitions to ready after ship-gate verification.

### 10.4 PR тЖФ checklist sync

Order: **commit тЖТ PR body update**. Commit is the fact; PR body reflects it. Reverse order creates "checklist ticked but commit absent" states. Refetch the remote body right before updating тАФ abort the auto-update if external edits (reviewer, GitHub UI, parallel session) are detected.

### 10.5 Topic-branch workflow

The default flow (`/work-on <#>`) targets `main`. For two scenarios the user can opt into an alternate base via `/work-on <#> --base <branch>`:

1. **Experimental work** тАФ risk too high for `main`. The user creates `experiment/foo` from `main`, iterates with a few PRs whose base is `experiment/foo`, and only consolidates to `main` via one final PR when the experiment stabilizes (or abandons the branch).
2. **Big features** тАФ a multi-PR refactor where the integration point is a long-lived feature branch. Sub-task PRs target the feature branch; the feature branch itself is eventually merged to `main`.

**Conventions:**
- Sub-task PRs use `Refs #N` (not `Closes #N`) so the issue stays open until work reaches `main`. `/work-on` enforces this default for non-`main` bases.
- The alternate base must already exist locally + remotely. `/work-on --base <branch>` does NOT auto-create it; the user creates the base deliberately (e.g. `git checkout main && git pull && git checkout -b experiment/foo && git push -u origin experiment/foo`).
- The alternate base's remote branch-protection settings are the user's responsibility. For sub-task PRs to auto-merge into `experiment/foo`, the GitHub branch-protection rules on `experiment/foo` must permit the same flow as `main` (or be more permissive). `/work-on` does not inspect or modify remote settings.
- The alternate base is NOT in SPEC ┬з6.1's protected list (`main`/`master`/`release/*`). The user is free to commit directly to `experiment/foo` between sub-task PRs тАФ it's an integration point, not the canonical product line.
- The work-branch name (`<gh-user>/<type>/<#>-<slug>`) is unchanged. Stacking multiple work-PRs on the same issue+base is not supported by `/work-on` alone тАФ manual branch creation (`git checkout -b ...`) is the escape hatch for that rare case.

**Use with Directives (dir-mode integration):** scenario 2 ("Big features") is the canonical pattern for Directive-scoped multi-PR work (┬з1.7, ┬з2.1). The user creates a topic branch from `main` (e.g., `feature/directive-92`); each Execution Issue parented under the Directive (via `/file-issue --parent <directive-#>`, ┬з5.2) runs `/work-on <execution-#> --base feature/directive-92`, producing sub-task PRs with `Refs #N`. The Directive Issue itself is **not** branched тАФ the `proposed-protect` matcher in ┬з6.1 blocks `git checkout -b` against a Directive Issue (any status), by design; the Directive scopes the work, the Execution Issues do the work. Consolidation follows the standard pattern (one final PR head=topic-branch, base=`main`, body `Closes` each Execution Issue), and `/ship`'s Directive-aware audit (┬з5.7) fires once per parented Execution Issue at consolidation. `/complete-directive <directive-#>` (┬з5.13) must run **after** consolidation тАФ `activation-reviewer` (┬з4.9) evaluates closed-Execution-Issue evidence, so running completion while the topic branch is still unconsolidated yields insufficient-evidence and blocks.

**Consolidation back to `main`:** when the topic branch is ready, open ONE PR with head=`experiment/foo` and base=`main`, body `Closes #<#>`. This is a regular `gh pr create` invocation тАФ `/work-on` is not designed for the consolidator step (the branch already exists; there's no planner phase to repeat).

**Enforcement тАФ the bare-`Refs`-to-default anti-pattern (#337):** the convention above requires that directive-scoped work reach the default branch via a PR that `Closes` an Execution Issue; a PR that merges to the default branch carrying only bare `Refs #N` (empty closing set) leaks the work тАФ no Execution Issue closes, so the dir-mode post-merge reflection chain never fires and the parent Directive gets no progress record (the historical #92 failure: PRs #100тАУ105 merged to `main` with bare `Refs`, no `Closes`). The **post-merge workflow** (`.github/workflows/dir-mode-post-merge.yml`, ┬з5.15) enforces this: on a merged PR whose base is the **live default branch** AND whose `closingIssuesReferences` is **empty** AND whose body carries тЙе1 `Refs #N` resolving (via the same depth-2 label-aware climb as the reflection resolver, #335) to a **directive-scoped** issue (a Directive, or an Execution Issue parented under one), it posts a single idempotent **warning comment on the merged PR** (marker `<!-- bare-refs-warning pr=#N -->`) naming the violation and the recovery (re-open + `Closes` an Execution Issue, or run `/reflect <pr>`). It is **warn-only** тАФ the merge already happened, so there is no block point тАФ and **fail-soft** (any `gh` resolution failure тЖТ no warning, never aborts the workflow). The check lives in the post-merge **workflow**, not a PreToolUse hook, deliberately: the #92 violations were predominantly human GitHub-UI merges, which a `gh pr merge` hook structurally never observes; the merge-triggered workflow fires regardless of who merged. The detection logic is a sourced, smoke-tested helper (`scripts/lib/detect_bare_refs_directive.sh`) with the same three-copy cmp-locked discipline as the resolver.

---

## 11. CI awareness

- **Right before** ready transition: `gh pr checks --json state` for a one-time check. **Block only on `failure` or `cancelled`**. `pending` / `in_progress` / `queued` pass тАФ the background watch picks up monitoring after ready transition. (┬з5.7 step 7)
- **Right after** ready transition: `gh pr checks --watch` runs in **background**, returning immediately.
- The background watch's failure detection routes to a PostToolUse hook (┬з6.2) notification.
- The post-push PostToolUse hook (`Bash` matching `git push`) also warns about PR-less push patterns (detached HEAD, missing draft PR).

This shell repo ships its own CI workflow at `.github/workflows/ci.yml` running on `pull_request` and `push: main`. The `syntax` and `smoke` jobs run on an OS matrix of `ubuntu-latest` and `macos-latest` (the BSD branch is the production path for the primary user; Linux-only CI would leave it unverified); the `mutation` job (┬з11.1) runs on `ubuntu-latest` only (its logic is platform-independent; the matchers themselves are covered per-OS by `smoke`):
- **syntax** тАФ `bash -n` AND `shellcheck --severity=warning --shell=bash` over `bin/ghjig`, `scripts/*.sh`, `scripts/lib/*.sh`, `.claude/hooks/*.sh`, `.claude/hooks/helpers/*.sh`. Repo-wide silences (e.g. SC1090 for dynamic sourcing via `BASH_SOURCE`-relative paths and per-test fixture variables) live in `.shellcheckrc`; documented-deliberate patterns (`eval` on jq-emitted `@sh` scripts in `helpers/status.sh`, `printf -v` to dynamic varname in `helpers/escape.sh`) carry inline `# shellcheck disable=SCтАж` with one-line justification. Both the enumeration and the invocation live in **`scripts/lint.sh`** тАФ the CI `syntax` job runs `./scripts/lint.sh`, and a developer runs the **same** script locally, so "clean locally" and "clean in CI" are one predicate by construction (the local-pre-image-of-remote-gate discipline, ┬з7.4/┬з18.6). shellcheck is **version-pinned** (`GHJIG_SHELLCHECK_VERSION`, currently `0.11.0`) and resolved reproducibly: `scripts/lint.sh` downloads the pinned `koalaman/shellcheck` release tarball for the host OS/arch (`curl --retry 3 --retry-all-errors`) and **SHA256-verifies it fail-closed** (hard error on mismatch/absence тАФ never runs an unverified binary) against a per-platform checksum table (linux.x86_64, linux.aarch64, darwin.x86_64, darwin.aarch64 тАФ the CI matrix legs plus the common local-dev platforms). The pin is **end-to-end**: both the release tarball *and* the extracted binary (the artifact actually executed) carry pinned hashes, and the binary hash is re-checked on **every cache hit** тАФ so a tampered, pre-seeded, or truncated cached binary is discarded and re-fetched rather than run (the "never runs an unverified binary" invariant holds on the warm path, not just the cold download; #549 review). The cache lives under a per-user root (`$RUNNER_TEMP` in CI, else `$XDG_CACHE_HOME`/`$HOME/.cache`) тАФ never a predictable world-writable `/tmp` path a co-tenant could pre-seed. The floor is `тЙе0.10.0` (first release shipping a `darwin.aarch64` asset тАФ `macos-latest` runners are arm64). In CI the download is wrapped in `actions/cache` keyed on version+os+arch so a green run does not re-fetch from the release CDN on every run (CDN flake would otherwise be red-CI-that-is-not-a-code-defect тАФ the non-reproducible signal this section exists to kill). **Memory guard** (the pre-#539 combined `shellcheck "${files[@]}"` run peaked ~18 GB RSS on the 13.7k-line `scripts/test/smoke.sh` and OOM-killed the ubuntu runner as an illegible "runner received a shutdown signal"): shellcheck is invoked **per file** (bounds peak RSS at the single largest file; `.shellcheckrc` sets `external-sources=true`+`source-path=SCRIPTDIR`, but following is scoped to files carrying an explicit `# shellcheck source=` directive тАФ only the `scripts/test/smoke.d/` sections do, #600 тАФ so per-file invocation still loses no meaningful cross-file analysis elsewhere), and on Linux the per-file pass is measured under `/usr/bin/time -v` and peak RSS is checked against a documented fraction of runner memory тАФ a **non-fatal flag** that surfaces an approaching-limit regression legibly (a single file creeping toward the cliff) *without ever failing CI*: the former per-file baseline (~12 GB, dominated by the pre-split `scripts/test/smoke.sh`) sat close to any runner-safe budget, so a hard exit would risk the exact false-red this section exists to kill (post-split #600 the per-file peaks are a few hundred MB, but the non-fatal posture stands). The combined-pass regression is instead gated by the smoke structural lock (┬з11.1-adjacent, `scripts/test/smoke.sh` ┬з138) тАФ and would OOM the runner before `/usr/bin/time` could report anyway. **Per-file split (#600):** the dominant file, `scripts/test/smoke.sh`, itself grew past the point where its *own* shellcheck peak (~20 GiB RSS at ~16k lines) OOM-killed the ubuntu runner тАФ the per-file split bounds peak at "the single largest file," but that file had become larger than the runner. The suite is therefore physically split into a thin orchestrator (`scripts/test/smoke.sh`) plus sourced section files under `scripts/test/smoke.d/` (each bounded well under the runner budget); they are `source`d into **one process**, so pass/fail semantics, shared state, and cross-section ordering are byte-identical to the former flat file (a pure code-move `refactor`). Each section file is shellcheck-linted again тАФ the interim #599 `sc_exempt` smoke.sh exemption is **removed**. Because the RSS flag is non-fatal (and OOMs before it can report), a **deterministic per-file line-count ceiling** (a reproducible, un-flakeable proxy for the RSS cliff) is the hard gate that fails CI if any single linted shell file crosses it, catching the next growth before an OOM. `.shellcheckrc` carries `external-sources=true` + `source-path=SCRIPTDIR` so the section files' `# shellcheck source=_preamble.sh` directive resolves the shared `ok`/`ng`/globals (scoped to files that carry the directive). A hard `ulimit -v` address-space cap is likewise *not* used тАФ it caps virtual address space, not RSS, so it false-reds legitimate runs.
- **smoke** тАФ installs `jq` (apt-get on Linux; pre-installed on macOS) and runs `./scripts/test/smoke.sh`.
- **mutation** тАФ runs `./scripts/test/mutation.sh`, the enforcement-matcher kill-rate guard (┬з11.1).

`fail-fast: false` on the matrix so per-platform failures surface independently.

### 11.1 Enforcement-matcher mutation harness

The smoke suite asserts that the enforcement matchers *behave* correctly; it does not, on its own, prove those assertions actually **kill** a regression тАФ a silently-weakened matcher could still pass a smoke assertion that no longer exercises the weakened path. `scripts/test/mutation.sh` closes that gap by measuring the smoke suite's **kill-rate** on the critical matchers (#423): it is the systematic, generalized form of the ad-hoc falsifiability premise-locks the suite already carries (the ┬з357 live-sink lock; the ┬з65i release-subject lock).

For each critical matcher the harness applies one **mutation** тАФ a weakened redefinition *appended* to a throwaway **git-worktree copy** of the tree (append-override: bash takes the last definition, so no fragile in-body edit) тАФ then runs the full smoke suite in that worktree (the worktree's smoke copy **self-locates** to it тАФ ┬з3.2.1; the harness sets no shell-root env), and asserts smoke **fails** (exit тЙа 0 тАФ the mutant is *killed*). A **surviving** mutant (smoke still green under a weakened guard) is reported as a harness failure: it means the matcher is no longer pinned by any assertion. The git worktree isolates the mutation from the parent working tree and is removed after each case, so the harness never mutates the live tree.

The seeded mutations (extensible) target the matchers whose wrong-*allow* cost is highest (┬з6.0): `check_commit_subject` тЖТ always-accept (commit-format), `scan_staged_secrets` тЖТ always-clean (secret), `PROTECTED_BRANCH_PATTERN` тЖТ never-match (protected-branch). Per ┬з6.0 this is the cost-asymmetry rationale made testable тАФ the same matchers whose negative gate fails safe toward blocking are the ones whose test coverage most needs a kill-rate proof.

So `/ship`'s `gh pr checks` step has something concrete to watch for on PRs against this repo. Other repos that adopt the shell can copy the workflow as a starting point.

---

## 12. Operational decisions (locked)

| Item | Decision |
|------|----------|
| Workspace structure | Inside the shell repo's `workspace/` by default; external paths registerable via `scripts/register.sh` |
| Scope of application | Only inside `workspace/` (cwd guard). External paths via registered symlinks count the same. |
| User-global impact | None (`~/.claude` left alone) |
| Enforcement level | "Strong enforcement; escapable on conscious choice." No policy is set in stone. |
| Hosting | GitHub (gh CLI) |
| Fork usage | None (upstream-only) |
| Quickfix path | Partially absorbed via issue-#-optional types (`chore`/`style`/`build`/`ci`/`test`/`revert`). External surface changes still need an issue. |
| Phase order | Strict for `feat`/`docs`/contract changes. `fix`/`refactor`/`perf`/spike use the ┬з1.2 relaxations. |
| Test gate | `/ship` runs tests right before ready transition. Draft commit stage is fast lint/format only. |
| Amend policy | Local amend allowed; amend after push blocked. |
| CI watch | `/ship` runs background watch. |
| Subagent calls | `planner` + `code-reviewer` default; others trigger- or explicit-call. |
| Operating mode | Default `attended` (stop at PR-ready). `unattended` is opt-in via ┬з5.7.1's resolution priority and continues `/ship` to merge or park. |
| Merge strategy | `gh pr merge --merge --delete-branch` (no-ff merge commit). Preserves the Doc тЖТ Test тЖТ Code commit graph on `main` and anchors each PR with a merge commit. See ┬з5.7.1 "Merge mechanism". |

---

## 13. Failure modes and recovery

| Situation | Handling |
|-----------|----------|
| Issue body is ambiguous | `/work-on` refuses to start; asks the user to clarify the issue |
| Phase A reveals the spec was wrong | Strike through the checklist with reason, re-invoke planner |
| Phase B test passes accidentally | Two branches: (a) Phase A spec is weak or test inputs insufficient тЖТ strengthen doc/test. (b) Adding a regression test for already-implemented behavior is legitimate тЖТ note in one line in PR body and proceed. Don't always restart from doc. |
| Base (main or `--base` target) advances during work | `git pull --rebase origin <base>` тЖТ resolve conflicts тЖТ re-push PR. The base is whatever the PR's `baseRefName` is тАФ read via `gh pr view --json baseRefName` if uncertain. Do NOT `git merge <base>` into the feature branch тАФ the ┬з6.1 `backmerge` matcher blocks that motion specifically to keep feature branches rebase-clean (escape `SKIP_HOOKS=backmerge` exists for exceptional cases but should be rare). |
| Another contributor touches the same branch | `--ff-only pull`, escalate to user on conflict |
| Can't finish in one PR | Intermediate PRs use `Refs #N`, the final uses `Closes #N` |
| Issue acceptance criteria change mid-work | Update the issue body + comment with the change log; mirror in the PR body |
| CI fails while local passes | `/ship` blocks. CI logs first, then hotfix commit + re-push |
| Hook misfires | Use escape hatch + audit it + file a fix PR for the hook |
| Same escape category repeats in audit | Sign the hook is wrong тАФ fix PR takes priority |

---

## 14. Security / sensitive items

- Direct editing of `.env`, `credentials.*`, `*.pem`, `id_rsa*`, etc. is blocked by hook.
- Pattern detection over staged diff for known secret formats (AWS, GitHub tokens, GitLab tokens, OpenAI/Anthropic keys, Slack tokens, password literals, etc.).
- Shell repo audit logs never contain secrets тАФ the diff body is not written to the log.
- bootstrap checks `gh auth status`. Claude creates issues/PRs under the human's name, so commits include a `Co-Authored-By` trailer.

---

## 15. (removed)

Operating decisions are documented in their respective sections in the body. No duplicate index here.

## 16. Build order (recommended)

When starting from an empty directory:

1. Directory skeleton + `.gitignore`. The shell repo's `.gitignore`:
   ```gitignore
   workspace/*
   !workspace/.gitkeep
   !workspace/README.md
   .claude/audit/
   .claude/state/
   ```
   The `workspace/` directory itself is tracked via `.gitkeep`; clones and symlinks inside are ignored, except for the explanatory `workspace/README.md`. `.claude/audit/` is the legacy shared audit log; `.claude/state/` holds legacy shared caches + the back-compat registry floor. Post-#314/#316 the per-project audit, caches, and registry live under `ghjig-state/` (┬з3.2.2), resolved via `ghjig_state_dir()` / `ghjig_registry_file`. `.claude/settings.local.json` exists only on the target side (as a symlink slot), so it's not in the shell repo's `.gitignore`.
2. `.claude/audit/` and `.claude/state/` empty dirs with `.gitkeep` тАФ at runtime the legacy shared `audit.jsonl` (audit/) and registry floor (state/) land here; the per-project equivalents land under `ghjig-state/` (┬з3.2.2).
3. `.claude/templates/*` first тАФ every command and agent consumes these.
4. `.claude/CLAUDE.md` тАФ shell norms (a summary of ┬з1, ┬з2 of this document).
5. `.claude/agents/*` (eleven of them).
6. `.claude/hooks/helpers/*` тАФ the full set is enumerated canonically in ┬з8 (the count is drift-guarded by smoke ┬з103; do not re-list here). `git_matcher` must precede `branch_guard` тАФ branch_guard sources it for the `PROTECTED_BRANCH_PATTERN` SSOT.
7. `.claude/hooks/{pre_tool_use, post_tool_use, stop, user_prompt_submit, session_start}.sh`.
8. `.claude/settings.json` тАФ registers the hooks above.
9. `.claude/commands/*` тАФ the full set is enumerated canonically in ┬з8 (count drift-guarded by smoke ┬з103; do not re-list here). The original core (onboard, file-issue, work-on, sync-pr, status, review, ship, adr, audit) came first; dir-mode / initiative / discussion / changelog / flush / bootstrap commands were layered on later.
10. `bin/ghjig` wrapper тАФ including the auto-register prompt for unregistered external paths.
11. `scripts/bootstrap.sh`, `scripts/clone-into.sh`, `scripts/register.sh` (sharing inject logic via a helper).
12. `scripts/test/smoke.sh` тАФ single-entry-point reproduction of the clone-into тЖТ /onboard тЖТ /file-issue тЖТ /work-on тЖТ D-T-C cycle тЖТ /ship simulation (┬з17's primary verification).
13. `docs/*`, `README.md`.
14. Run the smoke test once to confirm passing.
15. First-commit the shell repo on itself (bootstrap exception). All subsequent commits self-enforce the flow. **The same first-commit exception applies to target repos** via `/bootstrap-repo` (┬з5.0): a brand-new target with no default branch (empty repo / unborn HEAD reporting `main`) cannot make its seed commit ride a flow that presupposes a prior commit, so stage-0 makes the seed commit through the scoped, audit-logged `branch` escape. Both cases are the same chicken-and-egg, and both keep the bypass visible in `audit.jsonl`.

---

## 17. Verification checklist (does it meet the spec?)

All of the following must be yes before operating.

- [ ] `ghjig` works inside `workspace/`; hooks pass transparently outside it.
- [ ] Direct commits/pushes to protected branches are blocked by hooks.
- [ ] Force push is blocked by hooks.
- [ ] Commits without Conventional Commits + issue # are blocked.
- [ ] Secret patterns in staged diffs are detected and blocked.
- [ ] `--amend` (after push) and `--no-verify` are blocked.
- [ ] Dangerous commands (`rm -rf` with out-of-registry args, `git reset --hard`, `git clean -f`) are blocked.
- [ ] Edit/Write whose target path is outside any registry entry is blocked.
- [ ] Edits to `.env`, `*.pem`, `credentials*` are blocked.
- [ ] Shell installation and operation leave no changes in user-global state like `~/.zshrc` (┬з3.4).
- [ ] PostToolUse auto-formats changed files with the detected formatter.
- [ ] UserPromptSubmit injects a PR body + issue body + status summary into context.
- [ ] SessionStart warns when the shell repo is behind origin/main.
- [ ] `/onboard` checks fork status, push permission, MISSION presence, `.github/`, branch protection.
- [ ] `/file-issue`, `/work-on`, `/sync-pr`, `/status`, `/review`, `/ship`, `/adr`, `/audit` all behave as intended.
- [ ] The eleven subagents are defined; planner produces a Doc тЖТ Test тЖТ Code checklist.
- [ ] `.claude/templates/*` is the single source of truth for every command.
- [ ] The escape hatch works for every block category and is recorded in the audit log.
- [ ] The shell repo can develop itself on this same flow (dogfooding).
- [ ] `bootstrap.sh` self-registers the shell repo in its own per-project `.claude/ghjig-state/registry.txt` via `ghjig_registry_file "$SHELL_ROOT"` (idempotent тАФ ┬з3.6, #316).
- [ ] `register.sh "$SHELL_ROOT"` skips the `workspace/` symlink-loop and skips `inject_into` while still registering the path and ensuring the committed `.claude/ghjig-root -> ..` self-symlink (idempotent тАФ ┬з3.6, #539).
- [ ] The smoke scenario (clone-into тЖТ /onboard тЖТ /file-issue тЖТ /work-on тЖТ D-T-C cycle тЖТ /ship simulation) is reproducible via a single call to `scripts/test/smoke.sh`.
- [ ] Shell assets that conflict by name with the target's existing `.claude/agents/<name>.md` or `.claude/commands/<name>.md` are not injected; only a warning is printed.
- [ ] Local amend passes; amend after push is blocked.
- [ ] `feat`/`docs` commits require issue #; `chore`/`style` etc. pass without it.
- [ ] Draft PR commit/push runs only fast lint/format; tests run when `/ship` runs them right before ready transition.
- [ ] Right before a PR body update, the remote body is refetched; conflicts with external edits abort the auto-update.
- [ ] Commit subjects pass the codepoint 1..72 range. A 72-codepoint Korean subject is not falsely truncated.
- [ ] `ghjig <path>` triggers the auto-register prompt when called with an unregistered external path.
- [ ] A monorepo subproject's own `.claude/` is left untouched by the shell.
- [ ] `shellcheck --severity=warning --shell=bash` is clean across all shell sources on both CI matrix legs (`ubuntu-latest`, `macos-latest`); `.shellcheckrc` records intentional silences and inline `# shellcheck disable=` carry per-line justifications (┬з11).
- [ ] `gh pr merge` is blocked when a linked issue (`closingIssuesReferences`) has unchecked AC items and no `^## AC closeout` comment; `scripts/ac_closeout.sh <pr-num>` satisfies the gate idempotently and is invoked by `/ship` step 7.6 (┬з6.1).

---

## 18. Release backbone

Locks the shape of how releases happen: per-PR fragment files, one consolidator skill (`/release`), and a templated CI gate. Adopters consume the substrate via `/onboard-dir-mode` (┬з18.6). Established by Directive #128; depends on the VERSION + tag surface from Directive #122 (┬з3.5).

### 18.1 Fragment contract

The release line consumes per-PR **changelog fragments** under `changelog_unreleased/<category>/<N>.md`:

- `<category>` тИИ {`added`, `changed`, `deprecated`, `removed`, `fixed`, `security`} тАФ the six [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/) categories. Each is a subdirectory under `changelog_unreleased/`.
- `<N>` is the issue or PR number that introduces the fragment (positive integer; filename stem).
- The fragment body is a **single-line markdown bullet** (one line starting with `- `).
- The bullet **must contain `(#<N>)`** where `<N>` matches the filename stem. CI rejects mismatches (┬з18.6).
- **No YAML frontmatter, no multi-paragraph prose, no nested headers inside the fragment.** The contract is intentionally minimal тАФ the directory is the category, the filename is the PR/issue link, the bullet is the user-facing line.

`changelog_unreleased/TEMPLATE.md` documents the contract for fragment-authors in project-neutral language. The template ships in the shell and `/onboard-dir-mode` installs it (along with the six empty category subdirectories) into adopting repos.

`/release X.Y.Z` (┬з5.20) consolidates all present fragments into a new `## [X.Y.Z] тАФ YYYY-MM-DD` section in `CHANGELOG.md` at repo root, grouped under Keep-a-Changelog category subheadings, and deletes the consumed fragments in the same commit.

### 18.2 Version of record

The canonical version-of-record is the top-level `VERSION` file (locked by Directive #122 / ┬з3.5). `/release X.Y.Z`:

- Validates `X.Y.Z` is semver 0.x (`MAJOR=0`).
- Strips any `-dev` suffix from `VERSION`.
- Writes `X.Y.Z` to `VERSION`.
- Falls back to `git describe --tags` for **resolution-time queries only** тАФ never for write-back. The file is authoritative on `main`.

Multi-file version-of-record (`package.json`, `Cargo.toml`, `pyproject.toml`) is deferred. A documented extension point тАФ `.claude/release-config.json` тАФ is **reserved** at this location for projects whose VoR lives elsewhere; the file is currently unimplemented and the reservation prevents the name from being claimed by something else.

**Manifest-match preflight** (verify, not write-back; #469, Directive #468): while multi-file VoR *write-back* is deferred, `/release` runs a **verification-only** preflight тАФ it resolves the detected stack's version field via `detect_version` (┬з6.6) and **refuses** (non-zero, naming both the manifest version and the `X.Y.Z` being cut, with the fix: bump the manifest) when they contradict, so a release cannot tag a version the project's own manifest does not reflect. This is the **confident-mismatch** arm only; an unknown stack / absent or unparseable field is the **uncertain** arm and degrades to a graceful skip with a note (never a false block тАФ the diverse-project posture, ┬з6.0 cost-asymmetry). The manifest is **read, never written** тАФ write-back remains `VERSION`-only. Stack-aware bump *automation* is an explicit deferred non-goal (Directive #468).

### 18.3 Trunk branch model

Default development line is `main`. `/release` operates on `main` unless `--base <branch>` targets a maintenance branch (e.g., `0.3-maintenance`). Maintenance branches are **not auto-created by the shell** тАФ adopters who need LTS lines create them manually. See ┬з10.5 for the topic-branch / alternate-base flow.

The CI fragment-gate (┬з18.6) targets `main` and `*-maintenance` by default; configurable per project at workflow-install time.

### 18.4 Tag format

Tags follow `v` + semver 0.x тАФ `v0.1.0`, `v0.2.0`, etc. Locked by Directive #122 (CLOSED); preserved verbatim here so downstream tooling reads one canonical clause. Tag-freshness is **not** enforced as a merge gate per #122's non-goal тАФ tag-state drift is drift, not breakage. `/release` creates the tag (`gh release create vX.Y.Z --target <merge-sha>`) at the release-PR merge boundary; pre-merge release-PRs are tagless.

### 18.5 Non-goals

Locked by Directive #128 (closed):

- **No `/prepare-release` skill.** VERSION's `-dev` suffix replaces the scope-locking ceremony of a prepare PR.
- **No `/changelog-check` *lint* skill.** CI workflow + optional local hook arm cover the *validation* surface; a manual re-validation skill is a third redundant surface. This forbids a skill that **re-checks** an existing fragment's shape тАФ it does **not** forbid an **authoring** affordance: `/changelog` (┬з5.23) *writes* a fragment or applies the `skip-changelog` label and delegates all validation to the CI gate (┬з18.6), and the `/ship` pre-ready arm (┬з5.7, step 7.7) is exactly the "optional local hook arm" sanctioned in this clause. Authoring the artifact plus one in-flow presence check of the single contract is permitted; re-validating that contract a second time is not.
- **No tag-push merge gate, no tag-freshness enforcement** (preserves Directive #122's explicit non-goal).
- **No automated maintenance-branch creation, no backport / port-PR flow.** Deferred to a successor Directive when at least one adopter requests LTS.
- **No release-please / external-service integration.** The shell ships a ~30-line CI script under shell control. Adopters who already use release-please keep it; the shell does not displace it but also does not configure it.
- **No automated distribution** (npm, PyPI, Docker, Homebrew, binary upload). Per-project extension surface.
- **No release cadence enforcement.** When to cut a release is a human / per-project call.
- **No breaking-change policy enforcement.** Shell stays at `0.x` per #122 (`MAJOR=0` invariant); downstream projects at `1.x+` define their own compat policy.
- **No multi-file version-of-record bump.** `VERSION` is canonical; `.claude/release-config.json` is reserved but currently unimplemented.
- **No fragment frontmatter or template enforcement beyond filename/PR-number consistency.**
- **No major-rollover archive logic.** Shell stays at `0.x` per #122; revisit when `1.0.0` is on the table.
- **No retroactive per-milestone CHANGELOG entries** for pre-`v0.1.0` history. The inaugural section covers `init..v0.1.0` as one block, not split per historical sub-milestone.

### 18.6 Cross-project surface

`/onboard-dir-mode` installs the release-backbone substrate into adopting target repos as part of its tier-3 PR:

- `.github/workflows/check-changelog.yml` тАФ the per-PR fragment-gate workflow.
- `changelog_unreleased/TEMPLATE.md` + the six empty category subdirectories with `.gitkeep` placeholders.

The workflow validates the following rules on every PR targeting a protected branch (`main` and `*-maintenance` by default). Rule 1 is a presence check; rules 2тАУ4 are applied to **every** added fragment, and if **any** added fragment fails the gate fails тАФ a single valid fragment does **not** mask a malformed sibling (the all-valid contract, matching `scripts/release_consolidate.sh`):

1. The PR diff adds at least one file under `changelog_unreleased/<category>/<N>.md` where `<category>` is one of the six Keep-a-Changelog subdirectories.
2. The filename stem `<N>` is a positive integer.
3. The file contains `(#<N>)` where `<N>` matches the filename stem.
4. The bullet begins with `- ` (the single-line markdown bullet form, per `changelog_unreleased/TEMPLATE.md`).

Failure (no fragment, malformed filename, mismatched PR ref, or a non-bullet line) blocks the PR with an error referencing this section. Rules 2тАУ4 mirror `release_consolidate.sh`'s fragment validation so the per-PR gate and the release-time validator enforce one contract rather than diverging.

**`skip-changelog` opt-out**: a PR labeled `skip-changelog` bypasses the fragment check. The label is auditable on the PR; the workflow logs its application. Intended for PRs with no observable end-user behavior change тАФ pure docs-fix typos, dependency-only chores, internal refactors. **PRs carrying the label produce no fragment and are not represented in the eventual CHANGELOG section** тАФ by design, since there is nothing for a user to read about. Workflow trigger events include `labeled` and `unlabeled` so the opt-out re-runs the check.

Adopters consume the backbone with zero in-repo configuration beyond the substrate install plus their own `VERSION` file and a `CHANGELOG.md` at repo root. `/release X.Y.Z` runs against any repo where these three artifacts are present.

**Workflow does not self-trigger on its own landing PR**: per [GitHub's `pull_request` security policy](https://docs.github.com/en/actions/using-workflows/triggering-a-workflow#using-event-types), workflows modified inside a PR do **not** run on that PR (otherwise a fork could exfiltrate secrets via a self-modified workflow). The first PR after `check-changelog.yml` lands on `main` is the first empirical observation of the fragment-gate; the landing PR itself only validates the workflow's structure via smoke ┬з66c-e + the `code-reviewer` walk-through. Adopters running `/onboard-dir-mode` see the same: the substrate-install PR opens the workflow but the workflow fires from the next PR onward.

### 18.7 Skip criterion (the `skip-changelog` decision)

Every PR satisfies the fragment gate (┬з18.6) one of two ways: it **adds a fragment**, or it carries the **`skip-changelog`** label. Which one applies is a content judgment, and this clause is its SSOT тАФ `changelog_unreleased/TEMPLATE.md`, the `/changelog` skill (┬з5.23), and the `/ship` pre-ready arm (┬з5.7) reference this criterion rather than restate it:

- **Fragment required** when the PR changes user- or adopter-observable surface: a behaviour/contract change, a CLI/API/schema/protocol change, a SPEC contract change, or anything that alters how someone uses or integrates the project.
- **`skip-changelog` eligible** when the PR has no such surface: an internal `refactor` with unchanged external behaviour, `test`-only, `chore`/`build`/`ci`, `style`, or a docs-internal edit that changes no contract.

When in doubt, write the fragment тАФ a redundant one-line entry is cheaper than a silently missing one. This criterion governs the *decision* only; the *shape* of any fragment written is validated solely by ┬з18.6, and neither the skill nor the `/ship` arm re-validates shape (┬з18.5).

---

## 19. Closing

This document is the shell's SSOT. When gaps, contradictions, or improvements surface during implementation or operation, update this document before changing code. Update via a PR.
